Discussion Title: Pro-Life vs Pro-Choice: Should Abortion be Legal?

1. Women should have the right to choose abortion.
1.1. Con: Adoption is a viable alternative to abortion.
1.1.1. Con: Adoption is unlikely to be a feasible alternative unless the state intervenes to raise the demand for adopted children, for example by paying surrogate mothers.
1.1.1.1. Con: Maybe they should be. This is not an argument in favour of, or against abortion.
1.1.1.2. Con: In Brazil, for instance, [for every child available for adoption there are 6 families in the adoption queue](https://www.bbc.com/portuguese/brasil/2016/05/160509_adocao_criancas_ab). And 84% of the families are looking for children up to 5 years old. Interested families largely outnumber the children to be adopted.
1.1.2. Con: Telling a woman who wants to have an abortion, that they should consider adoption instead, is wrong. It pressures women to undergo the physically difficult and risky process of pregnancy and child birth against their will.
1.1.2.1. Con: Women should be properly informed about all options available to them with regards to their pregnancy. Informing women about adoption potential is not forcing a women to carry the child against her will. True and complete information is necessary to make the right choice for everyone.
1.1.2.2. Pro: Adoption is not a suitable option for all women. Many may not want to mother a child and then give it up.
1.1.2.2.1. Con: A woman who is uncomfortable giving her child up for adoption is probably likely to feel uncomfortable having an abortion.
1.1.2.2.1.1. Con: Woman may feel emotionally attached to their child if they are forced to carry it to term. It is coercive to force a woman to choose between her mental and economic well being.
1.1.2.2.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.2.1.1.
1.1.2.3. Pro: Pregnancy and childbirth are gruelling and have huge and varying impacts on women's physical and mental wellbeing. Therefore it is wrong to prevent women from seeking abortions.
1.1.2.3.1. Con: The existence of a possible remedy does not place an automatic moral mandate on society to allow that specific remedy.
1.1.2.3.1.1. Pro: In many countries, it is illegal to purchase certain street drugs even if they are taken to relieve physical or emotional pain.
1.1.2.3.1.2. Pro: Many countries regulate the usage of medicinal drugs, such as requiring a physician's prescription or not allowing new drugs to be sold without approval, even if it means that some citizens cannot then access helpful drugs.
1.1.2.3.1.3. Pro: A worker in a hard and grueling job is not allowed to kill his boss, though he may seek other remedies that are legally allowed.
1.1.2.3.1.4. Pro: Suicide is illegal, yet it has the same justification of alleviating pain. Abortion likewise is very much a permanent solution to temporary problems and/or obstacles. Obstacles not unlike what we all face everyday in life.
1.1.2.3.1.5. Con: By default, everything is allowed. Disallowing something should only be done with good reason. The burden of proof is on the person providing such reasons.
1.1.2.3.2. Con: Female human bodies are specifically designed to bear children.
1.1.2.3.2.1. Con: While female bodies may be designed to bear children, this does not undermine the significant burden this can be for women given the many symptoms they can experience as a result of pregnancy, such as nausea and exhaustion.
1.1.2.3.2.2. Pro: While the changes and potential harms that come with pregnancy and childbirth are natural and unintentional, all abortions include a volitional aspect. People mitigate the suffering of childbirth medically; nobody goes into an abortion hoping the child comes out alive.
1.1.2.3.2.3. Con: Even if the female body is "designed for" childbirth \(although you could make the argument that they're also "designed for" a lot of other things that we don't consider obligatory\), not all females are equipped for child rearing, which is generally the reason for wanting an abortion to begin with.
1.1.2.3.2.3.1. Pro: Not all women are equipped to bring a baby into the world. The UN Population Fund estimated that 289,000 women died during pregnancy in 2013. Conditions such as [HIV/AIDS](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4302331/), and cardiovascular disease can complicate pregnancy and increase the risk of maternal death.
1.1.2.3.2.3.1.1. Con: In these instances it is possible to make exceptions to the law without outright making abortion a legal choice.
1.1.2.3.2.3.1.1.1. Con: It would be cruel to require a victim of rape to justify their right to abortion.
1.1.2.3.2.3.1.1.2. Con: Legal processes are too long so the abortion may not be safe anymore or may not happen at all.
1.1.2.3.2.3.1.1.3. Con: Enforcing laws and drawing lines between what is legal and illegal is often a long process, prone to mistakes. Abortion is a time-delicate matter which cannot be postponed for next hearing.
1.1.2.3.2.4. Con: Women can decide for themselves what their body is made for.
1.1.2.3.2.4.1. Con: Women can decide what their body is used for, however there is no doubt that one of the functions they are made for is childbearing.
1.1.2.3.2.5. Con: Although the claim offers encouraging words to pregnant women, if women's bodies were specifically designed for childbirth, it would be painless to give birth and there would be no medical complications.
1.1.2.3.2.6. Con: A woman cannot be forced to be a mother, even if she is biologically "designed" to bear children, it does not mean she must have them. A pregnancy has effects on the woman's body that she shouldn't have to go through unwillingly.
1.1.2.3.2.7. Con: Female bodies are not designed.
1.1.2.3.3. Pro: The hormonal and psychological shifts that occur during pregnancy put some women at an increased risk for [mental illnesses](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/2014/12/18/pregnancy-affects-mental-health_n_6343186.html), such as anxiety and depression.
1.1.2.3.3.1. Pro: [Many women](http://postpartumprogress.org/the-facts-about-postpartum-depression/) suffer from postpartum depression.
1.1.2.3.3.1.1. Con: Many women who have abortions suffer a lifetime of [depression and guilt](http://bjp.rcpsych.org/content/199/3/180) as a result of terminating their pregnancies.
1.1.2.3.3.1.1.1. Con: 95% of women who have had abortions do not regret their decision to terminate their [pregnancies](http://time.com/3956781/women-abortion-regret-reproductive-health/).
1.1.2.3.3.1.1.1.1. Con: This 95% statistic is based on one study and biased reporting. Here is an [article](http://www.iowartl.org/get-the-facts/abortion/post-abortion-syndrome/) that shows 40 to 60% have negative reactions and 31% regret it.
1.1.2.3.3.1.1.2. Con: US [researchers](https://www.nytimes.com/2016/12/14/health/abortion-mental-health.html) followed nearly 1,000 women who sought abortions nationwide for five years and found that those who had abortions did not experience more depression, anxiety, low self-esteem or dissatisfaction with life than those who were denied it.
1.1.2.3.3.1.2. Pro: This is [especially true in women](http://www.postpartumprogress.com/postpartum-depression-risk-factors-2) who miscarry or in cases where the child is stillborn or has such a severe illness that it does not live for very long.
1.1.2.3.3.1.2.1. Pro: Depression after a [miscarriage](https://www.healthline.com/health/depression/miscarriage-depression#2) is usually most severe immediately after a pregnancy is lost. In one study, researchers discovered that after a year, women who had a miscarriage experienced rates of depression similar to those of women who didn’t have a miscarriage.
1.1.2.3.3.1.2.2. Con: If a stillborn child or child that doesn't live for very long causes an increased risk of depression, then a child terminated in the womb would cause an even greater increase of risk of depression. A [study](http://bjp.rcpsych.org/content/199/3/180) in the British Journal of Psychiatry found that women had a 37% higher risk of depression due to abortion compared to term birth. Stillbirth only has an [11%](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC31099/) higher depression risk compared to term birth and it declines over time.
1.1.2.3.3.1.2.2.1. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.3.1.1.2.
1.1.2.3.3.1.2.3. Con: A miscarriage or stillborn baby is 100% dead \(or non-living, depending on your view\). If a mother fears for this outcome of their fetus, an abortion should also be feared because it confirms the death of the fetus. However, if the mother chooses not to have an abortion, the chances of the fetus surviving birth is non-zero.
1.1.2.3.3.1.3. Con: Society doesn't give depressed mothers the right to kill their infants or toddlers, so depression in and of itself is not an ethically justifiable reason to terminate life.
1.1.2.3.3.1.3.1. Con: [Postpartum depression](https://www.nhs.uk/conditions/post-natal-depression/) affects 1 in 10 women, and is especially common in circumstances where the mother has a history of mental health problems. As depression is a serious and potentially life-threatening mental illness, these concerns can be a fair and legitimate factor when deciding whether to terminate an unwanted pregnancy.
1.1.2.3.3.1.3.1.1. Con: While postpartum depression is common, the risk of self-harm comes from [postpartum psychosis](https://familydoctor.org/condition/postpartum-depression/) which is more rare. The postpartum suicide rate is less than 2 out of every 100,000 births. This is [around the same risk](http://www.postpartumprogress.com/pregnancy-and-suicide) as the mother dying from hemorrhage/placenta previa or eclampsia/pre-eclampsia.
1.1.2.3.3.1.3.1.2. Con: [Screening questionnaires](http://www.postpartum.net/learn-more/screening/), [doctor follow-ups](https://familydoctor.org/condition/postpartum-depression/), and [local resources](http://www.postpartum.net/get-help/locations/) greatly mitigate the risks of a women with postpartum psychosis committing suicide.
1.1.2.3.3.1.3.1.3. Con: As society does not consider it morally permissible to allow mothers with known depression to kill their infant children, it would be even less morally permissible for a mother to kill an unborn child on the sole basis of potential future depression.
1.1.2.3.3.1.4. Con: Depression is only a possible post-birth complication, not a guaranteed outcome.
1.1.2.3.3.2. Con: Abortion puts the fetus at an increased risk for death \(that is the whole goal of an abortion\) and death is more severe than anxiety or depression.
1.1.2.3.3.3. Con: Raising a baby may increase those risks too but we don't think it is a valid argument to abandon or kill offspring. Moreover, the right to life is more important than a mental ilness because a mental illness of this kind is most surely reversible; death, unfortunately, is not.
1.1.2.3.4. Pro: Women's bodies change significantly as a result of pregnancy. Many women feel less attractive because of the stretch marks and weight gain.
1.1.2.3.4.1. Con: While pregnancy can take a toll on the body, the woman can work to minimize this and recover to some degree. The changes themselves are mostly cosmetic. Conversely, the terminated human life can never recover, and the changes to his/her body are literally life-altering.
1.1.2.3.4.2. Con: Stretch marks and other temporary blemishes are not sufficient justification for terminating a pregnancy because they can be remedied with other less severe methods than abortion.
1.1.2.3.4.3. Con: That is a cultural argument. In some countries those same 'defects' are seen as badges of honor, strength and beauty. Along those same lines, we should be able to dispose of anyone who makes us feel less than attractive.
1.1.2.3.5. Pro: [Pregnancy symptoms](https://www.cdc.gov/reproductivehealth/maternalinfanthealth/pregcomplications.htm) can be severe and can involve life-threatening illnesses.
1.1.2.3.5.1. Pro: In instances where the pregnant woman's life is at risk, she should be able to choose to have an abortion to save her own life.
1.1.2.3.5.1.1. Con: When the mother's life becomes medically threatened there is always the option to end the pregnancy with birth. Even without abortion factoring in, many babies survive premature birth. A life threatening situation of a pregnant mother could end in 2 deaths, 1 death and 1 living patient, or 2 living patients. Situations that require choosing death for a baby to save the mother are very rare.
1.1.2.3.5.1.1.1. Con: "There is always the option to end the pregnancy with birth" is a completely false statement. Medical practice does not generally allow inducing labor at any point for any reason. In some cases, inducing birth is actually the dangerous part. In some cases, the baby is far too premature for inducing birth to be any different than aborting it.
1.1.2.3.5.1.2. Con: While a life-threatening condition is a valid reason to seek an abortion, this is a specific case that does not legitimize a generalized right for women to choose abortion.
1.1.2.3.5.1.3. Pro: Even the Catholic church recognizes that if the life of an unborn baby is lost in the course of treatment which could save the life of the mother, this is not murder. It is not an intentional, unnecessary killing of the baby, it is an unfortunate and unintended side effect of saving the life of the mother.
1.1.2.3.5.1.4. Con: Having an abortion for medical reasons makes up [less than 1%](http://www.johnstonsarchive.net/policy/abortion/abreasons.html) of all abortions, even lower when the "life of the mother" is in jeopardy. The utilitarian justification for abortion is therefore very, very small.
1.1.2.3.5.1.4.1. Pro: It is reasonable to give priority to the mother over the child in extreme cases. However, this does not make voluntary abortions acceptable.
1.1.2.3.5.1.4.2. Con: The amount something happens doesn't always make it less important - it only takes one. If you, or someone else, were in that 1%, you would likely disagree.
1.1.2.3.5.1.4.3. Con: "Less than 1% of all abortions" could be misleading because if between 1970 and 2014, there were "44.5[million legal induced abortions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abortion_statistics_in_the_United_States)", then there could be 445k abortions that fall in this category. That would be a significant impact to a lot of people.
1.1.2.3.5.1.4.4. Pro: Statistics regarding the number of abortions due to endangerment of mother's life back this up.[Florida](https://ahca.myflorida.com/MCHQ/Central_Services/Training_Support/docs/ReasonGestation_2015.pdf), 2015: 0.065%. [UK](https://davidalton.net/2012/07/21/latest-abortion-figures-6-3-million-abortions-143-where-a-womans-life-was-in-danger/),1968-2011: 0.006%. [U.S.](http://www.johnstonsarchive.net/policy/abortion/abreasons.html#8) estimate: 1%.
1.1.2.3.5.2. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.2.3.1.1.
1.1.2.3.5.3. Pro: The symptoms, when inflicted upon a woman without her choice, are akin to torture.
1.1.2.3.6. Pro: Abortion has [less physical impact](http://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S1049386715001589?via%3Dihub) on the woman than pregnancy does.
1.1.2.3.6.1. Pro: The most common side effects of [abortion](http://americanpregnancy.org/unplanned-pregnancy/abortion-side-effects/) are abdominal pain and cramping, nausea, vomiting, diarrhoea, spotting and bleeding. They usually go away after a couple of weeks \(if they occur at all\). The common side effects of pregnancy tend to be more severe and usually last for months.
1.1.2.3.6.2. Pro: Generally speaking, abortions do not have a long-term impact on the body, and do not affect future [fertility](https://www.nhs.uk/conditions/abortion/risks/).
1.1.2.3.6.3. Con: In rare cases, abortions can cause dangerous and potentially life-threatening [complications](https://www.nhs.uk/conditions/abortion/risks/), such as infection of the womb, some of the pregnancy remaining in the womb, continuation of the pregnancy, excessive bleeding, damage to the cervix, or damage to the womb.
1.1.2.3.6.4. Pro: People who get abortions are less likely to have complications than people who have their [wisdom teeth](http://time.com/3623572/abortion-safe-complications/) removed.
1.1.2.3.6.5. Con: The overall mental hardships of pregnancy on a woman are not as [severe](https://www.cambridge.org/core/journals/the-british-journal-of-psychiatry/article/abortion-and-mental-health-quantitative-synthesis-and-analysis-of-research-published-19952009/E8D556AAE1C1D2F0F8B060B28BEE6C3D) as that of going through an abortion, so mental hardship cannot be a reason to prefer abortion over pregnancy.
1.1.2.3.6.5.1. Con: The mental hardships of pregnancy and the mental hardships of abortion are different for different people. Thus, women should be able to choose, based on their own needs
1.1.2.3.6.5.2. Pro: A 2003 [study](https://insights.ovid.com/crossref?an=00006254-200301000-00023) found an increased risk of preterm delivery and mood disorders, such as depression, in women with previous abortions as compared to women who had not had previous abortions.
1.1.2.3.6.5.3. Pro: A 2007 [study](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1111/j.1360-0443.2007.02040.x) found that women who aborted had an increased risk of later substance abuse or dependance than women who gave birth.
1.1.2.3.6.5.4. Pro: A [study](http://A study published in the British Journal of Psychiatry found that women who aborted had an 81% increased risk of mental disorders due to abortion, with 10% of that risk able to be directly related to the effects of abortion as compared to women who went to term and the other 71% correlative.) published in the British Journal of Psychiatry found that women who aborted had an 81% increased risk of mental disorders due to abortion, with 10% of that risk able to be directly related to the effects of abortion as compared to women who went to term and the other 71% correlative.
1.1.2.3.6.5.4.1. Con: There are fundamental issues with the validity of this study. For example, the researcher does not distinguish between mental health outcomes that occurred before abortions and those that occurred afterward, but still claimed to show a causal link between abortion and mental disorders. Additionally, several researchers and the editor of the Journal found that there were [serious issues](https://www.guttmacher.org/news-release/2012/study-purporting-show-link-between-abortion-and-mental-health-outcomes-decisively) with methodology and analysis.
1.1.2.3.6.5.4.2. Con: Negative emotional and psychological experiences after abortion are often linked to the individual's [own views](http://americanpregnancy.org/unplanned-pregnancy/abortion-emotional-effects/) about whether a fetus is a life from the point of conception. This suggests that people will have very different reactions to abortion depending on their beliefs, and reaffirms the view that it is therefore best for women determine the right choice for them.
1.1.2.3.6.5.4.3. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.3.1.1.2.
1.1.2.3.6.5.5. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.3.1.1.2.
1.1.2.3.7. Con: This argues for using lethal force \(abortion\) to prevent an impact to physical or mental wellbeing, i.e. self-defense. However, self-defense justifications for the use of lethal force requires certain or immediate threat to the person's life or major bodily harm. Very few pregnancies in developed countries threaten a woman's life or threaten major bodily harm. Therefore, the effects of the vast majority of pregnancy are insufficient to justify taking an innocent human life.
1.1.2.3.7.1. Con: This point rests completely upon the assumption that life begins at conception, which is in-and-of-itself a debatable concept.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1. Con: Biology textbooks are consistent that the lifecycle of a genetically distinct human organism begins at conception.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.1. Con: The majority of biology textbooks used to use creationism to describe the world's history and omitted evolution. The fact that biology textbooks are consistent in how they describe conception is not a reason we should believe in that description.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.1.1. Con: Does this argument imply that we get to choose which facts from biology textbooks we accept and which we do not accept arbitrary? Or that we should discard biology textbooks from education altogeter? 
Education textbooks indeed had some flaws, but those were discarded only after they were proven wrong. So in order to claim that some fact from biology \(or any other scientific\) textbook is wrong, it is first required that scientific community proves it wrong. That is not the case with conception.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.2. Pro: A living human organism [develops through stages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_development_\(biology\)), but is not biologically less or more a human organism at any stage. Some of the various stages are zygote, blastula, embryo, fetus, neonate, infant, adolescent, and adult.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.3. Pro: "The human life cycle begins at fertilization, when an egg cell inside a woman and a sperm cell from a man fuse to form a one-celled zygote" [www.biologyreference.com](http://www.biologyreference.com/La-Ma/Life-Cycle-Human.html)
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.4. Pro: Some quotes from Embryology textbooks have even made their way into the U.S. congressional record on this matter. [books.google.com](https://books.google.com/books?id=W6gziQydtBwC&lpg=PA197&ots=T-W4FAJT-h&dq=Although%20life%20is%20a%20continuous%20process%2C%20fertilization%20is%20a%20critical%20landmark%20because%2C%20under%20ordinary%20circumstances%2C%20a%20new%2C%20genetically%20distinct%20human%20organism%20is%20thereby%20formed.&pg=PA197#v=onepage&q=Although%20life%20is%20a%20continuous%20process%2C%20fertilization%20is%20a%20critical%20landmark%20because%2C%20under%20ordinary%20circumstances%2C%20a%20new%2C%20genetically%20distinct%20human%20organism%20is%20thereby%20formed.&f=false)
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.5. Pro: The fetus has a separate blood type and it is its own separate being from the mother. It shouldn't be the mothers choice to kill it if it is a separate being.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.5.1. Con: The fetus can not be considered a distinct, separate being from the mother - since it is unable to survive without the mother's body supporting it.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.5.1.1. Con: A fetus can be considered a separate being from the mother. As a parasite is, though it is reliant on a host for nutrients.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.5.1.2. Con: Premature babies live all the time. We are [getting better](https://www.wnyc.org/radio/#/ondemand/586996) at keeping them alive outside the womb.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.5.1.2.1. Con: The premature baby used as an example was born roughly 24 weeks into the pregnancy which is also the latest time for a surgical abortion to be performed. States already stop abortions after 24 weeks as from then on it's considered an “intent to murder.”
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.5.1.3. Con: A newborn infant cannot survive on its own without the mother either, that does not mean it is not a distinct and separate being. It is both distinct and separate.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.5.1.3.1. Con: A newborn infant can easily survive without the mother. All it takes is someone else to take care. The fetus can not.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.5.1.4. Con: Distinctiveness does not depend on an organism's ability to survive. The child is distinct because it is possible for its life to end while the mother's continues and vice versa.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.5.2. Con: Killing distinct living things is not murder. Eating salad kills distinct living things. Unlawfully killing a person is murder. The issue is whether a fetus is a person, and whether there is any lawful basis for killing the fetus.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.6. Con: Tadpoles are the beginning of the frog lifecycle. They are still not frogs any more than caterpillars are butterflies or blastocysts are human.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.6.1. Con: Actually [frogspawn](http://www.kidzone.ws/lw/frogs/facts3.htm) is the beginning of the frog lifecycle. And by this kind of thinking, you could argue that a child shouldn't be considered human because it hasn't grown into an adult yet.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.6.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.7.1.1.2.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.6.2. Con: They would still have the same DNA as a frog, which makes them a frog.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.6.3. Con: The science of embryology directly falsifies this claim.  Natural, developmental changes in the outward appearance of a living organism - even dramatic changes like with the butterfly - do not produce a different kind of organism.  [According to modern embryology](http://naapc.org/why-life-begins-at-conception/), a zygote is a distinct, living, and whole human being.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7. Con: Being a biological human being is legally and morally distinct from being a person with the rights and responsibilities ascribed to legal [personhood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personhood).
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.1. Con: This is a matter of public vote, not moral or scientific fact. So it’s somewhat cyclical to offer this as a pro-choice argument. The point at which we deem something alive is probably the most important point in the discussion of whether that thing should receive rights.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.1.1. Con: The biological definition of "life" serves a scientific purpose, and does not bestow any philosophical value on an object unless people decide that it does. Even if the deciding factor is deeming the fetus "alive", it will be a separate debate from what biologists consider useful to label as "alive".
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.1.2. Con: The public should not arbitrarily decide via a vote what is, and is not a life. They are often not qualified to do so. Scientists are qualified to do so, their expertise should not be dismissed in order to appease uninformed citizens.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2. Pro: A fetus does not have a 'right to life' as it does not qualify for the status of '[personhood](http://www.spiked-online.com/newsite/article/a-moral-case-for-abortion/18826#.Whn73Upl86w).'
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.1. Pro: Fetuses are yet to become citizens of the state since they are unborn and therefore have no rights or protection under common law.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.1.1. Con: The debate is about matters of right and wrong, not what is or is not permitted under some particular legal tradition \(e.g. the common law\).
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.1.2. Con: Citizenship is irrelevant to the legality \(and the morality\) of the act. Non-citizens enjoy the protection of the law just as much as citizens do. It is not legal to kill a non-citizen any more than it is to kill a citizen.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.2. Con: In 1857, the U.S. Supreme Court declared in [Dred Scott v. Sandford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dred_Scott_v._Sandford) that blacks were 'not persons' and therefore didn't have the rights of people. One group declaring that they don't consider another group of humans to be people is not a valid ethical excuse for stripping a group of humans of their natural rights.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.2.1. Con: Dred Scott v. Sandford had nothing to do with black slaves not being "persons", it ruled that black slaves were not American citizens, or the citizens or subjects of any other nation and therefore the Supreme Court did not have jurisdiction. Dredd Scott is not a good argument against abortion.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.2.1.1. Con: Dred Scott claimed a lot more than blacks merely being 'non-citizens'. It declared all African Americans as being outside the class of persons to which the human rights in the constitution applied to. [This and other arguments](https://supreme.justia.com/cases/federal/us/60/393/case.html) that blacks had no fundamental rights fed into the court's conclusion that blacks were non-citizens.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.3. Con: There is no generally accepted definition of "personhood", but this argument hinges on one particular definition.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.4. Con: Under Kantian ethics, on which the common basis for the pro-abortion personhood argument is based, it isn't just the unborn who are not people - it is anyone who cannot defend their personhood at the moment: infants, the unconscious, the asleep, the mentally infirmed, etc. Lack of personhood under this ethical system is not a valid reason to deprive a perceived non-person of life.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.4.1. Con: The pro-abortion personhood argument is not dependent upon the Kantian definition of personhood even if that is its philosophical origin. It is the capacity of [sentience](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sentience) which defines personhood, not its ability to defend its personhood in the moment.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.4.1.1. Con: The birth canal doesn't magically  give a baby sentience. It must be developed in the [womb](https://mobile.nytimes.com/2005/06/19/books/chapters/the-ethical-brain.html?referer=http://www.google.com/).
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.5. Con: This is an "is/ought" fallacy. It is clear that a fetus "is" not granted basic human rights \(life, liberty, property\), but that does not mean that a fetus "ought" not be granted basic human rights.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.6. Pro: Rights apply to persons. The essence of a person is emotion and motives/preferences/desires. Until a fetus reaches a stage in which those qualities arise; it is not a person and therefore does not have rights.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.6.1. Con: A person in a coma has rights. Unless the line is drawn at conception, the argument to allow abortion can also be applied to other living people.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.7. Con: Whether or not a human fits the criteria of sentient "personhood" is immaterial with regard to it's rights. A human in comatose may temporarily lose the characteristics that constitute personhood. Pulling the plug on their life support and killing them is still considered immoral if they're is a chance that they may regain sentience. Hence a foetus with a potential for sentience should not be stripped of the rights of a person when these characteristics are absent in the early gestational stage.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.8. Pro: Unborn and very young children are not yet "persons" in the philosophical sense, and do not have the ability to express preferences that makes us persons, so are morally owed the same rights as an animal, and the preferences of the mother should be given precedence.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.8.1. Con: Many people consider very young children to be "persons". In the U.S., very young children have legal rights. Killing very young children is typically [a capital offense](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/18/1111) while killing animals is not.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.9. Con: If we all share equal human rights, they must be based on something that we share equally, not something that some have more than others.  If you try to base rights on an ability \(e.g. self-awareness\) then you will include animals, exclude newborns, or both. The only thing that works to define human rights is our humanity. Each of us began our lives at fertilization. Whether a child is killed at 8 weeks or 8 months or 8 years, a unique, never-to-be-duplicated individual person is dead.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.10. Con: Personhood is an unproven philosophical concept. People determine the personhood of others based ultimately on subjective reasoning. Therefore, no real judgment can be made about the 'personhood' \(whether personhood even exists or not\) of the fetus.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.11. Con: They way we conceive of personhood as a rights bearing attribute, has to do with how humans have higher level thought and complex emotions which distinguish us from other life. Nevertheless, babies are also incapable of higher level thought and complex emotions, yet societies generally consider infanticide to be wrong because children grow up.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.11.1. Con: A fertility clinic is burning down. You grab a fire extinguisher and battle your way into the only open room. You see a large storage container with 1,000 fertilized eggs. Next to the container is a small child passed out from smoke inhalation. Most people's priority would be saving the 1 child over the 1,000 fertilized eggs. This shows that not all life is considered equal.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.11.1.1. Con: The issue with the fertility clinic analogy is that it's an emotional argument more than a rational one. Let's modify it this way: Your house is burning down and you have time only to take the fire extinguisher, enter a single room and save the people there, the rest can't be saved. There are two adults in one room, and in another there's your child \(you don't know who the adults are\). Most people would rather save their own child. None of those two intuitions solve the moral problem.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.11.1.2. Con: This is nothing like what happens in real life. It isn't normally a choice between 1,000 fertilized eggs and a small child. What actually happens is doctors kill one fetus at a time resulting in thousands being aborted without saving anyone's life. Even if the child's life is more valuable, it doesn't mean a fertilized egg or a fetus has no value and doesn't justify [abortion](https://www.dailywire.com/news/22360/pro-abortion-fanatic-presented-thought-experiment-ben-shapiro).
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.11.2. Con: Society can take responsibility for an abandoned infant, but it cannot take responsibility for a fetus. It's opinion has more relevance to the issue of infanticide than to abortion.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.11.3. Con: Infanticide provokes strong moral outrage for evolutionary reasons, not because children grow up. Killing children provokes greater outrage than killing adults because we are programmed to aggressively defend our children.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12. Pro: A [fetus](http://www.spiked-online.com/newsite/article/a-moral-case-for-abortion/18826) is not self aware, or conscious, or able to feel pain.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.1. Con: Neither are people who are asleep. Both being a fetus and being asleep are only true temporarily.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.1.1. Con: People who are asleep can feel pain, making them distinct from fetuses.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.2. Con: Recent [studies](http://www.pnas.org/content/110/37/15145) have shown that language acquisition begins in the 3rd trimester. This would indicate that the late term fetus is both aware and able to form memories prior to birth.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.3. Con: A fetus develops during the gestational period such that it does gain self-awareness, consciousness and the ability to feel pain. Therefore it can still be argued it should qualify for personhood status while still in utero.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.3.1. Con: While it is true that a fetus develops sentience in utero, it does not have sentience from the moment of conception. Therefore, a fetus should not be considered a person prior to the development of sentience which roughly coincides with the beginning of the 2nd trimester.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.3.2. Pro: A fetus develops the capacity for self-awareness, and consciousness around the beginning of the 2nd trimester of pregnancy. Therefore, the beginning of the 2nd trimester is when a fetus with a normally developing brain should be regarded as having the unalienable right to life.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.3.3. Pro: The fetal stage of human development is about 8-40 weeks from conception - two months until birth. The fetus has pain receptors present at 8 weeks, and observation shows the fetus 'responds' to painful stimuli in the same way adults do by 20 weeks. Cortical function is present by 30 weeks. While the exact beginning of pain sensation in a fetus is as-yet unknown, a human [can experience pain](https://www.medscape.com/viewarticle/845410) long before the fetal period is over.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.3.4. Con: Many non-human animals have cognitive capacities well beyond those of a fetus. These capacities are not typically taken to be sufficient for a right to life, in the case of animals, it is unclear why they ought to be sufficient in the case of fetuses.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.3.4.1. Pro: If we follow this line of argument, all pro-life supporters should abstain from eating meat, yet this is not the case.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.3.4.2. Con: It's very clear why cognitive capacities are sufficient for a fetus and not sufficient for an animal. A fetus is a human and an animal is not. Human rights are not the same as animal rights. Animals do have some rights. For example, you can't torture your dog. However, a "right to life" is not among animal rights. You can euthanize your dog.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.4. Con: A fetus has potentiality of these attributes, it will develop them naturally. Future people have rights.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.5. Con: The referenced material is very far from being the unanimous definition of personhood.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.5.1. Pro: Personhood is a variable concept depending on one's personal philosophy, and so should not be used as a benchmark for assigning value to human life.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.6. Con: Consciousness shouldn't be a declaration of whether someone has rights or not, people in a coma or people in an alive but unconscious state aren't disqualified as human or having less rights simply because they are not aware.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.6.1. Con: It is always considered wrong to end the life of a healthy human being. It is not always considered wrong to end the life of someone who is in a coma.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.6.1.1. Con: Some people do in fact always consider it wrong to end the life of someone who is in a coma.  As long as the patient isn't brain dead \(i.e. "dead"\) then it's wrong to pull the plug.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.6.2. Con: There is a distinction between violating someone’s rights, and never instilling them in the first place. Constitutional rights are assigned at citizenship, which takes place around birth. Moral rights are subjective, as moral values may differ from person to person. Freedom from having one’s life ended by another is not an absolute right outside of these two, because honoring an advanced directive by pulling the plug of a terminal patient remains an accepted option.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.6.2.1. Con: It is illegal to kill a citizen and illegal to kill a tourist.  Just because the victim doesn't have citizenship, doesn't mean the victim doesn't have rights. Our rights are not "instilled" by the Constitution. Our rights are acknowledged by the Constitution. Human rights are inalienable. They cannot be repealed or restrained by human laws.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.6.2.2. Con: "Honoring an advanced directive" implies voluntary euthanasia which would be consistent with self-determination, self-ownership and human rights. It is not an example of involuntarily having one's life ended by another so it is not comparable to abortion.
1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.7. Con: We do not have a rational, unambiguous definition or even description of "Self awareness" or "Consciousness". The more we learn about other animals the less unique humans appear. Any such definition must include intelligent, non-human animals or exclude young human children.
1.1.2.3.7.2. Pro: You can't terminate a life because the the individual needs care and provides an unwanted burden. Otherwise nursing homes and hospitals would be killing all patients.
1.1.2.3.7.3. Con: Abortion of a non-person is not comparable with self-defence against a person.
1.1.2.3.8. Con: Nursing an infant is gruelling and takes a huge toll on the body, yet society doesn't treat that as an ethical excuse for the mother to kill the infant.
1.1.2.3.8.1. Con: The situations are not comparable. A nursing mother can relinquish her parental rights without killing the infant by giving the child to another adult or to the state to raise with the help of infant formula or a wet nurse. It is not exclusively dependent on the mother to remain alive. Until scientists are able to develop an artificial womb, a pre-viable fetus is exclusively dependent on its mother and cannot be handed off to others.
1.1.2.3.8.1.1. Con: A pregnant mother can also relinquish her parental rights without killing the infant by transferring custody to another adult or to the state. Short of abandoning a child, it is generally [faster](https://adoptionnetwork.com/can-i-decide-to-place-my-baby-for-adoption-after-i-give-birth) and [easier](http://www.americanadoptions.com/pregnant/putting_an_older_child_up_for_adoption) for a pregnant woman to do so than it is for a mother of an infant or small child to transfer custody later on.
1.1.2.3.9. Con: The gruelling aspect of pregnancy and childbirth applies equally to planned and unplanned instances. The claim implies that the basis for wanting an abortion is that childbirth is a painful experience. There are less severe methods for alleviating the discomfort.
1.1.2.3.10. Con: The individual hardship does not outweigh the societal benefit of contributing to the physical and social growth of the human race.
1.1.2.3.10.1. Pro: Many children consider school to be mentally and emotionally gruelling, and physical education to be sometimes physically gruelling as well. Yet because the benefit to society is greater than the individual hardship, society still demands that all children be schooled either publically or at home.
1.1.2.3.10.2. Con: The human race does not require mandated births to grow physically or socially.
1.1.2.3.11. Pro: Child-birth is a dangerous and complicated medical procedure.
1.1.2.3.11.1. Pro: Even under ideal medical supervision each case can be potentially lethal to women. Unexpected bleeding, shock, side effects of medical drugs, infection, complications during c-section carry grave risks to the mother. No one can be forced to undergo a risky medical procedure. Some women know that they will have complications. They can't be forced to risk their lives.
1.1.2.3.11.2. Pro: Even in developed nations, with world class health care systems, there is still a [non-zero](https://www.varsity.co.uk/science/8644) chance that individuals may die whilst giving birth. Women who are under the age of 15, older mothers, and women from lower income groups are particularly at risk.
1.1.2.3.11.2.1. Con: This tiny, statistically insignificant minority of abortions does not justify the vast majority which are elective and entirely unrelated to medical concerns. Fringe cases do not justify the mainstream.
1.1.2.3.11.2.2. Con: The “non-zero” argument suggests that, since we cannot attain a perfect situation \(e.g. perfect birthing surgery\), we may as well accept the potential consequences of bad situations \(e.g. miscarriages\) and not act to reduce those consequences. This implies that we should give up anything where perfection is unlikely to be attained. For example, we may as well give up cars because the chances of having an accident is non-zero.
1.1.2.3.11.2.2.1. Con: Nobody is claiming that childbirth in general isn't worth it due to risk of death. The key point here is allowing the woman to have the choice to bear that risk, or not to.
1.1.2.3.11.2.3. Pro: As long as the risk of death during childbirth remains non-zero, it is unethical to force a person to continue their pregnancy.
1.1.2.3.11.2.4. Pro: In the U.S., [approximately two to three women die in childbirth every day](https://www.npr.org/2017/12/22/572298802/nearly-dying-in-childbirth-why-preventable-complications-are-growing-in-u-s).
1.1.2.3.11.3. Con: Most births aren't that complicated. Child birth has been ongoing since time immemorial.
1.1.2.3.11.3.1. Con: Abortions have also been [ongoing for centuries, if not millennia.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_abortion)
1.1.2.3.12. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.6.5.
1.1.2.3.13. Con: The unborn child is a human being, we cannot choose one person's convenience over another person's life. In a civilised society, the inherent right to not be murdered should always rank higher than an individual desire to be free from hardship or inconvenience.
1.1.2.3.14. Pro: A woman shouldn’t have to change her body or the course of her future based on one incidence of intercourse.
1.1.2.3.15. Con: Birth control or abstaining from consensual sexual contact will prevent pregnancy in the overwhelming amount of cases.
1.1.2.3.15.1. Con: Humans are designed to find pleasure in sexual relations. Sex is more than just for reproduction; it is also a bonding mechanism between life-long partners. Therefore an abstinence only method is an unreasonable burden for a person to bear.
1.1.2.3.15.1.1. Con: The primary role of sexual relations is reproduction. This is true in all species that reproduce by mating. The pleasure and bonding effect of a sexual relation is subservient to its purpose as a reproduction mechanism.
1.1.2.3.15.1.1.1. Con: If the primary role of sexual relations was reproduction, people would not have sex unless they wanted to reproduce. We know this is not the case.
1.1.2.3.15.1.1.2. Con: People have sex for [pleasure and bonding effects](https://www.jsm.jsexmed.org/article/S1743-6095\(18\)30132-2/abstract) more often than reproduction across all ages.
1.1.2.3.15.2. Con: Many women are not given proper sex education and are not aware of the risks of unprotected sex.
1.1.2.3.15.2.1. Con: The solution to this is that we should give them the proper education, not the right to abortion.
1.1.2.3.15.2.2. Con: About half the women who get abortions in the [U.S.](https://www.webmd.com/women/tc/abortion-reasons-women-choose-abortion) and [Britain](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2017/07/06/half-abortions-due-failed-contraception-new-report/) were actively using some form of contraception \(the pill, condom, etc.\) the month they got pregnant. That might support an argument that they weren't given proper sex ed on the fallibility of contraception methods, but not  an argument that they aren't aware of the importance of protected sex.
1.1.2.3.15.2.3. Pro: In some places, such as the United States, abstinence only education is common in schools and means that when people do decide to have sex, they do not know how to protect themselves.
1.1.2.3.15.2.3.1. Pro: Many people who oppose abortion on religious grounds also oppose contraception. This leads to a no win scenario where women can't enjoy sex without risk of pregnancy.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4. Con: It is possible for women to research contraception and the likelihood of pregnancy before they have sex, such that they are aware of the risks.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.1. Pro: The internet has made such information widely available, even in conservative communities.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.1.1. Con: This would assume that conservative communities are open to the use of contraception and the bodily autonomy of women which is statistically not the case; see Ireland's current referendum movement to remove the eighth amendment to their constitution as well as the concept of contraception in traditional Roman Catholic and similar monotheistic communities. Information may be available, that does not mean it aligns with religious persuasions and permissions.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.2. Con: In many developing countries traditional methods and [superstitions](http://nytlive.nytimes.com/womenintheworld/2015/09/26/why-222-million-women-cant-get-the-birth-control-they-need/) are held in higher regard \(and are more widespread\) than scientific information and [healthcare](https://opinionator.blogs.nytimes.com/2011/02/14/villages-without-doctors/).
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3. Con: No form of contraception is 100% effective.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.1. Pro: Even used perfectly, condoms are only effective [98%](https://www.plannedparenthood.org/learn/birth-control/condom/how-effective-are-condoms) of the time.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.2. Pro: Planned Parenthood states that the pill is only about [91%](https://www.plannedparenthood.org/learn/birth-control/condom/how-effective-are-condoms) effective because it is difficult to maintain perfect use.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.2.1. Con: If the pill is used perfectly it is 99% [effective](https://www.nhs.uk/Conditions/contraception-guide/Pages/how-effective-contraception.aspx).
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.3. Con: Using abortion as a form of contraceptive should not be legal because the inconvenience of becoming a parent does not justify the killing of an unborn child. Abortion should only be used in extreme cases where continuing with the pregnancy indangers the life of the mother. Abstinence is always an option for those who cannot accept the risk that comes with all contraceptives.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4. Con: Abstinence is always effective.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.1. Con: An abstinent woman can still be raped and become pregnant.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.1.1. Con: This is not an argument against the efficacy of abstinence. The efficacy rate of hormonal birth control is unaffected by the possibility that a significant other might replace a woman's birth control with a placebo. Similarly, the efficacy rate of condoms generally is not affected by the possibility that either partner might poke holes in the end. An uncontrollable circumstance like rape does not affect the efficacy of intentional abstinence.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.2. Pro: Abstinence is a form of contraception which, by definition cannot fail, as a failure to be abstinent is definitionally no longer abstinence. It is an infallible premise.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.3. Con: Abstinence is only 100% effective if used perfectly. The "typical use" effectiveness of abstinence as a contraceptive is not [100%.](https://www.guttmacher.org/gpr/2003/12/understanding-abstinence-implications-individuals-programs-and-policies)
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.4. Con: It is unreasonable to expect people to remain abstinent forever. There are people who may want to have sex lives but do not ever want to have children. For them there is no fail proof form of contraception.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.4.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.1.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.4.2. Con: This does not absolve them of responsibility for the potential consequences of their actions. If the risk of pregnancy with a given contraceptive method is deemed to be worth the benefit of a sex life, the actors bear full responsibility for that possibility and all of its implications. It is unreasonable to expect people to not desire to be wealthy, and yet society frowns upon robbery at all phases of life. We do not allow immoral or illegal actions to satisfy simple wants.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.4.2.1. Con: Expecting women who do not want to have children to take responsibility by being abstinent may result in other problems that could arise from a life devoid of that type of intimacy and connection.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.4.3. Con: Sterilization procedures \(hysterectomy, vasectomies\) are 100% effective.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.4.3.1. Con: Although it is rare, vasectomy failure is still a [possibility](https://www.nichd.nih.gov/health/topics/vasectomy/conditioninfo/Pages/effective.aspx). In the first year after vasectomy,15 to 20 of every 10,000 couples experience a pregnancy.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.4.3.2. Con: In [many states](https://www.plannedparenthood.org/learn/birth-control/sterilization) a woman is required to have a set number of children or be above a certain age to even have their "tubes tied" and most doctors will not even consider hysterectomy as an option unless there is a substantial medical reason.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.4.3.3. Pro: A very small number of those who get vasectomies report any infection, bleeding or pain. The surgery is so simple that it is often done in a doctors office, only requires local anesthetic, and takes around 10 minutes for completion of the procedure.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.4.3.4. Pro: Vasectomies are both reversible and do not stop your body from producing sperm. It is one of the most highly-effective birth control measures while still maintaining the possibility of having children in the future.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.4.3.5. Con: On average, one woman in 200 will become pregnant after undergoing a female sterilisation [procedure](https://www.nhs.uk/Conditions/contraception-guide/Pages/female-sterilisation.aspx).
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.4.3.6. Con: There is a risk that female sterilisation will not work - blocked tubes can rejoin any time after the [operation](https://www.nhs.uk/Conditions/contraception-guide/Pages/female-sterilisation.aspx).
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.4.3.7. Con: Sterilisation is a near-[permanent](https://www.nhs.uk/Conditions/contraception-guide/Pages/female-sterilisation.aspx) procedure - it is not a suitable contraceptive option for people who want to have children in the future.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.5. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.4.3.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.4. Con: Low-income women often lack sexual education and even if they do have this information, they sometimes lack the resources to buy contraceptives.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.4.1. Pro: According to [WHO](http://www.who.int/bulletin/volumes/89/4/10-083329/en/), only 43% of women of reproductive age in less developed countries use modern contraceptive methods, and a wide gap in use is seen between the highest and lowest wealth quintiles \(52% versus 35%, respectively\).
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.5. Con: A lack of sex education in many conservative regions means that couples are often ill equipped to properly use contraceptives such as condoms.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.5.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.4.4.1.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.5.2. Con: This non-excuse is not valid in an era of history where the vast majority of people in developed nations have instant access to the whole of human knowledge at the touch of a finger through the internet.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.5.3. Con: The solution for ignorance is to improve sex education, not implement a policy of allowing abortion.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.5.3.1. Pro: If abortion is legal, sex-ed must become better in order to make a responsible choice.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.5.4. Con: This [data](https://www.kff.org/womens-health-policy/state-indicator/abortion-rate/?currentTimeframe=0&sortModel=%7B%22colId%22%3A%22Location%22%2C%22sort%22%3A%22asc%22%7D) on abortion rates shows that the highest abortion rates are predominantly in liberal states while the lowest rates are primarily in conservative states.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.5.4.1. Con: According to this table, the highest abortion rates are mostly seen in states with large urban areas, while the lowest are seen in mostly rural states, therefore the difference in abortion rates may be due to other factors such as lack of access. For example, as of 2014 there were [only two abortion providers in the entire state of South Dakota](https://www.guttmacher.org/fact-sheet/state-facts-about-abortion-south-dakota) \(the 17th largest state in the US at nearly 80,000 sq mi in size\), whereas a quick Google search turned up about 20 in and near New York City.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.5.4.1.1. Con: While lack of access may or may not be a factor in why conservative regions tend to have lower abortion rates, it still wouldn't support the initial unsupported claim that conservative regions have higher abortion rates due to lack of sexual education.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6. Con: Religious women are often taught that use of contraception is deeply immoral.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1. Con: Contraception is considered immoral by certain religions because it interferes with the conception of a child. Religions who are against contraception are therefore also against abortion because it interferes with the birth of a child.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1. Pro: Religious values and beliefs support the view that abortion is immoral.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.1. Con: Until 1827, abortions prior to ["quickening"](https://publishing.cdlib.org/ucpressebooks/view?docId=ft967nb5z5&chunk.id=d0e195&brand=ucpress) \(the stage where a mother could feel the fetus moving\) were commonplace and accepted by everyone including religious clerics.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.2. Con: Biblically, life is associated with breath, not conception or heartbeats. From Adam being created from dust and then getting the breath of life; Ezekiel's army of bones; to when Jesus "breathed his last and his soul departed", the Bible is pretty clear on this.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.2.1. Pro: Judeo-Christian texts actually seem to suggest that "life" begins the moment the "breath of life" enters a person. Even Adam wasn't considered "alive", despite his physical development, until the "breath of life" entered him - which coincided with his first breath: "and breathed into his nostrils the breath of life; and man became a living being," \(Genesis 2:7\).
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.2.2. Con: It is not necessary to equate the Biblical use of "Breath of Life" to the first breath of oxygen through the nostrils. Adam was formed outside the womb, thus he had no oxygen coursing through his veins from his mothers cardio-vascular system, as a baby in the womb does. In essence, the breath of life is present for the fetus at the stage of an independent heartbeat at the very latest, which feeds the oxygen from the mother through the unborn child.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.2.2.1. Con: A current and accurate scientific view of oxygen transfer to a fetus does not alter the historical view that life began with the first \(observable\) "breath". While it may or may not be accurate, it is the belief that was held at the time.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.2.2.2. Con: Adam is a myth and has no scientific foundation. The early Hebrews believed men planted seeds in women who were vessels to carry the man's baby. They can not be reliable sources for this discussion.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.3. Con: Our laws are based on secular values, not specific religious ones, as the latter can vary from one religion to another.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.3.1. Pro: The moral stance on abortion differs between religions, and therefore is not universally considered murder.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.3.1.1. Pro: Abortion is [not uncommon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_and_abortion) among Hindu and Sikh communities where there is a cultural preference for male babies over female.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.3.1.2. Pro: In [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_and_abortion#Islam) a fetus is thought to become a living soul only after 120 days of gestation and so abortion is generally seen as permissible until this time.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.4. Con: Non-theocratic governments can't make religious/philosophical decisions for it's citizens. The concept of Life is philosophical not scientific, so the point at which life begins is a religious opinion or philosophical construct. Therefore this decision can't be made by the government, and should be left up to women and their doctors.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.4.1. Con: Human life is not a subjective concept, it is a well documented [scientific concept](https://lozierinstitute.org/a-scientific-view-of-when-life-begins/).
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.4.1.1. Con: The question is not whether there is life in an embryo--there is, and it has human DNA. So does the egg before it is fertilized. The question is whether 8 cells is a human person.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.4.1.1.1. Con: The above claim is not questioning the personhood of the embryo but whether life is a philosophical or scientific concept.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.4.1.2. Con: The article quoted states, "this definition does not directly address the central ethical question surrounding the embryo: What value ought society place on human life at the earliest stages of development?"
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.4.1.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.7.1.1.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.5. Pro: Classical [Hindu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_and_abortion#Hinduism) texts strongly condemn abortion.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.6. Pro: Many [Orthodox Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_and_abortion#Judaism) feel that abortion is wrong, except in cases where it is necessary to save the woman's life.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.6.1. Con: Historically, abortion has been [accepted in Judaism.](https://jwa.org/encyclopedia/article/abortion) While many orthodox Jews oppose abortion, many do not oppose it.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.7. Pro: Abortion is generally forbidden in [Sikhism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_and_abortion#Sikhism) on the basis that it interferes with the work of God.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.8. Pro: The [Catholic Church](https://www.catholic.com/tract/abortion) has always strongly condemned abortion.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.8.1. Con: Catholics do not uniformly oppose abortion. For example, the [Catholics for choice group](http://www.catholicsforchoice.org/about-us/), believe that abortion rights and Catholicism are not incompatible.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.8.2. Con: The Catholic Church has always condemned birth control as well. Most people, including Catholics, do not agree with this stance. Therefore, the Catholic Church's moral stance on an issue is generally accepted to fallible.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.8.3. Pro: [Pope Francis](https://cruxnow.com/vatican/2016/11/20/pope-francis-calls-abortion-horrendous-crime-grave-sin/) described abortion as a 'very grave sin' and a 'horrendous crime'.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.8.3.1. Con: Pope Francis's statements made it clear that women who have had abortions, would still be considered members of the Catholic Church, and that, they could be forgiven by priests. This represents a [softening](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-38054640) of the Catholic Church's position towards abortion. Previously, any individual who performed or had an abortion could be immediately excommunicated from the Catholic Church.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.9. Con: No one can be forced to live according to others' religious beliefs. Any denial of access to abortion based on religion is nothing other than forcing someone's beliefs on to others.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.9.1. Pro: If abortions are denied to women on the basis of another’s religious beliefs on when life begins, then the woman loses her right to her own religious beliefs.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.9.2. Pro: In the United States, the First Amendment states that "Congress shall make no law respecting an establishment of religion, or prohibiting the free exercise thereof." Banning abortion on religious grounds is therefore unconstitutional and illegal in the United States.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.10. Con: Religion is a human construct, it's morality comes only from other humans who interpret it, not a divine command. The form belief takes in practice is an entirely human process. Therefore the mere context of religion does not add any weight to a claim.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.11. Con: In a theocracy this argument might fit in somewhere, but in a free democracy it has no place. Choice is a human process not a divine arbitration. If a god dictated our entire life then there would be no choices ever and our existence would be inconsequential to the universe.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.12. Con: Many religions allow for a practical application of abortion. Judaism allows for abortion in cases that put the mother at risk or when the means to support the child are unavailable to the parent. Islam, under all circumstances, says that a foetus is not imbued with a soul until the 12th week. Both permit abortion in the case of rape. If this is to be an argument then one religion must be shown to be correct and above all others.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.13. Pro: The [Bible](https://www.ucg.org/the-good-news/the-abortion-debate-what-does-god-say) shows that God felt all human lives should be protected, including those in the womb.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.13.1. Con: Christians have long discarded many outmoded Bible covenants. The Bible states, "But every woman that prayeth or prophesieth with her head uncovered dishonoureth her head..."\([1 Corinthians 11:5](http://biblehub.com/1_corinthians/11-5.htm)\).Enforcing this in many countries would would be resisted by many of the same who are pro-life.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.13.2. Con: This statement is false and likely comes from a misreading of Exodus 21:22-24,  which proscribes a fine payable to the husband for accidentally harming a fetus, but “eye for eye/ life for life” if the woman carrying a child is harmed/killed.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.13.3. Con: There are numerous examples of god-ordained infanticide, child murder, and the murder of pregnant women in the Old Testament. These include [Jeremiah 11:22-23](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Jeremiah+11%3A22-23&version=NIV), [Psalm 135:8](http://biblehub.com/psalms/135-8.htm) and [2 Kings 15:16](http://biblehub.com/2_kings/15-16.htm).
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.13.4. Con: There is no scientific or factual evidence whatsoever of the existence of a "God", and any beliefs that are credited to him are simply moral constructs devised by humans.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.13.5. Con: The Bible does not describe the death of the child inside a baby as murder or death, but as property lost.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.13.6. Pro: The Bible states that God believes if a man causes injury to a woman who is pregnant, and in turn kills the fetus, then he should give [life for life](https://www.ucg.org/the-good-news/the-abortion-debate-what-does-god-say). This indicates that God believes the fetus to be a living being and its killing to be wrong.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.13.6.1. Con: This is inaccurate. Exodus 21:22 says that if a woman is accidentally injured in a fight and miscarries, the one who injured her [has to pay a fee to the husband](https://biblehub.com/drb/exodus/21.htm). The husband decides on the fee. If the woman dies, the normal punishment for murder is applied \(eye for an eye etc\). Some translations use the term "mischief" to describe the woman dying. Other translations specify different punishments based on [how far along in development the fetus was.](https://biblehub.com/sep/exodus/21.htm)
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.13.7. Con: Religious views are non-factual and interpretive. While there should never be mandated abortions due to religious beliefs, there should never be a legal banning of abortions due to one group's interpretation of their religious doctrine.
1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.14. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.13.7.
1.1.2.3.15.2.5. Con: If an un-educated woman becomes pregnant out of ignorance, then why is it okay to kill her baby before birth while is not okay after birth? This argument is basically about if the unborn is a human being similar to the born baby or not.
1.1.2.3.15.2.6. Con: Every individual who knows the basic natural or scientific facts about having sex has responsibility for the the consequences already known by this hypothesis.
1.1.2.3.15.2.6.1. Con: Knowing that sex causes pregnancy is not nearly sufficient. It is knowing clearly how to prevent pregnancy and / or to use contraception effectively that will prevent significant numbers of unwanted pregnancies.
1.1.2.3.15.3. Con: Regardless of whether there are methods to avoid pregnancy, once a woman is pregnant she should be given an option to avoid the gruelling effects of pregnancy.
1.1.2.3.15.4. Con: "Birth control" and "abstinence" are preventative measures. Given the original thesis of whether women should have the right to abort, and the sub-thesis on hardships of pregnancies, this argument is irrelevant / misplaced. No one is thinking of "birth control" or "abstinence" after they've become pregnant. This argument would be better placed in a discussion of birth control or how to prevent underage/unwanted pregnancies.
1.1.2.3.15.5. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.
1.1.2.4. Con: No matter the risks associated, pregnancy is natural; it is meant to happen, whereas taking hormone pills or having a surgical procedure are irrefutably unnatural and carry greater risks.
1.1.3. Pro: Even if adoption isn't perfect, it is still better than abortion because the child survives.
1.1.3.1. Con: Because the system is so overburdened, children are often placed in [abusive foster homes](http://www.upworthy.com/the-horror-stories-these-former-foster-care-kids-have-sound-too-bad-to-be-true-but-theyre-not) or replaced in the care of their abusive parents.
1.1.3.1.1. Pro: The rate of sexual abuse in foster homes in the UK was found to be [four times higher](http://www.hg.org/article.asp?id=6703) than the national average, and twenty eight times higher in group homes.
1.1.3.1.2. Pro: Despite the fact that $22 billion are spent on [foster care programs](http://abcnews.go.com/Primetime/FosterCare/story?id=2017991&page=1) every year in the US, nearly 60,000 children are reported weekly as abused or neglected. This suggests that the state is incapable of effectively preventing child abuse within the foster care system.
1.1.3.1.3. Pro: [Research](http://www.liftingtheveil.org/foster04.htm) in the US determined that over 28% of foster children experienced abuse while in the foster care system, and many [former foster children](https://www.psychologytoday.com/blog/somatic-psychology/201201/the-foster-care-system-and-its-victims-part-2) believe that the number of incidents are much higher.
1.1.3.1.3.1. Con: Quality of life should not determine value of life. Many great minds who have made lasting contributions to society experienced abusive childhoods.
1.1.3.1.4. Con: The possibility of a bad childhood doesn't justify taking an innocent human's life.
1.1.3.1.5. Pro: The banning of abortion in Romania lead to an orphan crisis, where [150,000](http://articles.latimes.com/2000/may/14/news/mn-29897) unwanted infants were put in extremely poorly run state orphanages.
1.1.3.1.5.1. Pro: Even decades on, many of these orphans [suffer](https://www.pri.org/stories/2013-01-16/romanian-orphans-face-challenges-decades-after-adoption) from mental and physical health conditions as a result of the conditions they lived in.
1.1.3.2. Con: Youth in foster care and adults who formerly were placed in care have disproportionately high [rates](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3061347/) of emotional and behavioural disorders.
1.1.3.3. Pro: The child can go on to have a whole life through adoption, and beyond the nine months of pregnancy, does not have to be a burden for the parent who did not want or was not ready to have them.
1.1.3.3.1. Con: This ignores the health of, and the concerns of the mother.
1.1.3.3.1.1. Pro: Some women are not capable of carrying a child without grave risk to them.
1.1.3.4. Pro: There are many people who are unable to have children and would like the opportunity to adopt one. In the [US](http://thefederalist.com/2016/08/18/why-so-many-families-who-want-to-adopt-cant/) there are significantly more people who want to adopt than there are children to adopt.
1.1.4. Pro: Some women do not feel ready to raise a child, but for religious reasons, think that having an abortion is immoral. For them, adoption is a viable option.
1.1.4.1. Con: Legalizing abortion does not prevent women from giving up their children for adoption. Religious women can still choose to give their children up for adoption.
1.1.5. Pro: Adoption respects the child's right to life while allowing the birth mother to forgo many of the burdens of raising a child, and instead allows that child to be raised by parents who are better equipped to take on that burden.
1.1.5.1. Con: Many, not all. Pregnancy can cause a plethora of issues for a mother, especially a [young](http://americanpregnancy.org/unplanned-pregnancy/teen-pregnancy-issues-challenges/) mother. The hips widen, extra fat is added, hormones go into overdrive, and there are many pregnancy-specific conditions that are often life-threatening or fatal.
1.1.5.2. Con: The adoption system is also not very good in most countries. A large part of the decision for women between abortion and adoption is whether or not the baby can be raised in a stable and healthy environment.
1.1.6. Con: Adoption does not guarantee a safe life for children.
1.1.6.1. Pro: Private foster care agencies have [allowed](http://www.huffingtonpost.com/evey-rosenbloom/where-do-the-children-go_1_b_8728758.html) criminals and registered sex offenders to acquire licenses and adopt foster children. This has led to neglect, sexual abuse and murders of children.
1.1.6.1.1. Pro: A caseworker in one such agency reported that three girls were happy and healthy in their foster home when in fact they had been [dead for three months](http://articles.chicagotribune.com/1996-09-20/news/9609200157_1_state-caseworker-report-illinois-supreme-court). This is indicative of the sheer ineptitude of many foster care agencies.
1.1.6.1.2. Pro: Many LGBTQ children in foster homes suffer abuse. As a result, in the US, 56% spent some time homeless because they believed they were safer on the streets than they were in their foster homes \([p. 5](https://www.childwelfare.gov/pubPDFs/LGBTQyouth.pdf)\).
1.1.6.2. Pro: State institutions are bad at properly assessing whether or not the environment of foster homes are safe.
1.1.6.2.1. Pro: According to the [Child advocate review](http://www.njleg.state.nj.us/OPI/Reports_to_the_Legislature/child_advocate_review_december2008.pdf) \(p.15\), the quality of safety assessments only met standards in 46% of reviewed cases.
1.1.6.2.2. Pro: The screening process is only as good as the person who makes the assessment and the level of stress or workload they may be facing. In New York, the [40% turnover](http://www.gothamgazette.com/housing/1915-flaws-in-the-screening-process-for-foster-parents) in caseworkers is testament to the heavy workload they face, which could reflect in the quality of their work.
1.1.6.2.2.1. Pro: The average foster care social worker is paid [$47,372](https://infograph.venngage.com/p/243734/3-ways-to-improve-the-foster-care-system) annually. This is substantially less than other working professionals such as IT Managers \([$79,584](http://www.foxbusiness.com/features/2015/07/09/average-salaries-for-americans-median-salaries-for-common-jobs.html)\) or HR managers \([$73,474](https://www.glassdoor.com/Salaries/human-resources-manager-salary-SRCH_KO0,23.htm)\). These workers are then forced to make tough decisions and deal with difficult situations on a day to day basis.
1.1.6.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.3.1.
1.1.6.4. Pro: There are more orphans and children in foster care in the world than families who are [willing and able to adopt](https://adoption-beyond.org/adoption-statistics/).
1.1.6.4.1. Con: This is a good reason to publicise adoption as an alternative to potential parents.
1.1.6.4.2. Con: -> See 1.1.3.4.
1.1.6.4.3. Con: -> See 1.1.3.1.4.
1.1.6.5. Con: Most children would probably prefer adoption to abortion if given a choice, even if adoption and foster care are not perfect.
1.1.6.5.1. Con: It is not possible to infer the preferences of an entity that lacks that the mental architecture to carry a preference.
1.1.6.5.1.1. Con: It is reasonable to assume that a late-stage fetus \(e.g. 8 months\) is no less capable of having a preference than a newborn.
1.1.6.5.1.1.1. Con: Abortions do not occur at 8 months, except in cases of fatal foetal abnormality or the death of the foetus.
1.1.7. Con: To deny abortion forces a child to be born and live in a world where they are unwanted by their natural mother.
1.1.7.1. Con: That does not imply it will not be wanted by anyone. Adoptive parents are often more caring and loving than natural ones because they're actually looking forward to having children but they can't themselves.
1.1.8. Pro: It is very likely that many adoptees and former foster children appreciate the [fact that they are alive](http://www.teenbreaks.com/abortion/abortionsurvivors.cfm).
1.1.8.1. Con: The [suicide](https://adoption.com/adoption-related-suicide-statistics-prevention) rate of adoptees is four times greater than the suicide rate of non-adoptees.
1.1.8.1.1. Con: Even with those tragic statistics in mind, the fact remains that many of adoptees appreciate the fact that they are alive. 7.6% perecent of adoptees trying to commit a suicide, as stated in this [study](https://www.medscape.com/viewarticle/810625), are still a small minority.
1.1.8.2. Con: Appreciating that you're alive is only possible if you're alive. There's no opposite — you can't be regretful that you're not alive.
1.1.8.2.1. Con: There is no evidence to support this claim.
1.1.9. Con: Choosing adoption over abortion is a very different decision, given it requires a woman to go through pregnancy and childbirth, and bring a genetically related child into the world. Therefore it is not actually a reasonable alternative.
1.1.9.1. Pro: Childbirth is a risk for any woman. Women that have health issues and should not give birth as it will impede their health need a viable and legal alternative.
1.1.9.2. Con: If it is more reasonable to place a newborn for adoption rather than kill the newborn, then it's more reasonable to pursue adoption rather than abortion. If someone disagrees with this analogy, then the real disagreement has to do with equal treatment of all humans regarding basic rights, not with adoption vs abortion.
1.1.9.2.1. Con: This analogy doesn't work as choosing for adoption during or at the start of the pregnancy entails being pregnant for longer and giving birth while in the first choice those costs have already been paid.
1.1.9.3. Pro: There are are a lot of social implications for the mother, she would be visibly pregnant to her family and peers and be judged and constantly have to explain herself, as well as having to go through the unpleasant experience of pregnancy with no good outcome for her.
1.1.9.4. Pro: Though adoption is a viable alternative for some, we must then understand that for many women abandoning a child through adoption is just as bad. Either way she is losing a child. With adoption she is then bound to have emotional scars regarding the child’s well being and fears that the unwanted child will resurface later in her life.
1.1.9.5. Pro: There are a large number of financial requirements of being pregnant and having a child, even if you plan to give it up for adoption. These include pre-natal care and hospital care during labour. These costs may mean adoption is not a viable alternative for many women.
1.1.9.5.1. Con: In many cases women may be able to find people wanting to adopt the child even before it is born, and in doing so those potential adoptive parents may be willing to take on some or all of the financial costs of the pregnancy.
1.1.9.6. Pro: The mother could suffer many physical, emotional, psychological, and socioeconomic problems if she had to carry the unwanted baby to term and give birth. Many women - [around 10-15%](https://womensmentalhealth.org/specialty-clinics/postpartum-psychiatric-disorders/) - suffer perinatal mental illness, which can lead to further socioeconomic and physical problems.
1.1.9.7. Pro: Even apart from the trauma of childbirth that a woman must undergo if she chooses adoption, pregnancy and childbirth cause incredible disruption to a woman's life, dreams, and future. A woman may be compelled to drop out of school, may be subjected to stigma when applying for jobs or higher education, or may become sick enough that she is unable to work or study.
1.1.10. Pro: All reasons to have an abortion that relate to post-birth issues such as "finances" or  "emotionally ready" are rendered moot by the availability of adoption. Any hypothetically legitimate reason to justify an abortion would have to relate to a good reason to prevent the birth.
1.1.10.1. Pro: Access to proper sex education and family planning tools in all areas should be the first step in promoting adoption as an alternative.
1.1.10.2. Con: If finances are a concern, then 9 months of going to regular ob/gyn appointments with ultrasounds \(often not covered by insurance\), taking vitamins, and missing work due to feeling ill or bed rest is not affordable, especially if it results in loss of job.
1.1.10.3. Con: For many women, giving birth to a child after carrying it for 9 months, knowing she may never see the child again, is more emotional scarring than aborting a fetus very early on.
1.1.10.4. Con: Adoption may not always be a possibility. Many children given up for adoption are never adopted.
1.1.10.4.1. Pro: There are [hundreds of thousands](https://www.acf.hhs.gov/sites/default/files/cb/afcarsreport22.pdf) of children waiting to be adopted.
