The reality is that tens of thousands of children will never be adopted, and are condemned to a childhood of foster care and youth homes. To say that 'adoption is always an alternative' is simply untrue.
1.1.10.4.2. Pro: About [135,000](http://www.pbs.org/pov/offandrunning/fact-sheet/) children are adopted in the United States each year vs about [650,000](https://www.cdc.gov/reproductivehealth/data_stats/abortion.htm) abortions in 2014. The number of adoptions would need to increase substantially to make up the difference or hundreds of thousands of additional children every year would end up in the already overburdened foster care system.
1.1.10.4.2.1. Con: The number of abortions would decrease if abortion was illegal. Not all unwanted pregnancies remain unwanted and parents may change their mind. Therefore the number of children in foster care would not increase as proposed.
1.1.10.4.2.1.1. Con: Countries in which abortion is available have [similar abortion rates](http://www.independent.co.uk/life-style/health-and-families/health-news/women-in-countries-where-abortion-is-illegal-just-as-likely-to-have-one-as-countries-where-it-is-a7025671.html) to countries in which abortion is illegal.
1.1.10.4.2.2. Con: This problem could simply be solved through better funding and more attention to the system. This is likely given the news coverage and discourse banning abortion would inevitably lead to.
1.1.10.4.2.2.1. Con: The real problem here is that adoption is so incredibly expensive, not that it doesn't have enough funding. It is hard to believe that it actually costs [$34,000](http://www.americanadoptions.com/adopt/the_costs_of_adopting) to facilitate a single adoption.
1.1.10.4.2.2.2. Con: The overlap between politicians who espouse pro-life beliefs and politicians who vote against funding increases for social welfare programs such as Child Protective Services is so significant that if it were a Venn diagram, it would very nearly be a circle. Yet private charity is unlikely to be able to handle the addition of ~500,000 extra children per year to the system.
1.1.10.4.2.3. Pro: The high demand for foster homes would likely force the government to accept applications from individuals who are not well suited for the role.
1.1.10.4.2.4. Pro: Women are likely to seek even more illegal abortions when the foster care system is imploding and can't guarantee a decent life for their children.
1.1.10.4.3. Con: This statement implies that growing up in foster home is worse than being aborted which doesn't seem tenable, especially when the recipient of either option has no say in the matter.
1.1.10.4.3.1. Con: Being aborted can't be bad to the subject because they stop experiencing good and bad.
1.1.10.4.4. Pro: Adoption is not a viable option in a huge number of countries, where social care system is not developed enough, so children remain in the orphanage until they are 18 and then there is no guarantee they will live normal lives as part of society, as they may have become institutionalised.
1.1.10.4.4.1. Pro: As of 2005, countries such as Bangladesh, Indonesia, Myanmar, Benin, Mozambique, Niger, Tanzania had adoption rates between[6-10 per million children under 18 years old and approximately 2 per million children under 5](http://www.un.org/esa/population/publications/adoption2010/child_adoption.pdf).
1.1.10.4.5. Con: Babies are adopted more easily than older children. The average age of[children waiting to be adopted](https://showhope.org/2015/06/19/9-stats-about-the-orphan-crisis/) is 7.5 years.
1.1.10.4.6. Con: Adoptive parents can be chosen before the baby is born. There are people on [waiting lists](https://www.adoption.net/waiting-list-page/) to be chosen already.
1.1.11. Con: Adoption is not always a legitimate alternative.
1.1.11.1. Pro: If a woman is in an abusive relationship, adoption is not always a viable option to abortion as the abusive father still has paternity rights and could claim the child and use it as leverage against the mother, as well as abuse the child itself at some point.
1.1.11.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.10.4.
1.1.11.3. Pro: Adoption is not a viable alternative to abortion in cases when the pregnancy endangers the mother.
1.1.11.3.1. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.5.1.4.
1.1.11.3.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.2.3.1.
1.1.11.4. Pro: Adoption is not a viable option when the mother is a drug addict. Drug addicts, prostitutes, young girls, marginalized women, etc. may not have the resources necessary for proper prenatal care. They may not have the support necessary to contact adoptive parents.
1.1.11.5. Pro: Forcing women to give birth will lead to an increase of the number of children waiting to be adopted. This will ultimately increase tax payer burden as it is the state who funds the resources required to care for these children. Taxes will go up and affect everyone, because it is considerably more expensive to fund many individual lives over many years then it would be to fund the organizations that perform abortions \(which is something that is already done\).
1.1.11.6. Pro: Adoption is not an alternative when abortion is chosen to avoid health risks, known pathologies would lead to a painful life for a future life, or the pregnancy itself would otherwise negatively impact the life of the mother.
1.1.11.7. Pro: -> See 1.1.9.5.
1.1.12. Con: The life long impacts of adoption, including [trauma](https://postinstitute.com/the-adopted-child-trauma-and-its-impact/) is well [evidenced](https://www.psychology.org.au/inpsych/2014/august/green/) and documented.
1.1.13. Con: With option of choice, women and girls will be less likely to go to the underground market \(illegal providers of abortions\), but rather be empowered legally to speak to those who could most offer them support and counselling, regardless of their choice. This would make it easier to keep a baby or allow it to be adopted because social supports would be more readily mobilized.
1.1.14. Pro: Technology will make early adoptions even easier, by allowing things such as embryo transfers for others to become surrogate parents.
1.1.14.1. Pro: [Embryo transfers](https://www.nytimes.com/1984/02/04/us/infertile-woman-has-baby-through-embryo-transfer.html?sec=health) can be performed. This is where a child in his or her earliest stages of development can be transferred from one womb to another, a surrogate's. This circumvents murdering the child or having to bring the child to term. Advances in technology have only served to strengthen the pro-life's argument. In fact, this solution has been available since the 1980s.
1.1.14.2. Con: Although embryo transfer is now more prevalent, the costs which are \(in the UK\) [in the thousands,](https://www.bournhall.co.uk/fees-funding/fee-calculator/) are not feasible or easily accessible to most women, some even [going into bankruptcy,](https://www.shape.com/lifestyle/mind-and-body/infertility-ivf-surrogacy-costs) potentially putting them under further financial and emotional stress.
1.1.15. Con: Many women who consider abortion the better choice when they discover they're pregnant won't be able to give the child up for adoption after spending nine months gestating it and then giving birth. This could leave them with the same problems they wanted to avoid through an abortion.
1.1.16. Pro: Adoption agencies can ensure that the child is matched with a family that has similar values and beliefs to that of the biological mother.
1.1.16.1. Con: This really isn't an important aspect. The mother's values and beliefs might be the reason why she is unable to care for the child.
1.1.16.2. Con: There is no way to ensure that information can be verified, potential parents can just lie about their values to get a child faster.
1.1.16.2.1. Con: The process for adopting a child can be [very long](https://adoptionnetwork.com/how-long-does-it-take-to-adopt-a-child), and it involves a [psychological assessment](http://www.annegraham.ca/international-adoption-psychological-assessment.html) that can hardly be forged.
1.1.16.3. Pro: There is a [shortage](http://www.americanadoptions.com/pregnant/waiting_adoptive_families) of children in need of parents in the west, meaning that agencies can choose parents from a large competitive pool.
1.1.16.3.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.3.4.
1.1.17. Con: The question here is whether women should or should not have the right to choose abortion, so the fact that adoption is a viable option is not incompatible with having abortion as another option.
1.1.17.1. Con: If it is true that adoption is a viable option, then abortion is not the only option. If there is another option besides abortion, with the benefit of saving lives, it should be valued over abortion. Thus adoption is a better option than abortion. We should do our best to encourage the better option over the weaker and ethically problematic one.
1.1.17.1.1. Con: Believing one option to be "better" is not an argument against people having multiple options.
1.1.17.2. Pro: Adoption is another choice that a woman should be able to make, but not forced into.
1.2. Pro: There are many reasons a woman may not be equipped to or want to raise a child. In these cases, it is important that she is able to choose abortion.
1.2.1. Con: -> See 1.1.
1.2.2. Pro: A woman may not feel emotionally, mentally or otherwise prepared to have a child, and ultimately this could be damaging for the child and for the relationship between the mother and child.
1.2.2.1. Con: Not being prepared to carry the consequences of your decisions and actions is not justification for terminating a human life. Both parents should accept the responsibility they brought upon themselves and prioritize the life they brought into the world. Mental and emotional readiness is something a person wills themselves into, not something that comes out of the blue one day.
1.2.2.1.1. Con: Some pregnancies are the result of an act of violence like rape.
1.2.2.1.1.1. Con: The crimes of a father have not, do not, and shall not, in the context of a Western, post-Enlightenment justice system, transfer guilt to a child of that father. An attempt to justify homicide by citing the guilt of a relative in an unrelated crime is a non-sequitur.
1.2.2.1.1.1.1. Con: Neither shall that guilt be transferred to the woman who was raped and who is a fully fledged human with all the rights they're entailed.
1.2.2.1.1.1.2. Con: The use of the term homicide when used on a human fetus \(particulary before a certain period of development\) is dubious and opinionated at best. Women, who are in this case victims of a crime themselves, have right for a different opinion on the matter and should not be forced to drastically change their lives because of someone else's world view.
1.2.2.1.1.2. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.2.3.1.1.
1.2.2.1.1.3. Pro: In cases of non consensual sex, the person who was forced by someone to have sexual intercourse has no moral obligation to not kill the unborn-person. Every harm caused to the unborn is responsibility of the person who forced the other to have sexual intercourse.
1.2.2.1.1.3.1. Con: You cannot transfer responsibility for harm to another person. The person responsible for the abortion is the person going to the clinic.
1.2.2.1.1.4. Con: In the rare case of pregnancy due to rape, terminating the life of the unborn child will not correct the horror done to the woman, it will simply pass on the act of force to an innocent party.
1.2.2.1.1.4.1. Con: Termination of the unborn child's life is not done to mitigate the effects of the crime on one's past, it is to minimize its effects on one's future.
1.2.2.1.1.4.2. Con: Terminating a pregnancy in the case of rape is not typically done with the intention of changing the fact she was raped in the past.
1.2.2.1.1.5. Con: Just because a person is conceived in unfortunate and difficult circumstances does not mean their life has zero/very low value and their existence can be terminated without any moral qualm.
1.2.2.1.1.6. Pro: When women experience a trauma such as rape it is understandable that they would want to forget or move on from such an experience. Carrying and then having a child fathered by their rapist does not allow them to do this.
1.2.2.1.1.6.1. Con: Possible or even probable psychological stress is not, has never been, and never should be, morally, ethically, or legally, justification for homicide. Lethal force used in the face of an imminent threat of physical harm is the only excuse to homicide.
1.2.2.1.1.6.2. Con: About 70% of women who get pregnant due to rape choose to keep their children. In two studies done on the topic, none of these women later regretted the choice. Of the 30% who chose to abort the child, about 78% later regretted it. \(Mahkorn and Dolan, p. 194\).
1.2.2.1.1.6.2.1. Pro: "I, having lived through rape, and also having raised a child ‘conceived in rape’, feel personally assaulted and insulted every time I hear that abortion should be legal because of rape and incest. I feel that we’re being used to further the abortion issue, even though we’ve not been asked to tell our side of the story."  [Kathleen DeZeeuw](http://afterabortion.org/2005/victims-and-victors-speaking-out-about-their-pregnancies-abortions-and-children-resulting-from-sexual-assault/)
1.2.2.1.1.7. Pro: Raped women often don't have an option to use birth control.
1.2.2.1.1.8. Con: The number of abortions as a result of rape are [around or less than 1%](http://www.nytimes.com/1989/10/13/us/rape-and-incest-just-1-of-all-abortions.html) of abortions.
1.2.2.1.1.8.1. Con: That data does not take into consideration that the majority of rapes and consent violations are unreported.
1.2.2.1.1.8.1.1. Con: This doesn't really matter if said incident didn't end in a pregnancy, therefore, no abortion was needed. If an unreported rape did end in pregnancy, the woman could have had an abortion without the need to report the rape.
1.2.2.1.1.8.1.2. Con: It's estimated that about [2/3s of all rapes go unreported.](https://www.nij.gov/topics/crime/rape-sexual-violence/Pages/rape-notification.aspx) Based on this, one could speculate that as much as 3% of abortions are necessitated by rape. This estimation is still a small fraction of abortion cases.
1.2.2.1.1.8.2. Con: The data in these studies is also very antiquated in that the newest data cited is from 1987.
1.2.2.1.1.8.3. Pro: This extreme outlier cannot be used as a valid argument for the legalization of the other 99% of abortion cases.
1.2.2.1.2. Con: Many women do not become pregnant by choice. It is wrong to force these women to remain pregnant when they do not want to be.
1.2.2.1.2.1. Pro: Contraception can fail during sex and lead to pregnancy.
1.2.2.1.2.1.1. Con: If a person does not want to conceive a child \(be it man or woman\) they simply should not have sex. Creating new life is an inevitable consequence of having sex. While risk can be mitigated it can not be avoided entirely.
1.2.2.1.2.1.1.1. Con: Skin cancer is a natural consequence of sun exposure. Would you advise people who don't want skin cancer to simply not go outside? Going outside and sex are both natural components of healthy lives. Both entail unwanted risks that can be only partially mitigated. That does not mean however that they should be avoided.
1.2.2.1.2.1.1.1.1. Con: Having children is also a natural component of a healthy life. It is not one that we all chose but it's the reason sex exists. Childbirth has historically been associated with the natural act of sex.
1.2.2.1.2.1.1.1.2. Con: Whether or not someone goes out in the sun it that person's choice. On the one hand they may get skin cancer, on the other they may deal with vitamin D deficiency. Likewise having sex is a person's choice. They may get a child or they may die lonely. What isn't a choice a person gets to make is killing someone else, regardless of weather they got skin cancer or pregnant.
1.2.2.1.2.1.2. Con: The frequent failure of contraception does not mean the woman is forced to become pregnant anymore than the far more rare failure of a parachute to open means a skydiver was forced to jump out of a plane. Failure of a precaution taken doesn't indicate one was forced into an action or consequence.
1.2.2.1.2.1.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.4.5.
1.2.2.1.2.1.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.
1.2.2.1.2.1.5. Con: Contraceptives advertise that they are not 100% effective. Even though these devices or drugs decrease the likelihood of pregnancy they don't negate the responsibility for the risk of the action chosen.
1.2.2.1.2.2. Con: If this were the case, an analogy could be drawn to men impregnating women. A boy could make several girls pregnant, say he did not choose to, and claim he has no obligation to support them.
1.2.2.1.2.2.1. Con: This is a valid but separate argument about legally severing paternity obligations.  Whether a boy is legally obligated to provide support to a child is not equivalent to a woman being required to give up her bodily autonomy for someone else.
1.2.2.1.2.2.2. Con: Having to carry a child for 9 months is not in any way comparable to paying child support as one has physical and emotional consequences while the other is a mere financial consequence.
1.2.2.1.2.2.2.1. Con: Whether pregnancy is experienced as a burden or a joy, or whether financial support is a hardship or peanuts, is a matter of personal circumstance. These apples and pears should not be compared or weighed against each other.
1.2.2.1.2.3. Con: But you have to keep in mind that the preborn child didn't have a choice either. The child did not choose to be inside that woman's body. It's not their fault that they happen to be there. They did nothing wrong. They should not be killed.
1.2.2.1.2.3.1. Con: There is no such thing as a pre-born 'child'. There are things such as a fertilized egg or embryo which grows into a foetus after the first trimester. The discussion about embryonic or foetal rights is an ethical one and highly controversial. In several \(religiously inspired\) constitutions \([lawteacher.net](https://www.lawteacher.net/free-law-essays/medical-law/embryo-and-foetal-rights.php)\), 'personal' rights are granted to embryos or foetuses but there is no consensus in philosophy, law or politics that this is the most accurate way of terminology.
1.2.2.1.2.3.2. Con: A tumor does not have a choice. The tumor did not choose to be in a body. It's not it's fault it happened to be there. It is alive and owes its existence to its host. It should not be killed even if it is unwanted.
1.2.2.1.2.4. Pro: -> See 1.2.2.1.1.
1.2.2.1.2.5. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.
1.2.2.1.2.6. Con: Medicine took care of this, by giving women the opportunity to prevent pregnancy. With the safety net of condoms, contraceptives and the morning-after pills the chance of getting pregnant is almost zero. The probability is [0.006%.](http://www.mathscareers.org.uk/article/statistically-safe-sex/)
1.2.2.1.2.6.1. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.
1.2.2.1.2.6.2. Con: Given that many women still find themselves in circumstances where they are pregnant and do not want to be, the bodily autonomy argument stands in those cases.
1.2.2.1.2.6.3. Con: We need not consider the circumstances of any pregnancy. If we accept the legal and moral concept of bodily autonomy it would be true in any circumstance that a person has no obligation to support the life of another with their body. Thus it would be true of any pregnancy that it's bearer would have the right to terminate it. We could claim it's worse if someone could have prevented an abortion with contraception, but that has no bearing on whether or not it should be allowed.
1.2.2.1.2.6.3.1. Con: Abortion is a unilateral decision involving two parties, therefore bodily autonomy doesn't apply.
1.2.2.1.2.6.3.1.1. Con: Bodily autonomy means no one has to use their body to support another even if that person will die if the support is lost.
1.2.2.1.2.6.4. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.4.5.
1.2.2.1.2.6.5. Con: Specific mental health situations side, access to medicine doesn't nullify one's body autonomy.
1.2.2.1.2.6.5.1. Con: Actually it does. Medicine allows for the autonomy of one individual \(the mother\), without violating the autonomy of another \(the child\). You have a right to be naked but you can’t exercise that right in front of a nursery school. If there are reasonable avenues that maintain the autonomy of both individuals \(prevention of conception\) then outlawing a single mode \(termination\) that violates one individual’s but upholds another’s should be pursued.
1.2.2.1.2.7. Con: \<0.05% of abortions result from rape. ~7% result from fetal or maternal health problems. [~92.5%](http://abort73.com/abortion_facts/us_abortion_statistics/) result from the woman's lifestyle choices or socio-economic status. Immaturity, irresponsibility or financial status are not a legal, moral, or ethical defences for murder. By law people are not permitted to murder their spouses or children because they are inconvenient to their lifestyle or expensive to maintain.
1.2.2.1.2.8. Pro: The urge to have sex is a primal and critical part of nature. One does not "choose" to have sex. Reproduction is a force of nature.
1.2.2.1.2.8.1. Con: Abortion is not a part of nature, abandonment is. The runt always gets left behind. Can't bring nature into an argument that takes a rational decision.
1.2.2.1.2.9. Con: Women consent to the risk of becoming pregnant whenever they choose to have sex.
1.2.2.1.2.9.1. Con: We do not hold people responsible for all unintended consequences of their actions. If a woman did not intend to become pregnant as a result of sex, she should not be forced to remain pregnant.
1.2.2.1.2.9.1.1. Con: When one human makes another human biologically dependent, they have an obligation to provide for that need they created.
1.2.2.1.2.9.1.2. Con: We do not hold people responsible when the consequences of an action could not have been foreseen, but pregnancy is a very foreseeable consequence of sex.
1.2.2.1.2.9.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.4.
1.2.2.1.2.9.3. Con: When women use contraception it is clear they are trying to avoid pregnancy and therefore should not be held responsible for the outcome.
1.2.2.1.2.9.3.1. Pro: Use of contraception indicates consent to pregnancy has explicitly not been given.
1.2.2.1.2.9.3.1.1. Con: Virtually all common contraceptives have clear and explicit labeling indicating their use is not 100% effective. If “buyer beware” is a reasonable principle, and the labels are clear, all literate women using these products have given consent.
1.2.2.1.2.9.3.2. Pro: -> See 1.2.2.1.2.1.
1.2.2.1.2.9.3.3. Con: Considering the 'consequence' is a large one, involving the creation of a new genetically distinct human life, mere implied intent to avoid new life forming is not enough ethically to support destroying human life once formed.
1.2.2.1.2.9.3.4. Con: If I drive drunk, but only at 30 on a 65, and I hit someone and kill them, I am not free from responsibility because my slow driving shows an unwillingness to kill. There is a surefire way to not hit someone: not drive. There is a surefire way not to get pregnant: not have sex. Birth control is not the best measure a woman could take, therefore she is not fully committed to not having a baby.
1.2.2.1.2.9.3.5. Con: There is a always a risk of failure with contraception which women need to take account of when they have sex. It is insufficient to say that one intended to avoid pregnancy.
1.2.2.1.2.9.4. Pro: -> See 1.2.2.1.2.1.1.
1.2.2.1.2.9.5. Pro: When someone hits the accelerator and rear-ends the car in front of them, they cannot avoid responsibility by saying "I didn't consent to the accident."  Similarly, if people have sex, they cannot avoid responsibility by saying "I didn't consent to pregnancy."
1.2.2.1.2.9.5.1. Con: This is a false analogy. When someone hits the accelerator, that is their choice. Sex, on the other hand, is not always consensual. If a woman is raped, then she can absolutely claim that she consented to neither sex, nor pregnancy.
1.2.2.1.2.9.6. Con: Arguing that in order for a woman to have sex she must consent to the possibility of pregnancy and therefore take responsibility by carrying the child is unreasonable. While biology dictates that women are the carriers of children, removing the means for a woman to end a pregnancy means restricting that woman to a child-rearing role even if it is not one she desires.
1.2.2.1.2.9.6.1. Con: Woman having to assume child-rearing role due to accidental pregnancy is no less unreasonable than a person having to work low-wage jobs because of lack of talent in better paying fields or means to get proper education towards it. People should bear responsibility for consequences of their actions.
1.2.2.1.2.9.6.1.1. Con: People at least have the option to cultivate their talents or acquire an education in some fashion. For half the population the possibility of child-rearing is a consequence they were born into rather than a responsibility that they actively chose.
1.2.2.1.2.9.6.1.1.1. Con: Most of the people in the world have no option to pursue education or cultivate their talent due to being born in to a poor family in a rural area of an undeveloped nation or other circumstances outside their control.
1.2.2.1.2.9.6.2. Con: This is an argument against biology. Women are already deemed the child-bearers by nature.
1.2.2.1.2.9.6.2.1. Con: Women have many other relevant roles in society and nature besides "child-bearer."
1.2.2.1.2.9.6.2.1.1. Con: This being true does not remove their critical to society role as child-bearers.
1.2.2.1.2.9.6.2.2. Con: Denying women the right to terminate pregnancies at an early stage implies that giving birth to children is the most important thing a woman will ever do; that her ability to give birth trumps any other contribution to [society](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2014/oct/14/abortion-right-to-privacy-women-right-to-equality) she could possibly make.
1.2.2.1.2.9.6.2.2.1. Con: Having a child and making an important contribution to society "X" is considered greater than only doing "X". 
Also, having a child is one of the most important things one can do. Nevertheless, denying the possibility to abort an already conceived child does not mean that having a child is the only contribution said person could make.
1.2.2.1.2.9.6.2.2.2. Con: An implication must rely on an assumption which is not a universal truth. Many women who have made great contributions to society have done so as mothers. To assume that a woman's worth to society is lessened if she is a mother is incorrect.
1.2.2.1.2.9.6.2.2.3. Pro: Denying women access to safe, legal abortion in the interests of the embryo values the woman’s actual life less than the potential life of the embryo.
1.2.2.1.2.9.6.2.2.4. Con: Denial of the right to terminate a pregnancy says nothing about the relative importance of giving birth. This does not follow.
1.2.2.1.2.9.7. Pro: In the biological process of having sexual intercourse always lies the possibility to create life. If people want the freedom to have sexual intercourse without the purpose of procreating they also have to accept the obligation to care for the life they created even if they don't want to.
1.2.2.1.2.9.8. Con: Sex is between two people. Both are responsible for a pregnancy, not just women.
1.2.2.1.2.10. Con: No one 'forces' the woman to remain pregnant or give birth by not allowing them to abort. Force, by its very definition, requires further work or action on something. It is biology, not force of arms or law, that will compel the process of development to continue until birth. Refusal to permit a human to make a forceful change to nature is not the logical or ethical equivalent of a human or society forcing a natural process to remain.
1.2.2.1.2.10.1. Con: Under this idea, we should not treat cancer or other terminal illnesses and allow a natural process to remain. We shouldn't create rules to differentiate between the natural forces we can stop.
1.2.2.1.2.10.1.1. Con: This is a false equivalency. Cancer is not natural. The body is not made to handle cancer. Cancer serves no function. Cancer is a disease often contracted by contact with unnatural chemicals called carcinogens that alters the natural sequencing of a person's DNA into an unnatural one that causes unnatural growths in the body. There is nothing "natural" about cancer. Pregnancy on the other hand is the very definition of natural.
1.2.2.1.2.10.2. Con: Being prevented from doing something by the state, that you would otherwise be able to freely choose, is the same as being forced to do something you do not want to do.
1.2.2.1.2.10.2.1. Pro: In this instance, by making abortion illegal, the state is not allowing women to end a pregnancy which they desire to do so, which can be viewed as forcing them to remain pregnant.
1.2.2.1.2.10.2.1.1. Con: "A bans B from using force Z to escape state Y" is not a logical equivalent to "A forces B to remain in state Y." B is already in state Y, and A commits no force unless it first forced B into state Y.
1.2.2.1.2.10.2.1.1.1. Pro: If the state doesn't allow someone to opt out of life via suicide, it isn't forcing that person to remain alive. The person already is alive, and will remain that way. Rather, the state has banned the suicidal person's request to use force to change his/her state.
1.2.2.1.2.10.2.2. Con: Medical procedures are rarely things that someone has the freedom to just choose to do, regardless of whether the law allows a procedure or not. Many factors besides law affect them: availability, cost, ethics, health needs, etc.
1.2.2.1.2.10.2.3. Con: Being physically forced to do something you dislike and being legally prevented from an action you are theoretically capable of are not logical equivalents.
1.2.2.1.2.10.2.4. Pro: Being prevented from doing something is in effect the same as being forced not to do something. The result is that the situation is left unchanged, which in this case is carrying a baby.
1.2.2.1.2.10.3. Con: It is biology that determines that some people have poor eye sight. However, if the state made glasses or contact lenses illegal, it would be legitimate to say that it was the state forcing someone to continue having difficulty seeing.
1.2.2.1.2.10.3.1. Con: That would not be a legitimate statement, as force is opposed to leaving something at rest. Prohibition didn't force people to stay sober, it was their natural state sans alcohol. Rather, prohibition removed the legal option of drink. The only force comes in when someone then broke the law and was arrested.
1.2.2.1.2.10.3.2. Con: The government does temporarily ban, or rather prohibit, certain medicines from distribution for a time. This may be while the FDA approves a drug, or to protect the initial intellectual property of a pharmacy. Such actions banning a potential remedy do not constitute force on the people who remain in their sick state.
1.2.2.1.2.10.3.2.1. Con: Taking time to approve of a drug does not force people to remain in their sick state, because it is not yet known what the alternative is. Protecting intellectual property is not force, because another pharmaceutical company is necessarily selling a similar product. Neither one is comparable to banning a remedy solely because the government decides that remaining in the unwell state is preferable to the remedy.
1.2.2.1.2.10.3.3. Con: The analogy does not fit. Glasses are a non-invasive tool which people wear to remedy a specific problem with one of the human senses. Abortion is an invasive surgery that's purpose is to terminates a human life, not a physical tool, and is only rarely related to a specific health problem of the mother.
1.2.2.1.2.10.3.3.1. Con: The details of the condition and the modification are irrelevant to the discussion of whether or not forbidding modifications to a person's natural state constitutes forcing that person to remain in their natural state. Those may be reasons why it would be justified to force a person to remain in their natural state, but do not pertain to the definition of force.
1.2.2.1.3. Pro: People are put in situations they are not ready to face all the time. They deal with them successfully by learning and adapting rather than running away from them.
1.2.2.1.4. Pro: Overcoming challenges is what makes a person [great](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sefscV3GvWM).
1.2.2.2. Pro: A [study](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16713893) of children born between 1961-63 investigated the adult mental health outcomes of those born to women who twice requested an abortion \(220 cases\) and compared to those whose mother did not request an abortion \(220 matched controls\). Significant differences in mental health outcomes were found between the two groups, all demonstrating worse outcomes for the "unwanted" children. This supports that being born from an unwanted pregnancy is a risk factor for poor mental health in adulthood.
1.2.2.2.1. Con: When abortion is allowed, the resulting children are killed. Death is a much harsher outcome than "a variety of social and psychological problems."
1.2.2.2.1.1. Con: The individual death of a semi- or non-conscious life isn't automatically a much harsher outcome than a civilization with a variety of social and psychological problems.
1.2.2.3. Con: A damaged, imperfect relationship / child would in most cases be better than no relationship / child.

1.2.2.4.2. Con: This is an argument for the state providing more support for mothers rather than for allowing abortion.
1.2.2.4.2.1. Con: Humans live in societies, not in abstract environments devoid of constraints. Therefore, forgetting this environment would be a mistake: if the state is unable to provide support for mothers \(for any reason, let it be economic situation or established laws\), abortion would enable better financial survival of mothers.

1.2.2.4.3. Con: Throughout history most people lived in far poorer conditions, yet managed to raise more children per household than we do today.

Therefore a lot of them were not raised, they died before maturity. On the contrary, today, it's no longer necessary to have a lot of children to ensure descendants.

Con: One of the reasons families were bigger in past centuries was because children could provide to the household economy at a much younger age and without having most of the qualifications that are necessary now. 1.2.2.4.3.2.1. Con: Supporting them until they finish a degree is an exaggeration. There are no age restrictions on certain types of jobs in the U.S. At 14, they can work limited hours at any non hazardous job. At 16, unlimited hours at any no hazardous job. At 18, unlimited at any job. If they choose college, there are grants loans that can pay their way if the parents can't.

1.2.2.4.5. Pro: Women who are denied abortions and instead give birth are [~3.8 times more likely to be in poverty](http://ajph.aphapublications.org/doi/pdf/10.2105/AJPH.2017.304247) and ~6.3 times more likely to be on public assistance 6 months after denial than women who received abortions. They are also more likely to be in poverty and remain on public assistance for 4 years after denial of abortion.

Pro: If a mother's choice to terminate her pregnancy is paramount and can be justified with as little as demonstrating that the child would have a negative effect on her life then the viability of the child to survive outside of the womb is irrelevant, and can be trumped even at full term by the mother's feelings.
1.2.5.4.1.7.4.3.1. Con: This same logic could be applied to babies, children, teenagers, and even adult children. The mother's feeling are not always what is most important and don't give her the right to kill anyone.
1.2.5.4.1.7.5. Con: Under-age abortions could result in legal debates regarding who has autonomy over a minor's body.
1.2.5.4.1.7.5.1. Pro: Minors have natural autonomy over their bodies and will do certain things regardless of controls inflicted upon them.
1.2.5.4.1.7.5.1.1. Pro: Maybe adults have too much control over minors.
1.2.5.4.1.7.5.1.2. Con: There are laws that say when a child is lawfully of age to choose sexual relations. Those same laws should apply to the age in deciding to having an abortion
1.2.5.4.1.7.5.2. Con: This question has already been resolved in most countries where abortion is legal either by statute or by case law.
1.2.5.4.1.7.5.2.1. Pro: In the [UK](http://www.healthcentre.org.uk/abortion/abortion-teenage.html) minors \(if they are seen as competent by medical staff\) are allowed to seek abortions without parental consent.
1.2.5.4.1.7.5.2.2. Pro: In [South Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minors_and_abortion), any woman of any age can get an abortion on request, with no reasons given, if she is less than 13 weeks pregnant, as long as she is able to give informed consent.
1.2.5.4.1.7.5.2.3. Pro: In [India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minors_and_abortion) girls under 18 need parental consent.
1.2.5.4.1.7.5.2.4. Pro: In [Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minors_and_abortion) parental consent is always required if the woman seeking abortion is a minor.
1.2.5.4.1.7.5.2.5. Pro: In [Australia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minors_and_abortion) a minor does not require parental consent or notification except in Western Australia, where in the event of the woman being under 16 years of age one of her parents must be notified, except where permission has been granted by the Children's Court or the woman does not live with her parents.
1.2.5.4.1.7.5.2.6. Pro: In [Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minors_and_abortion) parental authorisation is required if the woman is under 18.
1.2.5.4.1.7.5.2.7. Pro: In [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minors_and_abortion) a pregnant minor may ask for an abortion without consulting her parents first, but she has to be accompanied to the clinic by an adult of her choice. This adult must not tell her parents or any third party about the abortion.
1.2.5.4.1.7.5.2.8. Pro: In [Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minors_and_abortion) girls under the age of 18 must get written permission from a parent or guardian before being allowed an abortion.
1.2.5.4.1.7.5.2.9. Pro: Minors are allowed to have abortions without parental consent in [New Zealand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minors_and_abortion).
1.2.5.4.1.7.5.3. Con: Assuming the mother is conscious, there is no conceivable situation where in a fetus would have more legal autonomy over the mother's body than the mother, whatever the mother's age.
1.2.5.4.1.7.5.4. Con: Autonomy in medical decisions is distinct from legal autonomy \(age of majority, voting\), as established by different ages of consent for medical procedures even in countries without abortion legislation \(i.e. Canada\).
1.2.5.4.1.7.6. Pro: If women do not have the right to choose an abortion, someone else should not decide they have more of a right to deny them one. Those people do not have to live with the decision and it's likely they would be offended themselves if someone made a decision about how they should use their own bodies.
1.2.5.4.1.7.6.1. Pro: For very good reasons, we do not legally require a parent to donate a kidney to one of their children if that child will die without it. Abortion should both be as legal and morally reprehensible as refusing to donate a kidney to your dying child.
1.2.5.4.1.7.6.1.1. Con: An invasive procedure to transplant an organ is vastly different from childbirth because of the possibilities of multiple donors being available for the organ transplant. Additionally, removing a vital organ is different than removing a viable fetus. An organ, by itself, is not a human being. Thus, the analogy is false.
1.2.5.4.1.7.6.1.1.1. Con: The difference is technical, but ethically the analogy is legitimate. In both cases, a person is subject to an authoritarian decision about her own body to guarantee another person life.
1.2.5.4.1.7.6.1.1.2. Con: The number of valid donors doesn't change one's bodily autonomy over organ transplant, so it shouldn't hold sway here.
1.2.5.4.1.7.6.1.2. Con: A baby in the womb doesn't need an organ from the mother, only nutrients and oxygen. An abortion would be more correctly viewed as deciding you don't want to feed your child.
1.2.5.4.1.7.6.1.3. Pro: Not everything immoral should be made illegal. We do not make laws against *failing* to give other people food or shelter -- even though we may sometimes agree that it is immoral to withold food or shelter. It takes a great deal of art to decide when/if a person is morally culpable for withholding her/his property or body or time from a person in need. States are incapable of walking that line, so should make no laws mandating gifts of property or body or time to other beings.
1.2.5.4.1.7.6.1.3.1. Con: You can go to jail for failing to give your child food and [shelter](http://criminal.findlaw.com/criminal-charges/child-neglect.html).
1.2.5.4.1.7.6.1.4. Con: It should be a legal requirement for one of the parents to give a kidney to their child if necessary.
1.2.5.4.1.7.6.1.4.1. Con: This is not tied to the debate at hand. At present, there is no legal requirement or obligation to do so.
1.2.5.4.1.7.6.2. Con: A judge in a court of law has every right to prescribe the necessary course of action, whether they would or wouldn't like to be on the receiving end of the same judgement. Their obligation is to the law, not to the defendant.
1.2.5.4.1.7.6.3. Con: By the same argument, an aborted child also has to live \(or rather die\) with their mother's decision and it's likely they would be far more offended themselves were they given the chance to be part of the discussion concerning their termination.
1.2.5.4.1.7.7. Con: After viewing an ultrasound, making them aware that it is a baby, [most](http://www.politifact.com/wisconsin/statements/2013/jul/12/rachel-campos-duffy/more-90-women-change-their-minds-about-having-abor/) [women](http://www.lifenews.com/2013/02/07/78-of-pregnant-women-seeing-an-ultrasound-reject-abortions/) will not choose abortion. This means the choice is often not fully informed, and may be a reason to restrict women's ability to choose.
1.2.5.4.1.7.7.1. Con: It does not follow that the choice is often not fully informed. What follows is merely that emotional manipulation is somewhat effective.
1.2.5.4.1.7.7.1.1. Con: An ultrasound is not emotional manipulation if it is only provided as part of the medical process. This simply gives more information to the woman who is making the decision.
1.2.5.4.1.7.7.2. Con: This is an argument for giving women the full information before they make their choice, but does not justify stripping them of the choice entirely.
1.2.5.4.1.7.8. Con: Women do not have the right to abortions universally, as it is not recognised as a fundamental human right.
1.2.5.4.1.7.8.1. Pro: Human rights are those rights which allow for the flourishing of all humanity. Choosing abortion prevents the flourishing of some of humanity \(i.e. the aborted\). Therefore, choosing abortion is not considered a human right.
1.2.5.4.1.7.8.1.1. Con: Human rights are a misdirected ideal: there are civil rights, not human rights and, those rights ought extend to all persons rather than exclusively to human persons or even humans that happen to not be persons.
1.2.5.4.1.7.8.1.2. Con: This is not the definition of human rights. Human rights are simply rights which every human has. Apart from that, the definition is very much a matter of opinion and belief. Hardly a good ground to base an argument on as the argument starts falling apart as soon as someone else counters it with their definition.
1.2.5.4.1.7.8.2. Con: The topic is how things should be, not how they are nor how they got to be this way.
1.2.5.4.1.7.9. Pro: -> See 1.2.2.1.2.
1.2.5.4.1.7.10. Con: A woman’s right to choose has become a tool in the hands of a man to further oppress a woman for his sake. A woman’s legal right to choose abortion brings with it expectations from men. It encourages and enables men to threaten or coerce women into abortions to further free the men from any consequence of a sexually free lifestyle. Men oppress women in this way regardless of the woman's actual desired choice.
1.2.5.4.1.7.10.1. Con: Pressure and expectations come with any social liberty. Men needing to take responsibility and contemplate consequences for their actions does not translate to needing to further restrict the rights of women.
1.2.5.4.1.7.11. Pro: Due to their unique ability to give birth to new life, women enjoy the privilege to decide over its fate. In blunt terms: a time-limited license to kill. The question is not whether abortion terminates life, but when and where this privilege ends and protection by law should kick in.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12. Pro: Women have a moral right to bodily autonomy.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.1. Pro: Women should have the inalienable right to pursue [happiness](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2014/oct/14/abortion-right-to-privacy-women-right-to-equality), which includes the right to control their lives.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.1.1. Con: The right to pursue happiness should not trump one's duty to others. Women and men should make reasonable sacrifices to accommodate the needs of others. If men had an absolute right to pursue their own happiness and control their lives, then men would be permitted to skip child support payments.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.1.2. Con: -> See 1.2.2.1.2.9.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.1.3. Pro: The responsibility of carrying and having a child in many cases falls on the mother, as fathers may not be in the picture or may not want to be involved. Having a child then changes a woman's entire life and her ability to pursue her idea of happiness in a way that does not happen to men.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2. Pro: [Sovereignty](http://torstone.org/featured-articles/what-is-body-sovereignty) begins with the individual. As a result and without reservation, one has absolute right over their own body.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1. Con: Individuals live in societies and society makes decisions that affect individuals. Individuals cannot do everything they might like to do; society imposes rules for the good of all and could not function if individuals claimed precedence. There can be no blanket rule that allows individuals \(male or female\) do whatever they want to do. Society must debate and deliberate, review and rule.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.1. Con: This implies that society is harmed because of abortions, and that it benefits society for children to be born. If a child is born to an impoverished family, it is doubtful it will be beneficial to society.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.1.1. Pro: There is evidence to suggest that the Roe v. Wade decision to legalize abortion in 1978 was responsible for the [dramatic decrease](http://pricetheory.uchicago.edu/levitt/Papers/DonohueLevittTheImpactOfLegalized2001.pdf) in violent crime the United states experienced through at least 1999.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.1.1.1. Pro: Five US states legalised abortion three years before Roe v. Wade. Crime started falling three years earlier in these states, with property crime \(done by younger people\) falling before violent [crime](http://freakonomics.com/2005/05/15/abortion-and-crime-who-should-you-believe/).
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.1.1.2. Pro: After Roe v. Wade, the availability of abortions differed widely across US states. From the period 1985-1997, when the post-Roe generation was reaching peak crime ages, the states where abortion was more readily available saw a 30% decline in crime relative to states with low levels of [availability](http://freakonomics.com/2005/05/15/abortion-and-crime-who-should-you-believe/).
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.1.1.3. Pro: When we compare arrest rates of people born in the same state, just before and just after abortion legalisation, we once again see the identical pattern of lower arrest rates for those born after [legalisation](http://freakonomics.com/2005/05/15/abortion-and-crime-who-should-you-believe/) than before.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.1.1.4. Pro: There is evidence from Canada, Australia, and Romania that also supports the hypothesis that abortion reduces [crime](http://freakonomics.com/2005/05/15/abortion-and-crime-who-should-you-believe/).
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.1.1.5. Pro: Studies have shown a reduction in infanticide, teenage drug use, and teenage childbearing consistent with the theory that abortion will reduce other social ills similar to [crime](http://freakonomics.com/2005/05/15/abortion-and-crime-who-should-you-believe/).
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.1.1.6. Con: To not take into account the increase in law enforcement, both in terms of numbers of personnel, advanced weaponry, and tactics, and to not take into account the dramatic increase in incarcerations during this same period, in a discussion of decreased criminality, seems egregious.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.1.1.7. Pro: Research correlates legalized abortion to a [lower rate of violent crime](http://pricetheory.uchicago.edu/levitt/Papers/DonohueLevittTheImpactOfLegalized2001.pdf).
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.1.2. Con: Many children born to impoverished families have ended up being beneficial to [society](https://www.quora.com/Who-are-some-notable-examples-of-people-who-were-born-poor-but-still-went-on-to-achieve-wonders-and-what-were-the-reasons-behind-how-their-life-changed-at-one-point-in-time).
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.2. Con: There is a limit between what is considered private domain and public domain. Regulations regarding ones body should not be imposed, unless there is a direct thread to society, such as, for example, a danger of epidemic outbreak. This rhetoric does not apply to this case. It is an intrusion on personal freedom originating from religious dogmatism.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.3. Con: It's naive to think that the "society" acts only for the common good. The "society" has a dominant class, and that usually is the one who decides for the poor people, in favor of their own interest. Many abortions are practised by wealthier people in high level private clinics, without risks and without social or legal consequences, while the lower class citizens get abortions on dangerous places, risking their lives. This is a normal day situation in [South America's hospitals](http://www.lanacion.com.ar/1396232-las-cifras-del-aborto-clandestino-en-el-pais).
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.4. Con: This does not explain from where society derives sovereignty over an individual citizen's body. The assumed right over another individual's corpus is groundless.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.5. Pro: The state limits bodily autonomy and the actions of individuals through laws such as banning drugs, in recognition that this is best for society.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.5.1. Con: This statement works against itself. We are currently overpopulating the planet. In this light, limiting birth rate is what is best for society, and abortion works in parallel to this goal, as reflected in China's "one child" policy. Saying regulation is good for society, therefore women should not have freedom about they bodies, therefore abortion should be banned is a fallacy.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.5.1.1. Con: Overpopulation has been discussed in another branch. If this is your only measure in determining what is best for society, killing others would also work in parallel to the goal. Using overpopulation as a justification for killing is a fallacy.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.5.1.2. Con: A sustainable birth rate for a population is  2.1 children per couple. However birth rates in developed countries has dropped [well below this mark](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4255510/), as it is far more common for couples to have a single child or no children. This means any fears of over population are unfounded and abortion in no way makes up for this drop in birth rates which is attributed to societal expectations and contraception.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.5.2. Pro: Legally, you can't do anything you want to with your body. For example, prostitution, or driving naked is illegal in many places.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.6. Con: Society cannot trample the individual on a whim. It is generally recognized that the individual has specific rights that society cannot overrule without what is referred to in law as an "overriding state interest".
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.2. Pro: For an individual to be free, she must have agency. Agency requires having control over what happens to her body. Allowing women to choose whether to have an abortion or not maintains their agency, and thereby their freedom to control their own lives.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.3. Pro: The fetus cannot survive without the mother’s body nurturing it. When the law imposes this labor on a woman, it effectively enslaves her for the duration of the pregnancy. She cannot leave this responsibility. The law makes the fetus’s life more important than her liberty, instead of treating her as an moral end in herself, the law treats her body as a means to an end that she has not chosen.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.3.1. Con: It's not the law who imposes the labor, but nature. The mother had the liberty to get pregnant \(unless in cases of rape\), so she has the responsibility to develop the fetus's life.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.3.2. Con: The born baby, too, cannot survive without the mother's body nurturing it. If that argument legitimated abortion, then it should also legitimate infanticide.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4. Con: Individual liberty ends where another individual's liberties begin. As biology holds that a human life begins at conception, regardless of where one stands on the personhood or value of that life, the woman's freedom to make choices cannot supersede the liberty and rights of the human life inside her.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.1. Con: A baby's life begins at conception but its liberty begins at birth. Until then its life depends on the mother's choices just like her own life. In fact they are biologically one.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.1.1. Con: Biology does not treat them as one organism, but two [separate and distinct human organisms](https://www.kialo.com/should-women-have-the-right-to-choose-abortion-5637/5637.0=5637.1-5637.2+5637.371). While present in the mother's body, the fertilized egg is not part of the body and never becomes part of the mother's body. It travels through the fallopian tube entirely independent of the mother's nutrients until it attaches via placenta into the womb.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.1.1.1. Pro: A car traveling through a tunnel does not make it one with the tunnel, and a gasoline line does not make a car one with a gas station.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.1.1.1.1. Con: The car stays the same while it travels through the tunnel, and it is able to function as a car inside and outside the tunnel. This is not a good analogy of the fetus-mother relationship, as the fetus is constantly developing inside the mother's body, and it is not capable of functioning independently before it is born \(and, in fact, for a long time after\).
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.1.1.2. Pro: The unborn human has its [DNA set from conception](https://www.babycenter.com/2_inside-pregnancy-your-babys-dna_10354440.bc). While similar to the mother's and father's due to inherited chromosomes and genetic traits, the DNA is not the same as the mother's.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.1.2. Con: Even after birth, the baby is still dependant on the mother. It is even more dependant because no longer feeds by itself from the mother's nutrients as it did during pregnancy.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.2. Con: Modern society could not sustain a position of individual liberty before birth. These individuals would need to be identified \(i.e. Social Security numbers\) and provided with the rights and applicable services of other born individuals.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.3. Con: Choosing to cease bodily support of any individual inside or outside a womb does not supercede that individuals liberty or rights. If a dying man needs my kidney to survive, I am not violating his liberty or rights by choosing to not to donate it to him. By the same standard if a fetus requires my bodily support to live I am not violating it's liberty or rights by withholding that support. Thus this argument has no bearing on the conversation.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.3.1. Con: Failure to donate one of your kidneys that might potentially save a dying life is not analogous to deliberately terminating the life of a healthy, developing human.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.3.2. Con: Abortion is not 'withholding support.' It is deliberately killing another human life. While that might have a side effect of that human no longer using the mother's resources, abortion is not equivalent to withholding resources. The child doesn't die from the mother withholding support; he dies by pill, saline, dismemberment, or some other method.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.3.3. Con: If you connect someone to a machine that they cannot disconnect from for a time without dying, that doesn't confer a moral right to then disconnect the person just because it was your machine.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.4. Con: If a woman does not consent to the presence of the fetus inside her body, it is trespassing in a place where it has no right to be. The woman can revoke consent and evict the trespasser without infringing on it's right to life or liberty.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.4.1. Con: A trespasser is someone who comes into an area that they have no claim to from the outside without permission. Someone who is placed into an area without their explicit permission is not a trespasser. And as the natural reproductive process has the new human life implant into the mother's womb, it can't be said that the new human has no natural right to be there.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.5. Pro: Someone cannot choose to use his or her hand to kill or steal from another without consequence.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.6. Pro: When women make that choice they decide both over their own body and over the baby's body. Yes, the woman has a right to bodily autonomy - but so should the baby.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.6.1. Con: Everyone has the right to bodily autonomy "at some point". [Autonomy](http://Autonomy is defined as "freedom from external control or influence") is defined as "freedom from external control or influence". Minors, for example, typically would not have bodily autonomy until they reach some arbitrary age of maturity. It is the parents that essentially decide what goes on and in a child's body until a certain age. In most cases, children cannot refuse medical treatment because it is deemed that they lack the competency to make those decisions, even if it is their own body.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.6.2. Con: It would be quite a stretch to say that an unborn fetus is autonomous simply due the fact that it cannot sustain itself without the mother. Autonomy means free from external control. A fetus born at [23 weeks has a 25% of life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fetal_viability), and has to rely on the mother for at least that long. Even thereafter, the fetus still cannot sustain life without the assistance of others.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.7. Pro: In the [~87% of cases](https://www.guttmacher.org/sites/default/files/pdfs/pubs/psrh/full/3711005.pdf) where rape \(1%\) and maternal health \(12%\) were not cited as reasons for the abortion, bodily autonomy of the mother does not usurp bodily autonomy of the fetus.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.5. Con: The individual begins at conception. From that point on it is a seperate organism with it's own unique DNA. By your own logic as well as mine it should have sovereignty.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.3. Pro: The [first human right](http://www.un.org/en/universal-declaration-human-rights/) says: "All human beings are born free and equal in dignity and rights." Therefore women are free to choose, should be treated with dignity, and have the right to decide regarding their own bodies.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.3.1. Con: The terminology used is chosen by humans and does not change the inalienable truth that one human being is hosting another human being, that is being pregnant. There are two bodies, not one. One is helping the other until it can help itself. The helpless human being needs to be treated with dignity also.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.3.2. Pro: As a fetus is not a human being by the UN or biological standards and a pregnant woman is, it is only logical her rights to freedom of choice and life are protected, as an unwanted pregnancy can very much destroy not one but two lifes.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.3.3. Con: Appealing to authority isn't an argument but a fallacy.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4. Pro: Decisions which largely impact on an individual and their body should ultimately be made by that individual rather than by the state.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.1. Pro: To move the right to determine one's fate from the individual to the state, even in the case of saving another's life, accepts the possibility of forced abortions, forced organ donations, and other horrors. The individual must be able to choose their own fate.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.1.1. Con: The state proscribes the boundaries within self determination can operate to be those that do not harm others.  Those boundaries are the limits of the right to determine ones fate but do not move the right to the state, but protect others who might be affected by our choices.  I can buy an axe but I cannot legally wield it at another.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.2. Pro: Women should be able to judge for themselves what the best option is. Abortion could either be a painful or a liberating action. In both cases a huge emotional cost is involved, thus the right should be granted. It's not an easy way out, but rather the easiest in some cases.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.2.1. Con: The personal cost of alternative courses of action do not make them meritorious. The certainty of grave harm to another individual is a more relevant factor in limiting freedom of choice than costs to the chooser.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.3. Pro: The boundary of the law must stop at the skin. If the law does not respect a hard objective boundary then it is limited only by the political goals of the power elite who makes them. Legislators would be free to control what you may or may not want to do with your body: immunizations, tattoos, dietary restrictions, sexual preferences, drug usage \(or abstinence\), surgical procedures and more. If you want to be free then you must extend that right to others.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.3.1. Con: The higher principle is 'my liberty ends where yours begins'. The law can stop at the skin only provided to do so does not affect the liberty of another person.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.4. Con: Decisions regarding major surgery generally involve more than just someone wanting the surgery. Someone with body integrity disorder couldn't just walk in and ask a leg to be lopped off, for example. The doctor's opinion, insurance, and even the regulation of the state are all factors - not just the individual's opinion.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.4.1. Con: In many instance individuals are able to decide to have plastic surgery, and as long as a doctor deems the procedure safe, would perform the surgery if requested.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.4.2. Con: The doctor's opinion can matter while still allowing the decision to be largely in the hand of the individual. Doctor's often do still have to sign off on abortions being performed and will provide the individual with all the information prior to the procedure.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.4.2.1. Con: Doctors do not always give full information to a patient, or do so with enough time for the mother to make an informed decision.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.4.2.1.1. Pro: Many pro-choice organizations such as Planned Parenthood fight laws which would make it mandatory for Doctors to fully inform the patient of risks and options before an abortion procedure with enough time allowed for the patient to make an informed decision.
[thehill.com](http://thehill.com/policy/healthcare/354899-aclu-planned-parenthood-sue-missouri-over-new-abortion-law)
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.4.2.1.2. Pro: Some states allow or are seeking to allow doctors to withhold information on the health of the fetus if they believe it will increase the mother's chances of aborting.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.5. Con: If decisions which largely impact the individual and his/her body shouldn't ethically be made by the state, then the state shouldn't ethically be able to give one individual the right to terminate a different individual who did not grant consent.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.5.1. Con: There are two conflicting rights here: the right of a fetus to be carried to term, and the right of a person to their bodily autonomy. This argument puts one forth as a right, and simply doesn't mention the other. For it to be a valid argument, it would be necessary to state why the conflict is resolved in favor of the fetus and not the mother.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.6. Pro: The state allows me to choose whether to protect life in many situations. I am not required to donate blood, although lives are at stake. I am not required to put my life at risk to protect my own child, after that child is born. There is no general principle of which the state's assertion of control over a woman's body is a specific example. Therefore, regardless of the moral status of the act of abortion, there is no basis for the state restricting it.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.6.1. Con: The state does have power to prevent actions that harm others, rather than as you argue compelling actions to prevent harm. The two are not the same.  The law cannot compel me to jump in and save a drowning man, but it can intervene if I take actions to drown him.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.4.6.2. Con: You are not required to put your life at risk to protect your child but you are required by law to take care of it. Your argument supports the case for abortion where there is a high likelihood of death to the mother, but does not support a general right to choose abortion.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.5. Con: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.6. Con: Autonomy does not free one from consequences. I have the bodily autonomy to buy a dog, or not to buy a dog, but that does not free me from the responsibility of caring for a dog which I buy. Women have autonomy in choosing to have sex. They do not have autonomy in choosing not to deal with the consequences.
1.2.5.4.1.7.12.7. Con: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.
1.2.5.4.1.7.13. Con: Women have an obligation to provide due care for the unborn human since they \(and the father\) created the unborn human's biological dependence on the mother's body.
1.2.5.4.1.7.13.1. Pro: Many states punish pregnant mothers who deliberately pursue activities, such as illegal drug use, that they know will cause injury or disability to the unborn. [These laws](https://www.acog.org/Clinical-Guidance-and-Publications/Committee_Opinions/Committee_on_Health_Care_for_Underserved_Women/Substance_Abuse_Reporting_and_Pregnancy_The_Role_of-the-Obstetrician-Gynecologist) are based on the premise that the life of the child matters and mothers have an obligation to care for the unborn. Given this is the case, it seems principally consist to insist that women do not have a right to choose abortion, since this would also harm the life of the unborn child.
1.2.5.4.1.7.13.2. Con: Asserting that a woman holds a duty of care invites the question: if the duty of care is violated, what is the injury? If I negligently leave water on the floor, but no one is hurt, I have not committed a tort. The fetus lacks any of the qualities we would consider when asking what makes life valuable. Therefore it has lost nothing of value through its abortion, rendering irrelevant any breach of the duty of care the woman may have committed.
1.2.5.4.1.7.13.3. Con: Many times the creation of the fetus was no more intended by the mother than by the fetus. Without intent to enter it a contract is typically considered void.
1.2.5.4.1.7.13.3.1. Con: -> See 1.2.2.1.2.9.
1.2.5.4.1.7.13.3.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.
1.2.5.4.1.7.14. Pro: Women have a legal claim to a right to abortion.
1.2.5.4.1.7.14.1. Pro: Banning abortion betrays the role of government as preserving liberty as stated in [the Declaration of Independence](http://www.ushistory.org/declaration/document/).
1.2.5.4.1.7.14.2. Pro: To preserve bodily autonomy for men in all cases, and not women in all cases, is a violation of the [Equal Protection Clause](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equal_Protection_Clause) of the 14th amendment.
1.2.5.4.1.7.14.2.1. Con: There is a key difference in the case of abortion, in that a women is not acting only upon her body, but also upon a body of another human being by killing them.
1.2.5.4.1.7.14.2.2. Pro: Women should have full agency just as men have. To suggest that women “not be allowed” to do something infers that women are somehow unable to make choices. That inference is demonstrably false.
1.2.5.4.1.7.14.2.3. Con: This argument would only be valid if both men and women could get pregnant and men were allowed abortions while women were denied the same.
1.2.5.4.1.7.14.3. Pro: Individual freedom is the basis of the [US constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution). Freedom of speech, religion, from self incrimination, and unlawful searches are all guaranteed. There is no right more fundamental then the choices we make about our own bodies. If we do not have that right, then none of the others matter. By allowing a woman to choose, you are not condoning the action, you are only ensuring that you will have the right to make your own choices.
1.2.5.4.1.7.14.3.1. Con: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.
1.2.5.4.1.7.14.3.2. Con: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.5.2.
1.2.5.4.1.7.14.3.3. Pro: In Roe v. Wade the Supreme Court literally decided that [bodily autonomy was an unenumerated right](https://chicagounbound.uchicago.edu/cgi/viewcontent.cgi?referer=https://www.google.com/&httpsredir=1&article=4757&context=uclrev)that could be inferred from privacy protections in the constitution.
1.2.5.4.1.7.14.4. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.6.1.
1.2.5.4.1.7.14.5. Con: The legal right to "Bodily Autonomy" descends from [McFall v. Schimp,](http://www.ucs.louisiana.edu/~ras2777/judpol/mcfall.html) which established the precedent that the state could not violate one person's liberty by compelling them to perform medical procedures, even in order to save the life of another.  While this is frequently used to support abortion, this is faulty, as pregnancy is not caused by the state, and the only medical procedure is abortion, which violates a fetus's life and liberty for the benefit of the mother.
1.2.5.4.1.7.14.5.1. Con: Control over one's own body is "bodily autonomy".  Whether the state requires or denies the choices of an individual with what to do with their own body it is interference with bodily autonomy.
1.2.5.4.1.7.14.6. Con: Appeal to authority isn't an argument but a fallacy.
1.2.5.4.1.7.15. Con: This argument is self-refuting because abortion denies the same autonomy to the unborn human being.
1.2.5.4.1.7.15.1. Con: The exercise of autonomy requires a will. A woman seeking an abortion has the will and intention to free herself of an unwanted pregnancy. The government preventing her from obtaining an abortion is therefore an infringement on her autonomy. A fetus has a biological directive to continue growing and eventually become a human, but it lacks the conscious thought required to possess the will or intention necessary for the abortion to be a denial of its autonomy.
1.2.5.4.1.7.16. Pro: The only reliable basis we have on which to consider this issue is in relation to a woman's right to bodily autonomy.
1.2.5.4.1.7.16.1. Pro: We lack the necessary philosophical understanding to determine conclusively when sentience begins in a meaningful way.
1.2.5.4.1.7.17. Con: The voluntary taking of human life is considered in most societies to be murder \(except in circumstances of war or punishment\) therefore a woman isn't justified in killing a child just because the child is in and could be considered to be part of her body.
1.2.5.4.1.7.17.1. Con: "Taking" is an important word here. Murder is evil because it is taking life away from someone who wishes to remain alive. A fetus is unconscious. It has no conception of life, living, or the self. Anything that makes life valuable - that makes the deprivation of life evil - is absent from the fetus. Therefore nothing real has been taken from an aborted fetus.
1.2.5.4.1.7.18. Pro: If women were denied the right to bodily autonomy based on the perceived needs of others \(fetuses\), then any healthy individual in society could potentially have their body used for other people's well-being. If a woman's body is not her own, then nobody's body is their own. Such a society would be deeply unpleasant.
1.2.5.4.1.7.18.1. Con: The mother/fetus relationship in an abortion is unique to most other intra-personal relationships in that the mother is the one trying to infringe on the fetus's bodily autonomy. A person who infringes on another's bodily autonomy necessarily forfeits their own.
1.2.5.4.1.7.19. Con: No person is wholly their own and no act exists inside a bubble. Suicide is considered a selfish act because it impacts those who associate with the suicidal person. To terminate the growth of what will become an independent person is a decision that impacts many more people than just the mother. It is therefore not an independent act and society has the right to coin in their objections of the practice.
1.2.5.4.1.7.19.1. Con: The other people who could possibly be impacted by the potential person have a mere expectancy interest - there is a chance that they may be impacted by the existence or absence of the expected person, but it is not guaranteed that such an impact will exist \(let alone that it is a positive impact!\). By contrast, the woman has an actual, present interest in her bodily autonomy; the woman's actual interest should therefore outweigh any expectancy interests that may exist.
1.2.5.4.1.7.20. Pro: If the government is given the power to tell women they have to give birth, the next logical step is that the government will have the authority to tell us we can’t have children or another scenario where the government tells us when to have our children and how many children we can or cannot have. The government has no place in a woman’s vagina.
1.2.5.4.1.7.20.1. Con: This argument would be valid if the woman were forced to get pregnant and provide children to the State. Government does not have this authority; it has solely the responsability for protecting a resistless life.
1.2.5.4.1.7.21. Con: Bodily autonomy is an arbitrary and protean concept. There is no justification possible for ''rights''.
1.2.5.4.1.7.21.1. Con: Rights are easily justifiable through utilitarianism: recognizing the right to bodily autonomy creates something the law and its enforcers must protect. One of the most basic protections would be against battery, which causes suffering. Thus, suffering is reduced by recognizing bodily autonomy.
1.2.5.4.1.7.21.2. Con: Subjective concepts exist within a social context and claiming that they don't exist doesn't add anything meaningful to the discussion.
1.2.5.4.1.7.22. Pro: The laws have to organise life and interactions between the citizens, but it's not supposed to control your personal life. If a woman doesn't want to be a mother, she won't, and it's her own and only business. Finally, a woman has no right to decide for other women.
1.2.5.4.1.7.23. Con: Bodily autonomy is not an unlimited or absolute right.
1.2.5.4.1.7.23.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.
1.2.5.4.1.7.23.2. Pro: This would also mean all women must be granted the legal right to suicide. They must also have the right to have the suicide process be medically accessible, with the only basis or reason for requesting the suicide being 'it is my body, I have the right to bodily autonomy, so I can do with my body as I wish'.
1.2.5.4.1.7.23.2.1. Con: The majority of Americans [support access to euthanasia](https://news.gallup.com/poll/211928/majority-americans-remain-supportive-euthanasia.aspx), which essentially does grant people control over their bodies to the extent that they can have support in ending their lives. It is possible bodily autonomy should be extended to allow this.
1.2.5.4.1.7.23.2.1.1. Con: Physician Assisted Suicide \(PAS\) is still illegal in nearly all states. Regardless, a core tenet of ethical arguments to allow PAS to be legalised always have 'motivation' as a primary consideration. Generally, the motivation must include a physician's diagnosis of a terminal illness, and with [six months or less to live](https://euthanasia.procon.org/view.resource.php?resourceID=000132). Furthermore, with abortion the woman is making a decision over someone else's life and not just her own, this is not the case with PAS.
1.2.5.4.1.7.23.3. Con: Even if bodily autonomy is not a right which is unlimited or absolute, it can only be limited, restricted, or infringed upon for an extremely compelling purpose \(other than what the given law says must happen\) using means very narrowly tailored to achieving that purpose. That test cannot be met by an abortion ban.
1.2.5.4.1.7.24. Pro: Giving women autonomy over her body via reproductive rights is the only known [universal](https://www.unfpa.org/press/ensuring-reproductive-health-and-rights-would-go-long-way-overcoming-poverty-new-report-says)[cure](https://www.ippf.org/news/announcements/sexual-and-reproductive-health-and-rights-are-crucial-ending-poverty) for [poverty](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2775139/).
1.2.5.4.1.7.25. Pro: We do not give people the right to use other's people's body to use or sustain them without express and ongoing consent. If women want to remove that consent, they should be able to do so by having an abortion.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.1. Con: The geographical overlap of woman and child is unfortunate but not determinative of the moral issues involved in terminating the life of a preborn baby. Consent only applies here if one can show that enveloping another being's body creates a cessation of rights for anything enveloped. If one cannot show such a cessation of rights, ongoing consent here is meaningless for this discussion.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.2. Con: The mother's body created the egg inside the ovary. The mother's body ejected the egg from the ovary into the fallopian tubes. The father's sperm attached to the egg. The egg was fertilized by the mother's egg and father's sperm at some point in the fallopian tubes. At no point in this did the egg, sperm, or newly formed human life do anything to the mother's body without her consent as they were reactive parties to the natural biologic functions and actions of both parents.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3. Pro: A fetus's right to life does not imply the right to use the mother's body to sustain its life.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.1. Pro: People do not have a right to use another's body in order to remain alive. For example, we do not require people to donate their organs even though doing so could prevent deaths.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.1.1. Pro: If my brother requires daily blood transfusions to live I have no legal or moral obligation to give them my blood. It is the same if my fetus requires daily bodily support to live: I have no legal or moral obligation to give my bodily support.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.1.1.1. Con: The situations are not functionally equivalent as the mother's body naturally sends nutrients regardless of her intellectual or legal consent, whereas doctors will only remove blood by written consent. One is a naturally occurring process, whereas the other is artificial.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.1.1.2. Con: These scenarios are not functionally or ethically equivalent, as your brother would not be dependent on your blood due to your own actions, but rather due to natural disease or some other outside factor.
