1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.1.1.3. Con: The scenarios are not ethically equivalent, as the law does not give someone legal permission to stop someone's IV or prohibit someone from receiving nutrients. The law also does not give permission to kill your brother so he cannot receive any blood from you in the future. There is a large difference between not donating something that is yours and terminating someone so they cannot receive anything of yours.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.2. Con: You always have a duty to someone you have placed in a precarious situation.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.2.1. Con: This makes two assumptions that aren't safe. One is that the mother has placed the fetus in this position. There are many reasons she might not have. The other is that, if she does have an obligation to the fetus, that obligation extends to risking her life for the fetus as well as serving as the fetus's entire life support system for the length of the pregnancy, not providing life support but being the human life support. It's unclear whether, if obligations exist, they extend this far.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.3. Con: The mother's body naturally provides nutrients and is designed for the housing and development of the prenatal human life. The process is automatic. It is not ethically wrong for the fetus to accept the nutrients the mother's body naturally offers.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.4. Con: Someone existing in an environment and taking nutrients at someone else's instigation for a predetermined period of time does give them an implied right to continue to do so barring breach of law or contract; the man in the iron lung at the hospital, the tenant at a bed and breakfast, the patron at a restaurant, the child learning from his teacher, the sick woman with a walking IV, etc.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.5. Pro: In Judith Jarvis Thomson's famous [violinist example](http://spot.colorado.edu/~heathwoo/Phil160,Fall02/thomson.htm), she argues that people would be outraged if upon waking up they found themselves plugged to an ailing violinist and told that in order for the violinist to remain alive, they must remain plugged to them for the next nine months.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.5.1. Con: No outside person or force is forcibly plugging the mother to another human.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.5.2. Con: Even if someone was horrifically kidnapped and attached to an ailing violinist, it would not justify murder of the other victim vs. outrage at the kidnapper.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.5.3. Con: The human life inside the mother is growing, not ailing. It would be ailing if killed or removed prematurely.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.5.3.1. Con: Ailing is not the relevant part of the analogy.  Dependency is the relevant part.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.5.4. Con: The violinist example is not analogous because withdrawing support is very different from directly killing and the kidnapped person didn't create the violinists dependency on their body whereas the biological parents make the unborn human biologically dependent on the mother's body thereby creating an obligation to provide due care.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.5.4.1. Con: There are two assumptions here- first: that withdrawing support is different from direct killing. This distinction is unclear at best, since both cases involve a decision \(terminate life\) causally connected to a consequence \(termination of life\). Second: that biological parents choose to create life, which confers obligations. This is also unclear; many pregnancies are accidental, and even if they weren't, you should be allowed to change your mind after experiencing the realities of pregnancy.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.5.4.2. Con: The mother did not take someone independent from her body and make that person dependent on her body. She brought someone into existence as a person dependent on her body. If you take someone who was independent on you and make them dependent on you, then you'd be responsible for them, as you deprived them of their independence. But when it's not your fault that they're dependent, since they would be non-existent, not-independent, if it weren't for you, you don't have the same responsibility.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.4. Pro: For this reason, even if a fetus has rights, they do not extend to being able to demand somebody else sustain their life, as this is not a right we award to anyone.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.4.1. Con: It is a right we often afford in cases where initial consent or action implies continued consent for a reasonable time period.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.4.1.1. Pro: A man with a sign posted on his private land allowing cars to travel over a private bridge cannot suddenly blow up the bridge with cars on it as he 'removed consent.'
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.4.1.2. Pro: A person renting out a property cannot evict a tenant suddenly and without reason, since the initial lease determined the period of mutual consent so long as both parties follow the terms.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.4.1.3. Pro: A sick person in the hospital cannot be removed from life-support and ejected from the hospital if the doctor doesn't want to continue treating him.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.4.1.4. Pro: A college can't expel a student for the sole reason that it no longer consents to teach the student.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.4.1.5. Pro: A bus driver cannot kick everyone off the bus solely because he doesn't consent to drive them.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.4.1.6. Con: However we also accept that assuming consent is ongoing can be problematic, particularly when it is directly related to the use of another's body, such as in the case of sexual relationships. In these instances we allow consent to be removed.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.4.2. Con: The child is completely independent of the mother's resources to sustain life as it travels down the fallopian tubes. It would not make sense for the new human life to have rights due to independence but then lose them due to later taking nutrients.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.4.3. Con: The mother's body naturally sends nutrients to the fetus. That she might not consciously approve of this doesn't mean the fetus is violating her rights by [accepting the nutrients offered](https://www.kialo.com/argument/5637.335).
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.4.4. Con: The fetus accepting offered nutrients is not [demanding](http://an insistent and peremptory request, made as if by right. "a series of demands for far-reaching reforms" synonyms:	request, call, command, order, dictate, ultimatum, stipulation "I gave in to her demands" verb 1. ask authoritatively or brusquely. "“Where is she?” he demanded" synonyms:	order, command, enjoin, urge; More) anything, nor using force against the mother.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.4.5. Con: The mother receives benefits from the fetus, [such as stem cells to repair heart disease](https://www.newscientist.com/article/dn21185-fetus-donates-stem-cells-to-heal-mothers-heart/). No one would argue that the mother is demanding such benefits without consent from the fetus and that the fetus has the right to kill her because her life might depend on it.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.4.5.1. Con: No one would argue this case because they are not the same comparatively. The fetus definitively has no chance at life without the mother. In your example, the mother's life is not wholly dependent upon potential benefit of the stem cells. The outcomes are drastically different.
1.2.5.4.1.7.25.5. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.5.
1.2.5.4.1.7.26. Pro: It is not anyone's place to decide when a woman should start a family or not. It is the sole responsibility of the woman to make that decision. Just like it is not anyone's place to decide when a man should start a family. It's not a democratic or public decision, it is a personal and private decision.
1.2.5.4.1.7.26.1. Con: In cases where a male partner wants an abortion and a woman doesn't, women decide when men will start a family all the time. Since adoption is an option, it isn't valid to equate a baby to 'creating a family'.
1.2.5.4.1.7.26.2. Con: Giving birth to a child doesn't necessarily equal starting a family.
1.2.5.4.1.7.26.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.
1.2.5.4.1.7.26.3. Con: We are often given trials we are not ready for or want but we adjust and often when we look back we would not have it any other way.
1.2.5.4.1.7.26.4. Pro: The most significant portion of the time; emotional, physical, devotional and mental will be allocated by the woman, regardless of the intent of the man. Why is it feasible to deprive a woman of her voice to declare her readiness to change her whole life? Yes, certainly, obstacles crop up for everybody, no matter your privilege or position but within the possibility of the field of choice, why should this instance be forbidden to a woman. Choice is paramount.
1.2.5.4.1.7.27. Pro: Forced pregnancy, or denial of abortion rights, is an inherently sexist and discriminatory practice, since there is no other instance in a parent's life in which they are forced to  provide bodily resources \(i.e. blood, organs, bone marrow\) to serve their child. \([Cook, Dickens, and Bliss, p. 583](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC1508897/pdf/amjph00004-0113.pdf)\)
1.2.5.4.1.7.27.1. Con: If an infant required blood and you denied the child access to your own, society has supported the creation of blood blanks to provide what the parent cannot. The age of your child should not dictate it's worthiness to access the most basic of medical needs via blood.   During pregnancy a mother's blood supply increases, so she is not sharing a pre-pregnancy supply of blood. She had created enough for two.
1.2.5.4.1.7.27.2. Con: Forced pregnancy is not the same as denial of abortion. It presupposes that intercourse was not consensual. For instance, there is no instance in which someone is forced to break a leg, and doing so is assault and ilegal, but if you decide to practice extreme sports then you implicitly comply to the risk of breaking your leg, not ilegal.
1.2.5.4.1.7.27.3. Con: This argument relies upon a false premise which compares every single other instance in which a parent may be requested to provide bodily resources and finds them to be equivalent. Refusing to donate blood to a child who needs it is not tantamount to causing the injury which lead to the exsanguination. The supposedly "forced" provision of resources and murder are not mutually exclusive in any other case.  Motherhood is scientifically, ethically, morally, and legally unique.
1.2.5.4.1.7.27.4. Con: No manner of pro-life thinking can be sexist because we can't treat pregnant men differently from pregnant women \(because they don't exist\).
1.2.5.4.1.7.27.5. Con: Abortion is not a "right" because it had to be invented, and is therefore not innate. There is no grounds on which to designate abortion as a right.
1.2.5.4.1.8. Pro: It is more, or at least equally unethical to raise a child without the proper resources or place them in the poorly managed foster care system, forcing them to live a life of hardship and suffering.
1.2.5.4.1.8.1. Pro: In an American court of law, someone who must endure suffering is weighted heavier than someone deceased. This is because we as humans understand that continued suffering is inhumane, whereas we assume that after death there is no feeling. Even in Christian thought, someone who is completely innocent of their concept of god still gets to go to heaven, therefore is no longer in pain. This is why we put animals to sleep when they are in pain.
1.2.5.4.1.8.1.1. Con: While some Christians believe that someone who never heard of God or who dies before a specific age goes to heaven, that is not a staple belief of Christianity. The Bible simply says those with faith are forgiven and resurrected, but those who do not have faith remain under condemnation. While the belief of individuals vary, there is no 'guarantee' in Christianity that aborted children all are resurrected to live in the new heavens and earth.
1.2.5.4.1.8.1.2. Con: That consideration in the law is made in comparison post-death with someone who has already died vs. someone still living, not as an ethical determination as to whether or not someone should be killed to escape future potential suffering.
1.2.5.4.1.8.1.3. Con: The unborn child is generally not in pain, nor wounded, nor dying slowly, so cannot be compared to putting an animal out of its misery.
1.2.5.4.1.8.2. Con: It is not more \(or even equally\) unethical to let someone suffer rather than killing them. If that were true, then we ought to kill all people in poverty or with disabilities.
1.2.5.4.1.8.3. Con: You should not assume a life of hardship is not worth living.
1.2.5.4.1.8.4. Con: A life of suffering often brings a life that is sensitive, creative, and aspiring. Just because a child may struggle because of a parent's decisions doesn't mean his life or lack of should be bound by them.
[ranker.com](https://www.ranker.com/list/celebrities-who-grew-up-in-foster-care/celebrity-lists)
1.2.5.4.1.9. Pro: It is wrong to bring an unwanted child into the world. Even if the child is put into foster care, they may not find a family who wants them or may grow up feeling abandoned by their parents.
1.2.5.4.1.9.1. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.
1.2.5.4.1.9.2. Con: There is no objective basis or any evidence provided for this claim. In the same way, one could say it is wrong to let an unwanted newborn live, or an unwanted elderly person live, or a person with a mental disability live. This claim places subjective value on human life that would apply to all human life if taken to its logical conclusion.
1.2.5.4.1.9.2.1. Con: Killing a person \(newborn, elderly person, disabled person\) harms them. If a fetus is not considered a person \(which is debated elsewhere\), then killing a fetus before it becomes sentient does not harm a person and is solely a matter of whether a potential person lives or does not live. There is thus a fundamental difference between debating whether a fetus should be born and debating whether a person should continue living.
1.2.5.4.1.10. Pro: A child's right to be wanted should take precedence over its right to live. A child should have a right to a certain quality of life, not merely a right to exist. Denying this to a child dehumanizes it, making it no longer a creature worthy of love and nurture but merely a creature worthy of existence.
1.2.5.4.1.10.1. Con: Using the word "should" presupposes an objective standard, yet allows for a subjective standard for "quality of life." Who determines what is a sufficient quality of life? Couldn't that be said for any human who doesn't meet a subjective standard for quality of life? The poor, the criminals, the elderly, all could fall into this category of having a less than sufficient quality of life. The only objective standard we have is the inherent value given to all humans based solely on their humanity.
1.2.5.4.1.10.2. Con: Even supposing that a child has a right to be wanted and even a right to a certain quality of life, such a right would not require a particular person \(its birth-mother\) be that person who wants it or provides that quality of life. Many childless couples, and those with children, are both able and willing to take such children and provide such things. Furthermore, if such rights did supercede the child's right to life and therefore justify abortion, they would also justify infanticide.
1.2.5.4.1.11. Con: -> See 1.2.2.1.2.10.
1.2.5.4.1.12. Con: Societies in general do not allow a mother to [neglect an unwanted child once born](http://criminal.findlaw.com/criminal-charges/child-neglect.html), nor do they generally allow her to [murder the child](https://www.theguardian.com/uk-news/2017/jul/27/mother-who-murdered-two-year-old-daughter-jailed-for-16-years). Most societies throughout time have considered these crimes. With ethical practice primarily against it, there cannot be claimed a fundamental moral principle that killing an unwanted child is moral, or that not allowing the mother to stop caring for her child, while the child is under her guardianship, is immoral.
1.2.5.4.1.12.1. Con: The alternative to caring for an unwanted child is disowning the child, not killing them or neglecting them. Ethical practice is not primarily against disowning a child.
1.2.5.4.1.13. Con: Abortion has the goal of ending the child's life. This would, not just could, harm the child in all cases. Even in the rare case of a child surviving, the child is harmed.
1.2.5.4.1.13.1. Con: The "child" would not be harmed by being terminated because it is not, and would never be, capable of having experiences and categorizing them as good or bad, which is a requirement for meaningfully designating something as harmful.
1.2.5.4.1.13.1.1. Con: There are many mentally ill people who are incapable of categorizing their experiences as good or bad, yet society would still judge their assault or murder to be harmful.
1.2.5.4.1.13.1.1.1. Con: Anyone who experiences pleasure, pain, or any emotion is categorizing their experience as good or bad. Anyone who has desires, goals, or fears is categorizing their potential future experiences as good or bad. There are few, if any, people who are incapable of all of those things.
1.2.5.4.1.13.1.2. Con: The [legal definition of harm](http://dictionary.law.com/Default.aspx?selected=964) does not include verbiage about someone's ability to categorize or evaluate experiences.
1.2.5.4.1.13.1.2.1. Con: The legal definition of harm was written for legal purposes and is inadequate for philosophical purposes.
1.2.5.4.1.13.1.2.1.1. Pro: The legal definition of harm includes harm to corporations, which are legal persons. If you agree legal harm to corporations is not morally equivalent to harming a person, then you agree something being legal harm does not make it actual harm.
1.2.5.4.1.13.1.2.1.2. Pro: Since fetuses are generally not considered legal persons, there is no need for the law to define the philosophical nature of harm in order to include or exclude the possibility of harming fetuses. Thus, whether it is interpreted as including or excluding that possibility is incidental.
1.2.5.4.1.13.1.3. Con: The child would be capable of having experiences and categorizing them if left alone to birth naturally. Interfering in that natural process to keep the child from ever experiencing the outside world would be a harm in the form of robbing the child of natural development which would otherwise lead to new experiences.
1.2.5.4.1.13.1.3.1. Con: The fetus is indifferent to whether or not it becomes a child which has new experiences, and thus is not harmed. It may be better to create another child who will experience the world than not to do so, and the fact that it will naturally happen if left alone may be relevant, but that is not the same as claiming that the fetus in particular is being harmed by not becoming a child with experiences.
1.2.5.4.1.13.1.3.1.1. Con: A fetus [as young as eight weeks](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2900087/) reflexively pulls away from painful stimuli. This is why anasthesia is given to humans in the fetal stage. An indifferent response would be no reaction at all.
1.2.5.5. Con: The argument that the mother does not own the fetuses life really comes down to what we are using as a definition of life. While in the womb, the fetus is a parasitic being, it cannot live on its own. Once the fetus is born the parasitic bond is broken and life begins. So during pregnancy Mom had the rights, if fetus is born it too has earned rights. The definition of life is also going to vary from one religion to another and in the US you cant force your religion on other people.
1.2.6. Con: All women are equipped to bring a baby into the world, after all they have been doing it since the Stone Age. Today is just a matter of numbers, time, perhaps career, but this is no excuse. There are initiatives such as child care to help low-income mothers. Quality time is not in time itself, but in the level of involvement and there is no  profession that prevents someone from having children.
1.2.6.1. Con: While professions may not prevent women from having children, it can be more difficult for women to have successful careers in fields such as corporate law when significant time is taken out of work in order to have and raise children.
1.2.6.1.1. Con: Desire for a successful career does not redeem anyone of the responsibility they have to the child they conceived.
1.2.6.2. Con: Initiatives to help low-income mothers are not necessarily enough. It may still well be necessary for the mother to attempt to work multiple jobs and raise her family, which can cause a great deal of stress.
1.2.6.3. Con: There are numerous countries around the world that do not have sufficient social [security](http://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=36773#.Wjt9xCMwj-Y) and childcare services. Unwanted children in these countries can easily push families below the poverty line.
1.2.6.3.1. Con: Most of the countries mentioned in UN's report without efficient social security programs are agriculturally based; this is an environment in which large families are welcome. In fact, the farm lifestyle is very different, as boys and girls help the family in the daily tasks so a greater family means greater income.
1.2.6.3.1.1. Con: This is a generalisation - not everyone in these countries works in agriculture, and we should not be the ones deciding what is best for these people. It should be up to individuals and individual families to make decisions about reproduction and family size.
1.2.6.3.2. Con: A child does not reduce family income - parameter that defines the threshold- only increases expenses, but the family remains in the same stratum. The calculation uses the simple [equation](http://siteresources.worldbank.org/PGLP/Resources/povertymanual_ch4.pdf)"Gi = \(Z-Yi\) .I \(Yi \<Z\)" where Gi is the poverty gap, Z represents the poverty line and Yi is the real income for poor individuals. The gap is zero for everyone else. Children are not considered in the calculation.
1.2.6.3.2.1. Con: Even if children are not considered in the technical calculation of what it means to be below the poverty line, it does not change the fact that having a child increases costs for a family and in some cases will also require a parent to stop working, such that overall the family will be poorer.
1.2.6.4. Pro: With the proper will and sacrifices, it is possible to have a career and raise children.
1.2.6.5. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.2.3.1.
1.2.6.6. Con: There are not enough initiatives for low income parents to have access to quality childcare. There is not universal access to quality affordable childcare.
1.2.6.7. Con: Statements like this make it seem like a woman's only purpose is childbearing, and her only 'natural' state is a mother, not a person. Women are not brood mares, and economic position, health and other variables do have a say in an important decision like pregnancy.
1.2.7. Pro: Bringing a child to life has consequences not only restricted to the moment of birth but for the rest of the mother's life and for all the people around them.
1.2.7.1. Con: Unless those consequences are extremely severe they cannot plausibly serve as ample justification for killing the child.
1.2.7.1.1. Con: A woman should, at the very beginning, have the right to evaluate whether she wants to or is able to deal with the long term consequences of raising a child. If she decides to keep the fetus it means that she has accepted responsibility, at least to a certain extent. Killing the resulting child therefore would not be the same as getting an early stage abortion.
1.2.7.1.1.1. Con: -> See 1.2.2.1.2.9.
1.2.7.2. Con: A 4 year old child also can have a negative impact on a mothers life, but this doesn't mean that is a legitimate reason to kill the child.
1.2.7.2.1. Con: -> See 1.2.7.1.1.
1.2.7.2.2. Con: It can not be said that ending the life of a 4 year old, is equivalent to ending the life of an unborn child. The 4 year old child and the unborn child have very different sets of capacities \(self awareness, ability and conceptualize pain, ability to form social ties etc.\).
1.2.7.3. Pro: Pregnancy and motherhood have a substantial impact on a woman’s career.
1.2.7.3.1. Pro: Motherhood has a greater impact on a woman’s career prospects than her level of education, according to a [study](https://www.youngwomenstrust.org/assets/0000/5376/Young__Female_and_Forgotten_Short_Report.pdf) by the Young Women’s Trust. Women with a dependent child are six times more likely to be economically inactive than those without children. In contrast, having children does not impact on whether or not men are in work.
1.2.7.3.2. Pro: Once women return to work after giving birth, many women face a "[motherhood wage penalty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motherhood_penalty),” especially at the bottom of the income spectrum. This means that working mothers encounter systematic disadvantages in pay, perceived competence, and benefits relative to childless women \([pg.14](http://content.thirdway.org/publications/853/NEXT_-_Fatherhood_Motherhood.pdf)\).
1.2.7.3.2.1. Pro: Many women spend time at home caring for children, and thus interrupt their job experience, or at least full-time job experience, which can lead to lower wages. Both childbearing and child-rearing detract from the time that could be spent developing job skills, furthering education, or gaining experience in the workforce. \([Human capital theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motherhood_penalty#Human_capital_theory)\)
1.2.7.3.2.2. Pro: Mothers may trade higher wages for “mother-friendly” jobs that are easier to combine with parenting.
1.2.7.3.2.2.1. Con: This is not always possible. Single women, or couples in which the woman is the breadwinner, tend rely on this higher income, especially if it is needed to support a family.
1.2.7.3.2.2.1.1. Pro: In [2014](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/women/11279824/Female-breadwinners-why-earning-more-can-poison-a-marriage.html) thirty-one per cent of British women were found to be the main financial provider in their family – a rise of 80 per cent in the past 15 years, with an increase across all age and income groups.
1.2.7.3.2.2.1.2. Pro: According to a 2013 [study](https://www.psychologytoday.com/blog/its-never-too-late/201705/can-being-female-breadwinner-cost-you-your-relationship), 40 percent of American households with children have a woman as the higher earner, and 60 percent of African-American families have a female breadwinner. Female breadwinners include single mothers and married women who earn more than their partners or husbands.
1.2.7.3.2.3. Pro: Mothers may earn less because the needs of their children leave them exhausted or distracted at work, rendering them less productive. Mothers may also be less productive at work because they are saving their energy for their “second shift” at home. \([Work-effort theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motherhood_penalty#Work-effort_theory)\)
1.2.7.3.3. Con: In no scenario should career aspirations dignify the murder of a child.
1.2.7.3.4. Con: In most Western countries there are legal measures that allow women to retain their employment status and forbid discrimination based on having children.
1.2.7.4. Pro: With the arrival of an infant, many households experience a significant [decline](http://equitablegrowth.org/working-papers/income-volatility-around-birth/) in economic well-being in the time around a birth. They face increased demands on resources, changes in the composition of income, and a potentially heightened risk of economic insecurity.
1.2.7.4.1. Pro: The drop in parents’ [income](http://equitablegrowth.org/working-papers/income-volatility-around-birth/) around childbirth can have major consequences for children as well. Inadequate family income is harmful for children—particularly young children—affecting their long-term social-emotional, cognitive, and academic outcomes \([pg.15](https://www.urban.org/sites/default/files/publication/32706/412899-The-Negative-Effects-of-Instability-on-Child-Development-A-Research-Synthesis.PDF)\).
1.2.7.4.1.1. Con: Discouraging people of low socio-economic status from having children because poverty impairs their performance in society is basically eugenics.
1.2.7.4.1.1.1. Con: Genetics do not determine socio-economic status.
1.2.7.4.2. Con: Pregnancy and the growth in household size may trigger an increase in public program eligibility and benefit levels among economically disadvantaged households.
1.2.7.4.2.1. Pro: The Special Supplemental Nutritional Program for Women, Infants and Children \([WIC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WIC)\) is a federal assistance program that provides near-cash nutritional assistance targeted at this time period. It targets low-income pregnant women, breastfeeding women, and children under the age of five.
1.2.7.4.2.2. Pro: Many major cash and near-cash safety net programs in USA including the Temporary Assistance for Needy Families \([TANF](https://www.acf.hhs.gov/ofa/programs/tanf)\) program, the Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program \([SNAP](https://www.fns.usda.gov/snap/supplemental-nutrition-assistance-program-snap)\), the Earned Income Tax Credit \([EITC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earned_income_tax_credit)\) and the Child Tax Credit \([CTC](https://www.cbpp.org/research/federal-tax/policy-basics-the-child-tax-credit)\), either restrict eligibility to households with children, or increase benefit levels when a new child is added to the assistance unit.
1.2.7.4.2.3. Con: Even in most of the developed countries, the social assistance that new mothers are entitled to is rarely sufficient on its own, especially if the mother was forced to give up her job to care for the child.
1.2.7.4.2.3.1. Pro: The amount an average single parent with two children receives in the [US](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-us-canada-37159686) is set by each state, with a 60 month lifetime limit. In Mississippi, they would receive $153 a month. In Alaska, the average benefit was $642 a month.
1.2.7.4.2.3.2. Pro: A single person with one child in Ontario, [Canada](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-us-canada-37159686) would receive a benefit of just less than $1,000 Canadian dollars a month, with no lifetime limit.
1.2.7.4.2.3.3. Pro: In [France](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-us-canada-37159686) a single parent with two children would be eligible for as much as €1,068.61 each month, but that benefit would be lessened by any actual income or other cash benefits the person was claiming.
1.2.7.4.2.3.4. Pro: In the [UK](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-us-canada-37159686), a single parent with two children could expect £292 a month. The person must have no income or low income, work less than 16 hours a week, and have savings of under £16,000.
1.2.7.5. Con: Aborting a child has consequences not only restricted to the moment of birth but for the rest of the mother's life and for all the people around them. Consider the risk of infertility, psychological damage, and social backlash.
1.2.7.5.1. Pro: Abortion has [harmful](http://www.thelifeinstitute.net/current-projects/safer-without-abortion/abortion-harms-women/) mental and physical consequences for the woman involved.
1.2.7.5.1.1. Pro: Those who choose abortions are often minors or young women with insufficient life experience to understand fully what they are doing.
1.2.7.5.1.1.1. Con: Those who have children at such young ages seriously impact their [ability to earn](https://www.businessinsider.com/why-delaying-parenthood-and-having-kids-later-is-a-big-deal-2015-6) and have a reasonable quality of life afterwards, and often lack the resources and support to raise them.
1.2.7.5.1.1.1.1. Con: While this might hold some weight in third world countries, it is a hard argument to make in countries like the U.S. where the majority are in the top 5% of the world wealth-wise, regardless of how many children they have, and even those at poverty level is usually in the top fifth of the world. Not having many extra things or having to work hard is not the same thing as not having a reasonable quality of life.
1.2.7.5.1.1.1.1.1. Con: This statement is no longer true, The States have been downgraded to a [developing country.](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/americas/us-developing-nation-regressing-economy-poverty-donald-trump-mit-economist-peter-temin-a7694726.html)
1.2.7.5.1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: That is one economist's opinion about trends he sees, not an actual credit status or official economic evaluation. His opinion is based on things like the lower class having little perceived impact on social policy and perceived 'racist' undertones, not the actual wealth level of the typical U.S. citizen.
1.2.7.5.1.1.1.1.2. Pro: This webpage has a widget that will estimate your wealth as compared to the world: [poverty.ucdavis.edu](https://poverty.ucdavis.edu/faq/what-current-poverty-rate-united-states)

1 person, no kids, making $25,000: richest 5.4%
2 children making poverty level $22,000: richest 19% 
Family of 6 with 4 children making $35,000: in the richest 17%
1 parent, 6 kids, making current median $59,000: richest 12%
2 parent, 1 kid, making $53,000: richest 5.7%
1.2.7.5.1.1.1.2. Con: There are many support groups and charities available to help new or struggling parents that lack information or resources.
1.2.7.5.1.1.1.2.1. Con: Those support groups are often religious in nature, or are government supported, which either puts a strain on our already reduced fiscal resources allocated for those services or forces a religious doctrine.
1.2.7.5.1.1.1.2.1.1. Con: The religious beliefs of an organization are irrelevant to whether or not it is available to offer aid except in the very rare case that a group is closed to non-members. A woman not wanting to take advantage of resources due to dislike of a particular religion doesn't mean the resources are not there.
1.2.7.5.1.1.1.2.1.2. Con: It is illegal in the U.S. for any group to force a religious conversion on someone. Exposure to a religious doctrine is not the same thing as forcing a religion on someone.
1.2.7.5.1.1.1.2.1.3. Con: Government support of a group that aids new mothers is not more of a financial strain than any other safety-net program that society votes for.
1.2.7.5.1.1.1.2.1.4. Con: That religious groups are often charitable in helping post-birth is a good thing, as it increases the number of support groups available. If support groups were restricted to only secular or atheist groups, there would be far less resources available for struggling mothers.
1.2.7.5.1.1.2. Con: The vast majority of abortions are women who do not fit in the minor or young woman categories.[Only about 17 percent are teens.](http://www.nbcnews.com/id/22689931/ns/health-womens_health/t/whos-getting-abortions-not-who-youd-think/#.WiDwvLaZOu4) About 60 percent have given birth to least one child prior to getting an abortion.
1.2.7.5.1.1.2.1. Con: 17% is still a significant percentage, as it is [almost 1/5 of all abortions](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4852976/table/T1/) in the U.S.
1.2.7.5.1.1.3. Con: Teenage pregnancy [increases the risk](http://www.momjunction.com/articles/effects-of-teen-pregnancy-on-society_00384725/) of spending the entire life in poverty for both the teen parents and the baby.
1.2.7.5.1.1.3.1. Con: Adoption is a good solution to this problem, and then no one has to die.
1.2.7.5.1.1.4. Con: -> See 1.2.2.5.
1.2.7.5.1.1.5. Con: The "insufficient life experience" argument could also be used to favor legalizing abortion, as minors would, given their life experience, be unable to raise a child properly.
1.2.7.5.1.1.5.1. Con: Yes, except that adoption exists, which is a viable and good alternative.
1.2.7.5.1.1.6. Pro: Teenagers getting pregnant at an early age cannot pursue their higher education due to extra responsibility.
1.2.7.5.1.1.6.1. Pro: Some teens even decide to [drop out of their high school](http://www.momjunction.com/articles/effects-of-teen-pregnancy-on-society_00384725/) and find a job to supplement themselves.
1.2.7.5.1.1.6.2. Pro: This might reduce their chances to make a career and get a high paying job.
1.2.7.5.1.1.6.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.7.5.1.1.3.
1.2.7.5.1.1.7. Pro: A teenage mother could face several social obligations like not getting respect from friends and family members and experience an emotional trauma for bad reputation.
1.2.7.5.1.2. Con: [PPD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Postpartum_depression) shows that both women who abort and women who keep the baby have a trauma, therefore it makes no sense to ban the option of having an abortion.
1.2.7.5.1.3. Con: Experiencing feelings of guilt or regret in the short-term after an abortion is not a mental health problem; in fact, such emotions are a normal part of making a life decision that many women find to be [difficult](http://time.com/3956781/women-abortion-regret-reproductive-health/).
1.2.7.5.1.3.1. Pro: There might also be 'mental and physical consequences' if a woman has a baby she does not want. It is up to the woman to decide which course of action will cause them the least harm and she should be provided adequate information in order to do so.
1.2.7.5.1.3.1.1. Pro: Postpartum depression [PPD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Postpartum_depression) is quite frequent \(15% of women giving birth\). PPD can in its serious form result in postpartum psychosis \(1/1000\). Psychosis is one of the leading reasons for murdering children in the first year. It makes no sense to make something illegal on the basis that there is some small risk to mental and physical well being as a side effect of a medical treatment.
1.2.7.5.1.3.1.1.1. Con: Legal status of abortion is not based only on medical risks concerning the act of abortion but also ethical dilemma and implications of it.
1.2.7.5.1.3.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.3.1.1.1.
1.2.7.5.1.4. Con: -> See 1.2.7.5.1.3.1.
1.2.7.5.1.5. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.6.
1.2.7.5.1.6. Con: An important part of the mental consequences of abortion are related to the fact that right now it is taboo. Legalizing it puts the problem on the table and thus makes it easier for women to talk about it or deal with post-abortion.
1.2.7.5.1.6.1. Con: There is no evidence that the consequences of abortions are due to it being taboo. Moreover, many wrong things are taboo and have negative consequences. This does not mean they should be legalized.
1.2.7.5.1.6.1.1. Con: What it means is that negative consequences which are the result of people opposing it are not a good reason for something to remain opposed.
1.2.7.5.1.6.1.2. Con: Recent research suggests that two out of three pregnant persons who have abortions anticipate [stigma](https://abguide.uchicago.edu/page/understanding-abortion-stigma-and-shame) if others were to learn about it. In a large US survey, 58% of pregnant persons felt they needed to keep their abortion secret from friends and family and 17% believed their regular healthcare provider would treat them differently if they knew about the abortion.
1.2.7.5.1.6.2. Pro: The mental problems often arise because of the conflict with society itself. Women who chose an abortion are too often told that they do something wrong and immoral. It's only understandable and normal that someone who is forced to hear such things will develop mental issues. If society itself was more understanding towards this topic there would be less mental problems after choosing an abortion.
1.2.7.5.1.7. Con: There are mental and physical consequences to literally every action. This is not a valid reason to restrict individual freedom.
1.2.7.5.1.8. Con: Women seeking an abortion are generally able to get expert counselling and advice on the possible mental and physical consequences, which can help them make responsible [decisions](https://www.nytimes.com/2016/12/14/health/abortion-mental-health.html).
1.2.7.5.1.8.1. Pro: In the US, women seeking abortions are required to be counselled about possible emotional or psychological effects in 22 states, nine of which focus almost entirely on potential [negative effects](https://www.nytimes.com/2016/12/14/health/abortion-mental-health.html).
1.2.7.5.1.8.1.1. Con: There is no [medical evidence](http://time.com/4599806/abortion-doesnt-negatively-affect-womens-mental-health-study/) to justify laws requiring women seeking abortions to be warned about negative mental and emotional side effects.
1.2.7.5.1.9. Con: Medical help is available for women who experience mental or physical problems after having an abortion.
1.2.7.5.1.9.1. Con: Medical assistance will not necessarily be accessible and affordable for suffering women of low socio-economic status.
1.2.7.5.1.9.2. Con: Medical and psychiatric help is also available to women during their pregnancies who feel reluctant to birth a child due to prenatal depression or other issues surrounding it.
1.2.7.5.1.10. Pro: Studies have shown that abortion has adverse psychological impacts on women.
1.2.7.5.1.10.1. Pro: A [recent study](http://www.jpands.org/vol22no4/coleman.pdf), limited in scope to self-reporting by 987 women visiting CareNet pregnancy centers, found that only 13% of the women had visited a psychologist, psychiatrist, or counselor pre-abortion, but 67.5% sought care post-abortion.
1.2.7.5.1.10.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.6.5.4.
1.2.7.5.1.10.3. Pro: A [survey study](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3395931/) of 278 women in Tehran post-abortion found that one-third experienced negative psychological side-effects following an abortion. Of this third, 60.5%  reported depression, 48.7% reported developing an eating disorder, 43.7% reported decreased self-esteem, 39.5% reported having nightmares, 37.5% reported feelings of guilt, and a third expressed regret.
1.2.7.5.1.10.3.1. Con: -> See 1.2.7.5.1.6.
1.2.7.5.1.10.3.2. Con: There are all sorts of issues with that study. It's a very small sample, only 278. Its purpose is "Detecting types and frequent psychological side effects of abortion among post abortion care seeking" so everyone involved will have something negative to say or they would not be seeking post abortion care. Its conclusion is anything but anti-abortion — "Women's Psychological consequences of abortion have considerably been neglected in a community which has sinful and illegal look to abortion".
1.2.7.5.1.10.3.3. Con: Another [survey](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2580059/) on 192 non-pregnant woman shows the effects of unwanted pregnancy on women. 28% were willing to trade time from the end of their life, 16% of women were willing to accept an immediate risk of death and 60% of women were willing to pay some amount of money to avoid pregnancy.
1.2.7.5.1.11. Pro: Women can be face severe bodily harm as a result of abortion.
1.2.7.5.1.11.1. Pro: There can be immediate and long-term [medical consequences](http://www.aul.org/womens-health-defense-actlate-term-abortion-limit/) of abortion including haemorrhage, infections, organ damage and future pre-term births.
1.2.7.5.1.11.1.1. Con: Which is why it should be safe and easy to get an abortion quickly before a surgery is required. [Between 2-10 weeks the mother can have a non-surgical abortion.](https://adviceandaid.com/abortion/types-of-abortions/)
1.2.7.5.1.11.1.2. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.6.4.
1.2.7.5.1.11.1.3. Con: There are always potential consequences of medical treatments and operations. However, we allow people to opt into these even when they are not medically necessary, such as with plastic surgery.
1.2.7.5.1.11.1.3.1. Pro: The decision to undergo such a medical treatment or operation should be made by the individual woman, with full information provided by medical professionals.
1.2.7.5.1.11.1.4. Con: Legal abortions performed in the developed world are among the [safest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abortion#Safety) procedures in medicine.
1.2.7.5.1.11.1.4.1. Pro: A [2012 study](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22270271) in the US found that from 1998-2005 induced abortion had a maternal mortality rate of 0.6 deaths per 100,000 abortions, compared to a maternal mortality rate for pregnancy and childbirth of 8.8 deaths per 100,000 live births.
1.2.7.5.1.11.2. Pro: Women with an abortion history are at an increased risk for [sexual dysfunction](http://www.wecareexperts.org/sites/default/files/articles/Abortion%20and%20intimate%20relationships_0.pdf) and face problems related to sexual desire, frequency of sexual intercourse, orgasm ability, and sexual satisfaction.
1.2.7.5.1.11.2.1. Pro: 10-20% of women [experience](http://www.wecareexperts.org/sites/default/files/articles/Abortion%20and%20intimate%20relationships_0.pdf) abortion-related sexual problems in the early weeks and months after an abortion, while 5-20% of women report sexual difficulties a year later.
1.2.7.5.1.11.2.2. Pro: More than 30% of women in a Swiss longitudinal study reported a minimum of one sexual problem six months after an abortion \([pg.4](https://www.imfcanada.org/sites/default/files/Interconnected_May2014_1.pdf)\).
1.2.7.5.1.11.2.3. Con: This does not disqualify the choice of abortion. It should be up to the woman to decide, whether to take the risk or not.
1.2.7.5.1.11.2.4. Con: -> See 1.2.7.5.1.7.
1.2.7.5.1.11.2.5. Con: -> See 1.2.7.5.1.8.

1.2.7.5.1.11.2.8. Con: -> See 1.2.7.5.1.3.1.1.
1.2.7.5.1.11.3. Pro: As the fetus becomes more developed, there is a greater risk that an abortion will result in [health risks and complications](http://www.spiked-online.com/newsite/article/10015#.WhrwQEpl86w) for the mother.
1.2.7.5.1.11.3.1. Pro: The [complication rate](http://www.aul.org/womens-health-defense-actlate-term-abortion-limit/) for abortion increases from about 3-6% in the first trimester, to over 50% as abortions are performed in the later trimesters.
1.2.7.5.1.11.3.2. Con: The easier it is for women to have abortions, the earlier they will take place.
1.2.7.5.1.11.3.3. Con: The health risks associated with a late abortion, are still [less](http://www.spiked-online.com/newsite/article/10015#.WhrwQEpl86w) than then health risks associated with childbirth.
1.2.7.5.1.11.3.3.1. Con: The original [article](https://www.rcog.org.uk/globalassets/documents/guidelines/abortion-guideline_web_1.pdf) only considers mental health of unintended pregnancies for this comparison.
Furthermore, this response completely ignores the foetus, central in the original argument.
1.2.7.5.1.11.4. Con: Doctor's can and should inform patients of the risks in any operation. The presence of these risks doesn't change the right of the patient to make an informed choice.
1.2.7.5.1.12. Pro: Women are [more likely to die](http://afterabortion.org/2012/multiple-abortions-increase-risk-of-maternal-death-new-study/) following an abortion.
1.2.7.5.1.13. Pro: There are dozens of [studies](https://www.cambridge.org/core/journals/the-british-journal-of-psychiatry/article/abortion-and-mental-health-quantitative-synthesis-and-analysis-of-research-published-19952009/E8D556AAE1C1D2F0F8B060B28BEE6C3D) by [various groups](https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/full/10.3109/14767058.2015.1051022) finding that woman are not only much more prone to various mental illnesses post abortion, such as clinical depression, PTSD, and suicidal tendencies, but also various physical maladies such as chronic pain, unintentional sterility, and future pregnancy complications.
1.2.7.5.1.14. Con: It is dishonest to tell women who are considering an abortion, that they face medical risks. The overwhelming majority of abortions are perfectly [safe](http://www.spiked-online.com/newsite/article/a-moral-case-for-abortion/18826#.Whn73Upl86w).
1.2.7.5.1.14.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.6.4.
1.2.7.5.1.14.2. Pro: -> See 1.2.7.5.1.11.1.4.

1.2.7.5.2. Con: Social backlash is not an issue in secular regions where abortion is legal and normalized.
1.2.7.5.2.1. Con: Just because a country is secular and abortion is legal it does not mean that abortion does not have a negative stigma attached to it in society, or that it cannot generate social backlash. Most of these countries have lobbyists and political parties that are strongly anti-abortion.
1.2.7.5.2.1.1. Pro: In the majority of EU countries abortions are legal, but in some states a wave of "retrogressive restrictions" are threatening women's health and well-being, according to a report by the [European Council](https://euobserver.com/health/140158).
1.2.7.5.2.1.2. Pro: In the [US](https://www.nytimes.com/2018/01/19/us/politics/trump-anti-abortion-marchers.html?rref=collection%2Ftimestopic%2FAbortion) President Trump has expanded religious freedom protections for health care providers who object to performing abortion; created a new entity within the Department of Health and Human Services called the Conscience and Religious Freedom Division; and declared the 22nd January 'National Sanctity of Human Life Day.' In a speech addressed to thousands of anti-abortion protesters, he said "We are with you all the way."
1.2.7.5.2.1.3. Pro: There are a large number of anti-abortion organisations in the [US](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_anti-abortion_organizations_in_the_United_States).
1.2.7.5.2.1.3.1. Pro: For example the [Army of God](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Army_of_God_\(United_States\)) is a Christian terrorist organisation that has engaged in the use of violence in the United States to fight against abortion.
1.2.7.5.2.1.3.2. Pro: In the [US](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-abortion_violence) violence directed towards abortion providers has killed at least eleven people, including four doctors, two clinic employees, a security guard, a police officer, two people \(unclear of their connection\), and a clinic escort.
1.2.7.5.2.1.3.3. Pro: Since 1977 \(in the [US and Canada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-abortion_violence)\) there have been 17 attempted murders, 383 death threats, 153 incidents of assault or battery, 13 wounded, 100 butyric acid stink bomb attacks, 373 physical invasions, 41 bombings, 655 anthrax threats, and 3 kidnappings committed against abortion providers.
1.2.7.5.2.1.4. Pro: Anti-abortion organisations and movements are widespread across [Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-abortion_movements).
1.2.7.5.2.1.4.1. Pro: In [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_for_Life_\(Paris\)), the anti-abortion movement organises a yearly protest called 'March for Life'.
1.2.7.5.2.1.4.2. Pro: In [Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-abortion_movements), over one million demonstrators took part in a march in Madrid in October 2009 to protest plans by the government to legalise abortions and eliminate parental consent restrictions.
1.2.7.5.2.1.4.3. Pro: In 2010 in [Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-abortion_movements) over one million people signed a petition opposing the government's liberal abortion policy.
1.2.7.5.3. Pro: Abortion can have a negative effect on living children.
1.2.7.5.3.1. Pro: Post-abortal women report that their ability to respond to the remaining or future child\(ren\) can be manifested in several ways: a feeling of emotional numbness which leads to a lack of bonding, acting out of hostility and anger which can result in child abuse, and considering future children as “replacement children” who become overindulged \([pg.11](http://www.deveber.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/Chap15.pdf)\).
1.2.7.5.3.1.1. Pro: After abortion, “replacement” children may find themselves the object of obsessive [parenting styles](https://cdr.lib.unc.edu/indexablecontent/uuid:204af9c9-18ec-450b-8680-7f19890eec5a) of post-abortal parents who focus inordinate time, affection, or material goods on them. Parents may attempt to replace the lost child with a “wanted” child soon after the abortion. This can be [detrimental](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2791524/) to a child's development and behavior \([pg.13](http://www.deveber.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/Chap15.pdf)\).
1.2.7.6. Pro: [6 out of 10](https://www.plannedparenthood.org/learn/abortion/considering-abortion) people who get abortions already have children, and many feel they need to dedicate their time and resources to the children they already have, rather than having another.
1.2.7.6.1. Con: That seems to be remedied easily and ahead of potential pregnancy by tubal ligation and/or vasectomy rather than abortion.
1.2.7.6.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.4.3.
1.2.7.6.1.2. Con: Parents might not want another child for a time being and decide to attempt at pregnancy few years later.
1.2.7.6.1.2.1. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.4.4.3.4.
1.2.7.6.2. Pro: The birth of an unwanted child may have significant effects on existing children, including reductions in availability of care giving and increases in poverty. A [study](https://www.ansirh.org/sites/default/files/publications/files/2014-9foster-unwanted-pregnancy-effects.pdf) by University of California shows that existing children of women denied an abortion have 4 percentage point lower scores across all six domains of child development.
1.2.7.6.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.7.4.
1.2.7.6.2.2. Con: -> See 1.2.7.5.3.
1.2.7.7. Pro: Parenthood has a negative impact on marriage and the relationship between spouses suffers once children come along.
1.2.7.7.1. Pro: Parenthood hastens [marital decline](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2367106/) - even among relatively satisfied couples who select themselves into this transition. The rate of the decline in relationship satisfaction is nearly twice as steep for couples who have children than for childless couples.
1.2.7.7.1.1. Pro: In the event that a pregnancy is unplanned, the parents experience even [greater](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2702669/) negative impacts on their relationship, including increase in relationship conflict and a decrease in love.
1.2.7.7.2. Con: Abortion can also have a negative impact on marriage and relationship.
1.2.7.7.2.1. Pro: There is an increased risk for separation or divorce following an abortion \([pg.2](https://pdfs.semanticscholar.org/b499/4a5f23c5c9da17418d51e341cec0ee8d3eb1.pdf)\).
1.2.7.7.2.1.1. Pro: A [study](http://www.lifeissues.net/writers/air/air_vol20no1_20071.html) by Rue and colleagues reported that out of 331 Russian and 217 American women, 6.8% of Russian women and 26.7% of American women indicated relationship problems caused by an abortion experience. 7.8% of Russian women and 19.8% of American women indicated that their relationships had ended as a direct consequence of the abortion.
1.2.7.7.2.2. Pro: Associations between abortion and relationship conflict are logical since [anger](http://americanpregnancy.org/unplanned-pregnancy/abortion-emotional-effects/) is a common post-abortion emotional [response](https://ramahsvoice.com/5-types-anger-abortion/).
1.2.8. Con: If as a society we put others first, people would be there to help with what is needed to raise the child. In this type of society, the mother wouldn't have to consider ending another's life for convenience.
1.2.8.1. Con: But we do not live in a society where people are just willing to help raise other people's children. We live in a society that blames women for accidentally getting pregnant, and decries welfare systems that help these women.
1.2.8.1.1. Con: There are people, programs, and organizations willing to help. [SNAP](http://www.ny.gov/services/apply-snap) and [WIC](https://www.fns.usda.gov/wic/women-infants-and-children-wic) are examples of government programs that help single mothers. There are many local charities all over the country that help single mothers. While some people may blame the women and decry welfare, many would want the best for the women. In some people's view an abortion wouldn't be the best for the woman. Embracing available help would lead to healthy relationships.
1.2.8.1.1.1. Con: The woman in question should be the one to decide what is best for her. If society sees her as able to handle the responsibility of raising a child, she should also be able to make other decisions concerning her own life.
1.2.8.2. Pro: In a society where women were able to fully raise these children or ensure that they end up in safe homes, caveating that everything was consensual, the only harm to the woman would be pregnancy. The minor pains and inconveniences of pregnancy should not outweigh a child's life.
1.2.8.2.1. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.5.
1.2.8.3. Con: Such an ideal environment does not exist in any commonplace way, and is so rare as to be completely useless to the average women making this decision.
1.2.8.3.1. Con: People willing to help others is common. We should strive to make this more known and more common for these issues.
1.2.8.3.1.1. Con: Insofar that this ideal is not an absolute then exceptions must exist, including exceptions when women must have the right to choose abortion.
1.2.8.3.2. Pro: Until this ideal society is considered the norm and resolves all women of the need to make this decision, it cannot be accepted as a reason to deny all women the right to abortion.
1.2.8.4. Con: Abortions are rarely done for convenience.
1.2.8.4.1. Con: Most of the reasons given have to do with[convenience](http://www.johnstonsarchive.net/policy/abortion/abreasons.html).
1.2.8.5. Con: If we accept that in a society where people put others first, women do not need to consider abortion and therefore women should not have the right to choose then we must also accept that in a society where people do not put others first, women do need to consider abortion and therefore they should have the right to choose. In contemporary society, women do consider abortion. Therefore, we do not live in a society where people put others first and women should have the right to choose.
1.2.8.5.1. Con: The proposition to demand abortion as a right is ensuring to produce a society that does not put others first.
1.2.8.6. Con: This argument merely refers to a subset of all abortions \(those conducted for reasons of convenience\). Regardless of whether you accept the premise, it does not provide a reason to oppose the right to abortion under other circumstances. To oppose women’s rights to abortion under some circumstances but not others suggests that in those other circumstances they should still have the right to choose.
1.2.9. Pro: A woman might feel that her home does not provide a safe environment for a child.
1.2.9.1. Pro: Women in physically violent and abusive relationships are likely to stay [tethered](http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1363/47e2315/pdf) to abusive partners when they are unable to terminate unwanted pregnancies. This puts both the women and their children at increased risk of violence and other negative health consequences.
1.2.9.1.1. Pro: Intimate partner violence is [common](https://bmcmedicine.biomedcentral.com/articles/10.1186/s12916-014-0144-z) among women having abortions, with between 6% and 22% reporting recent violence from an intimate partner. Concern about violence is a reason some pregnant women decide to terminate their pregnancies as they do not wish to expose children to violence.
1.2.9.1.2. Con: Governments have processes to remove children from these types of situations. In the United States, they have Child Protective Services. This service alongside adoption, imprisonment, and help from family members saves countless children from harm.
1.2.9.1.2.1. Con: The original claim dealt with women worried about raising children in their own home environments. Child protective services takes children away from parents, which does not help the women seeking a safe environment and the intervention of the Child Protection Service may make that environment even worse.
1.2.9.1.2.2. Con: -> See 1.1.6.
1.2.9.1.2.3. Con: -> See 1.2.4.1.1.1.
1.2.9.2. Con: -> See 1.1.
1.2.9.3. Con: Optimal conditions for child-rearing are relatively rare. Children raised in unsafe environments can survive and thrive despite risk factors.
1.2.9.3.1. Con: This is an overly optimistic view. Childhood neglection, violence and trauma can amount to an ordeal that is all but destroying a child from within.
1.2.9.4. Con: Aborting the child does not make her home safer for the mother nor for any other child. Aborting a baby, thus taking its life away to protect them from getting harmed is the pinnacle of intellectual bankruptcy.
1.2.9.5. Con: Much like we wouldn't consider killing the woman for being in an unsafe environment, we shouldn't consider killing the child. The solution is to get the woman and/or child out of the unsafe environment.
1.2.10. Con: There are cases where a woman feels like she is not equipped when in fact she is. In these cases she only needs more self confidence, not an abortion.
1.2.10.1. Con: -> See 1.2.8.1.1.1.
1.2.10.2. Con: In the cases where the mother feels like she is not equipped, she would be better served by help and guidance, rather than being forced to go through it. [Andrea Yates](http://time.com/4375398/andrea-yates-15-years-drown-children/), [Tamara Butler](https://caymannewsservice.com/2016/03/god-told-mother-to-kill-her-child/), and [Christina Treadway](http://people.com/crime/carolina-panthers-mom-killed-children-jumped-bridge/), for example. Pro-birth pundits should focus on care for mothers which would help both the born and unborn.
1.2.10.2.1. Con: The remote possibility that an extremly mentally derranged woman could end up doing terrible things is not a reason for a relatively healthy woman to have an abortion.
1.2.10.2.2. Con: These examples while horrific, are outliers, not representative of the general population. The vast majority of women are perfectly capable of raising children. Many do not see their own strength.
1.2.10.3. Pro: Prenatal depression is a factor that might push a pregnant woman towards abortion. Were it to be treated she might decide otherwise.
1.2.10.3.1. Con: Yes, it may impact some mothers. Quickly treatable prenatal depression not associated with unfortunate life circumstances that would significantly impact the mother's ability the raise child is a small subset of the population. 1.2.10.3.2. Pro: Some women would only need to see their own strength. They might end up seeing children as giving purpose and meaning to their life.
1.2.10.4. Con: It is not the place of society or legislators to assert whether or not a woman needs confidence or an abortion. Passing laws based upon the assertion of what someone ought to do is a slippery slope that could lead to other assertions about what people ought to do. It is not the place of the government to prescribe certain beliefs and decisions upon people's life choices.
1.2.10.5. Con: Women often have a multitude of sources to help them with this decision including friends, family, the father, a doctor, counselors and so on.
1.2.11. Pro: The pragmatist will concede that we do not live in a perfect world and we are, more often than not, forced to live in grueling self-reliance. Many women who are disadvantaged cannot, under any circumstances, give the proper care required for a healthy child, emotionally and physically, to develop. When this occurs there is a net negative imposed on the society and the individuals impacted by the restricted access. It is unhealthy for the people and communities to restrict freedom.
1.2.11.1. Con: The impact on our society is exceedingly more negative if we allow our moral values to be overruled by net impacts. Although it is not good for a child to grow up disadvantaged, it is much worse for them to have their potential predetermined and be consequentally cheated out of life altogether. The final point conflates the restriction of freedom with limited opportunities and assumes that every child that grows up with socioeconomic barriers is incapable of overcoming them.
1.2.11.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.9.5.
1.2.11.2. Con: This claim misses the main point of contention about abortion: the restriction of the child's freedom.
1.2.12. Con: Lack of preparedness of a mother does not justify abortion.
1.2.12.1. Pro: Being ill equipped to raise a child is no justification for killing a child. If the fetus can survive detached from the mother then the mother has no unilateral right to kill it for any reason, least of all due to a lack of preparation.
1.2.12.2. Pro: The fact that someone is a burden to you does not make it moral to kill them. Institutionalised patients are a tremendous burden to the taxpayer, yet it would be immoral if the government killed them in order to balance the budget. Corresponding it should be immoral for a woman to abort her baby because her circumstances dictate it inconvenient.
1.2.12.2.1. Con: This argument is based on the flawed assumption that fetuses have a moral status that is equivalent to adult human beings.
1.2.12.3. Pro: Abortion is part of society's control addiction which is unhealthy. When we imagine that we can be in total control of our lives we are constantly disappointed and stressed. The striving to control all aspects of nature to the point of destroying an unplanned pregnancy is one aspect of an unhealthy and unethical approach to life. Being open to the unexpected and unplanned is more sane.
1.2.12.3.1. Con: It is unclear what is meant by "society's control addiction," and whether or not this is verifiable, or whether it applies to all individuals in a society equally. It is also unclear why preferring as much control as possible would negate someone's claim to control over their pregnancy.
1.2.12.3.2. Con: This argument asserts that controlling an unplanned pregnancy is unethical without properly establishing that it is unethical.
1.2.12.3.3. Con: This argument seems to assume that all abortions will be done from a near-psychotic obsessive mind-state, and that the harmful effects from being in that mind-state are enough to outweigh the harmful effects of an unplanned pregnancy.
1.2.12.4. Pro: Mothers of infants are also often unprepared but we call it murder when such a mother kills her 1 year old. The same laws should apply to the fetus.
1.2.12.5. Pro: You should not be able to decide whether the fetus is a life or not based on whether you want the baby or not.

1.2.14. Pro: If she became pregnant from being raped, and was not mentally stable "to carry" or raise a child, then abortion may have to be a consideration.

1.2.14.1.1. These are cases that might lead to abortion, besides rape. Making people take full responsibility for things they cannot control is wrong. Many people such as the government, the man, or the prejudices of society in whole is part of the blame. But, banning abortion without proper welfare is shoving all the blame upon the woman.
