1.2.16.2. Con: Raising the child is not the only choice available. Public policies supporting the pregnancy and further adoption of the child could provide the necessary welfare to women without needing neither abortion nor raising the child.
1.2.17. Pro: Pregnancy and parenthood are very [expensive](https://www.parents.com/parenting/money/family-finances/the-price-of-parenthood-an-exclusive-family-finances-survey/) and time consuming. Many women who get abortions are already mothers, and they want to provide the best care they can to their existing children, financially, emotionally, and physically. This should be their choice.
1.2.17.1. Con: If the fetus is already a child, then it follows from your argument that one should be able to terminate one's offspring to better provide for the rest. This is immoral, and therefore, abortion for the reasons you presented is immoral.
1.2.17.2. Pro: -> See 1.2.7.6.2.
1.2.17.3. Con: -> See 1.1.
1.2.17.4. Con: Vasectomy or tubal ligation would be adequate and less harmful in this scenario.
1.2.17.4.1. Con: Some hospitals do not perform vasectomies or tubal ligations on religious grounds. \(e.g. Many Catholic hospitals in [Canada](http://www.cbc.ca/news/canada/hospital-halts-abortion-birth-control-procedures-1.160978) and the [United States](http://www.times-standard.com/article/NJ/20170916/NEWS/170919863) have not performed these services in the recent past, see links.\) Therefore, this point only applies if these services are readily available and not themselves disallowed.
1.3. Con: When abortion is easily available, it incentivises irresponsible behaviour.
1.3.1. Pro: When access to abortion is easy and cheap, abortion is more likely to be viewed as a legitimate form of contraception or as a fallback option, rather than encouraging women to use preventative contraception such as condoms and the pill.
1.3.1.1. Con: Abortions often require a number of doctors visits and a medical procedure. They are therefore unlikely to be viewed as a legitimate contraceptive option when other contraception is more simple and accessible.
1.3.1.1.1. Con: Birth control pills have continuous physical and mental [side effects](https://www.medicalnewstoday.com/articles/290196.php) that can burden women who choose to use them. Some women might consider abortion to be a better option than deal with the side effects on an almost daily basis.
1.3.1.1.1.1. Pro: The birth control pill has to be taken at the same time daily and pregnancy rates increase dramatically in women who miss a pill \(rates rise 30-80 times, according to the [ARHP](http://www.arhp.org/Publications-and-Resources/Patient-Resources/fact-sheets/Successful-Contraception)\).
1.3.1.1.1.2. Con: Being pregnant has many [similar and often more severe](https://www.mayoclinic.org/healthy-lifestyle/getting-pregnant/in-depth/symptoms-of-pregnancy/art-20043853) side effects, so for most women it is unlikely that repeatedly getting pregnant and having abortions would actually be a better experience.
1.3.1.1.1.3. Con: Unless there are numbers to support this, it is pure speculation.
1.3.1.2. Con: The state has the ultimate power over the availability of abortions and contraceptives. Therefore it is up to the state to promote contraception and family planning over abortions.
1.3.1.3. Pro: A 2016 [paper](https://journalistsresource.org/studies/society/public-health/abortion-birth-control-substitute) on Nepal’s legalisation of abortion provides evidence of true substitution between use of modern contraceptives and abortion. It showed that each new legal abortion provider in a woman’s district of residence was associated with a 2.6 percent decrease in the likelihood of using modern contraception.
1.3.1.3.1. Con: This substitution seems to require holding ease of access to contraceptives constant. Thus, if we as a society decide that using abortion as birth control is bad, we can keep that practice rare by increasing access to birth control at the same time that we increase access to abortion.
1.3.1.4. Con: You cannot deprive the vast majority of legitimate users of abortion just because some will use it as a form of contraception.
1.3.1.5. Pro: The costs paid for so-called "easy free" abortions are shifted onto taxpayers. This is bad because other taxpayers may be more sexually responsible and yet are being forced to cover the enormous costs of the sexually irresponsible.
1.3.1.5.1. Con: It is more expensive for taxpayers to cover the costs of services when a child is born to a mother who can't financially afford to raise a kid. If abortions aren't available to less-wealthy people, taxpayers pay more overall.[The net savings for the nation as a whole over a two-year period if abortions were publicly funded in every state would total at least $339.6 million.](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3100324)
1.3.1.5.2. Con: "Easy free" is just one of the models at which abortions might operate. It can be solved by people paying most of the price in small amounts over time or doing community service hours or many other things. Banning abortion because of taxpayers is as far from the actual issue as it gets.
1.3.1.6. Con: The fall-back option is firstly the morning-after pill.  It is highly unlikely that "in the moment" anyone would consider that they will just get an abortion if they happen to get pregnant.
1.3.1.7. Con: There is nothing easy about an abortion. An easy option is access to affordable birth control.
1.3.1.8. Pro: In many countries without strong state support for family planning services, doctors might be more inclined towards the lucrative work of performing abortions over the prescription of birth control - as was the case in [Romania](http://www.nytimes.com/1996/11/21/world/romania-s-communist-legacy-abortion-culture.html) throughout the 1990s.
1.3.1.8.1. Con: The possibility of doctors being corrupt and state not having strong family planning services support are not variables that should come into play when deciding general legality of abortion. They circumvent the fundamental "right to abortion" issue by blaming external factors.
1.3.1.9. Con: Abortion is considered a serious enough procedure that people are unlikely to rely on it as a form of birth control.
1.3.1.9.1. Pro: The [impact](http://bjp.rcpsych.org/content/193/6/444) an abortion has on the temporary mental health of a women is evidence to show that it is not something taken lightly because the repercussions are quite intense. Hence, it is very unlikely that abortion access will increase irresponsible behaviour. Moreover, abortion will not protect you from an STD.
1.3.1.9.2. Pro: -> See 1.3.1.1.
1.3.1.9.3. Con: Countless statistics refute your claim. A majority of abortions are done out of convenience \(i.e. [inconvenient timing](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/m/pubmed/3243347/) or circumstances\). Additionally there are testimonials of people claiming they use abortion as a form of birth control. Regardless of how seriously doctors take abortion, people are often ignorant or choose to ignore the risks.
1.3.2. Con: It is unclear why access to abortion would necessarily lead to more promiscuity than access to contraception more generally does, as people now have far greater control over their reproductive capacities.
1.3.2.1. Pro: This claim ignores that a second party is required for sexual intercourse to take place. It assumes that the risk of child birth is a dis-incentive to engage in sexual intercourse. The claim is an over-generalization or over-simplification -- that the risk of child birth, not the risk of pregnancy, is dis-incentive enough that more women would engage in sexual intercourse if abortion were available for its mitigation. It ignores that contraception is a mitigation for pregnancy.
1.3.2.2. Pro: It will always be easier, cheaper and less traumatizing to use a condom than to undergo an abortion.
1.3.3. Con: Improved access to abortions does not prevent women from behaving responsibly. Societies which grant women abortion rights almost always stress the importance of behaving responsibly when having sex, for example, by strongly encouraging norms of wearing condoms to prevent STDs.
1.3.4. Con: A woman being impregnated is not invariably a consequence of "irresponsible" \(an arbitrarily-defined term\) behavior on her part, so it is not fair that all women be invariably banned from performing an abortion.
1.3.4.1. Pro: Women do not just have sex on their own - if pregnancy is at stake it means they are having sex with a man, which means it is both the woman and the man's responsibility to make sure no child is conceived during it.
1.3.5. Pro: The abortion pill can be taken at home. This could encourage women to think it is not a serious medical [procedure](https://www.plannedparenthood.org/learn/abortion/the-abortion-pill).
1.3.5.1. Con: The use of the abortion pill; although convenient enough to be taken at home, requires some medical guidance, as using it incorrectly could lead to serious harms to the woman.
1.3.5.2. Con: Taking the [abortion pill](http://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0010782406000783?via%3Dihub) induces substantial bleeding, nausea, and pain so intense that it often requires narcotics to control. It seems unlikely that someone could go through this and not think it is a serious medical procedure.
1.3.5.3. Con: This seems at best a reason to ban the pill, not the procedure itself.
1.3.6. Pro: Some men already use the pill as an excuse not to wear a condom. When abortion becomes easier and cheaper, men are more likely to use this as a way of getting out of using condoms, and pressuring women into being okay with it.
1.3.6.1. Con: Using the manipulative behaviors of men as a justification to impose restrictive laws on women is unfair and disturbingly misogynistic.
1.3.6.1.1. Pro: We would not implement a law that forces all women to carry pepper spray at all times because that would be restrictive to women and would not prevent men from committing acts of assault.
1.3.6.1.2. Pro: Also, women may be as equally sexually active as males. Suggesting that males are the only initiators of sexual contact without strong supporting statistics removes female agency from the argument.
1.3.6.1.3. Con: Justification here is not abusive behavior of men but rather irresponsible behavior of both parties leading to accidental pregnancies. Both men and women should be responsible for mitigating risk of pregnancy if they don't want to raise children.
1.3.6.1.3.1. Con: In the hypothetical scenario above, both men and women are being responsible for mitigating the risk of pregnancy - the woman is on a pill in that scenario.  Hardly an irresponsible behaviour, considering it is the most effective contraception method we know of \(excluding vasectomy and such\).
1.3.6.2. Con: If women are on the pill, then it isn't relevant whether abortion is an option due to the efficacy of said contraception.
1.3.6.2.1. Con: It still is relevant. No form of contraception is 100% effective. Abortion is very likely to be used as a fallback option exactly by women who are on the pill but got pregnant nonetheless.
1.3.6.3. Con: This point directs at a different problem: sexual abuse. Sex is supposed to feel good for both partners, it is up to both to decide if they prefer to use a condom. If a man is manipulating a women into not using a condom when she would prefer to, it is not a mutual decision, and he is obviously taking advantage of her.
1.3.6.4. Con: Having a complete disregard for the woman's ability to think for herself in this situation is a dangerous concept. A woman is capable of making responsible decisions and saying no. The two situations are unrelated.
1.3.6.4.1. Con: While women do think for themselves \(as all humans do\) they often make irresponsible decisions, especially if enabled or encouraged by other people \(as all humans do\).
1.3.6.4.1.1. Con: "What if" scenarios are not a basis for banning the right to abortion from every woman. There are many ways a woman can get pregnant, many of which are not the result of woman's irresponsible behaviour. Almost everything would have some reason to be banned if we went down this rabbit hole.
1.3.6.5. Con: It is male-centric thinking that women would succumb to pressure to have unprotected sex just because abortion is an easier or cheaper option.
1.3.6.6. Pro: It's plausible that in the heat of a romantic moment both consensual partners may be less concerned about protected sex if abortion is an easy enough option.
1.3.6.6.1. Con: It's not plausible to consider abortion to be an easy enough option. Medical operations rarely are as there are many associated risks and costs.
1.3.6.6.1.1. Pro: Abortions, even when done early, come with cramping and other unpleasant physical side effects.
1.3.6.6.2. Con: Couples who are caught up in the heat of a romantic moment and engage in unprotected sex seem far more likely to use "morning after" birth control than to wait for a potential pregnancy and then have an abortion.
1.3.6.7. Con: An irresponsible man and a woman that create a situation where he is able to "talk" her into having unprotected sex because an abortion is easy or cheap, is a perfect example of two people that don't need to be parents. If they are this careless they should not have to raise a child that neither are mature enough for.
1.3.6.7.1. Pro: Disfunctional relationships may lead to disfunctional families, which in turn may lead to disfunctional people. Abortion may be the better option, both for individuals involved \(and potentially involved, e.g. the child\) and for society.
1.3.6.8. Con: -> See 1.3.1.9.
1.3.7. Con: There is no evidence that abortion access makes women engage in more irresponsible behaviour.
1.3.7.1. Pro: Legalising of abortion did not occur to make it easier on the irresponsible. In [Norway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abortion_in_Norway#Gradual_liberalization_and_a_core_feminist_cause), it started with really hard cases where a committee decided for the pregnant persons whether they could get an abortion. After 25 years there are now [less abortions](https://www.ssb.no/helse/artikler-og-publikasjoner/25-aar-med-selvbestemt-abort-i-norge) per 1000 women than at the start. This suggests legalisation does not increase behaviour that leads to more abortions.
1.3.7.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.10.4.2.1.1.
1.3.7.3. Pro: Comparing [OECD countries](https://data.worldbank.org/indicator/SP.ADO.TFRT) with and without legal abortion shows that legalisation of abortion does not lead to irresponsible behaviour, while allowing more self determination.
1.3.7.4. Pro: The argument relies on the weak idea that availability of a choice \(abortion\) may make other behaviours more likely - even though there is no evidence to support that claim. However, we know for a fact that if women are denied access to abortion, the consequence is an unwanted pregnancy, and an imposition of someone else's will on that of a woman in a very difficult or health-endangering position. A weak hypothetical risk should never outweigh a very serious real one.
1.3.7.5. Pro: If we consider this a valid argument, then we should also consider that healthcare makes people take bad food choices, and we should not provide treatment for type 2 diabetes \(because people got sick conciously\). There should not be medical aid to people who got injured for being driving a car drunk, etc. Answer is education on prevention.
1.3.7.6. Con: This [study](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/m/pubmed/15457623/) argues that there is a link between access to abortion and increased sexual activity, which was also linked to an increase in STDs.
1.3.7.6.1. Con: The study argues that more access to abortion created an increase in STDs, which the authors used to measure an increase in risky sex. We should see if it links to more pregnancy not just STDs, as there are a lot of contraceptives, but only condoms can prevent STDs. Therefore if the woman is using pills, implant, etc. they are not protected from STDs.
1.3.7.6.2. Con: Abortion should not be conflated with birth control. Abortion is the termination of a pregnancy, so any claims about its use or consequences should not include claims about STDs and/or increased sexual activity.
1.3.7.6.3. Con: The study showed only an association, not direct causation. The data was used to support a previously made hypothesis, not to develop a hypothesis from observed behaviour. Relationships to other activities and behaviours may exist, but have not been tested. Cherry picking, or argument by selective observation, is a well known logical fallacy and the result of the study may need to be challenged.
1.3.7.6.4. Con: It is only natural that increased sexual activity correlates with an increase in STDs. That's like saying that increased production of automobiles correlates with an increase in traffic accidents. Whenever people do something more regularly, the activity more regularly leads to accidents. This is not a sensible reason to stop doing things.
1.3.7.6.5. Con: According to [data](https://www.cdc.gov/std/stats12/tables/1.htm#modalIdString_CDCTable_0) from the CDC there is indeed a rise of gonorrhoea cases in America starting 1970 but there is a drop of syphilis cases at the same point which contradicts that study.
1.3.7.6.6. Con: Sexual intercourse is a normal human function. It is not irresponsible behavior.
1.3.7.6.6.1. Con: A normal consequence of sexual intercourse is pregnancy. Having sex \(especially unprotected sex\) disregarding consequences of the act is the very definition of "irresponsible behavior".
1.3.7.6.6.2. Con: The original claim was not that sexual intercourse was in and of itself irresponsible. For example, protected sex is responsible, unprotected sex with the realisation that pregnancy is possible is also responsible. Unprotected sex expecting to abort the pregnancy as a form of birth control is irresponsible.
1.3.7.6.6.3. Con: Humanity has evolved to the point where practicing unsafe sex while unable to support a child is indeed irresponsible.
1.3.7.6.6.3.1. Pro: This is undeniably true when considering the access and expense of frontline contraceptives.
1.3.7.6.6.4. Con: There are plenty of laws on the books that curb/prohibit what otherwise would be considered to be "normal human behavior."
1.3.7.7. Pro: Women are already taking part in sexual relationships, which is not the issue. Abortion is not specifically for women who have had a 'one night stand' and need a quick solution, it is for women who for a variety of reasons \(sexual assault, no financial support, physical ailments\) cannot have a baby.
1.3.7.8. Pro: If this claim was true, it would also be true that having emergency rooms incentivises people to have more head injuries. Even if this fact would be proven by research, it would still be unreasonable to shut down all emergency rooms, just as it would be unreasonable to stop providing abortions in cases of unwanted pregnancy.
1.3.7.8.1. Con: The proposition, "If this claim was true, it would also be true \(...\)", stated above, would be very hard - or even impossible - to support. The behaviour or conditions that lead to abortion are very different from the ones that can lead to head injuries. From another perspective: Can we propose that having emergency rooms can lower the perceived impact of a possible head injury on one's life, thus leading to a lower estimation of the risk of a behaviour that may lead to a head injury?
1.3.7.8.1.1. Con: The behaviour and conditions that lead to abortion are not so different from the ones that lead to head injuries. Examples include: the inability to foresee the consequences of one's actions and being intoxicated. Since many unwanted pregnancies occur as accidents under conditions similar to head injuries, it is unethical and illogical to refuse sensible medical solutions to those problems and make these solutions illegal, while we find it normal to care for head injuries using tax money.
1.3.7.8.1.1.1. Pro: Both head injuries and pregnancies can be the result of assault.
1.3.8. Con: Moral values and habits \(along with irresponsible behaviour\) are taught and learned from home. Abortion is just a method.
1.3.8.1. Con: The set of rules and beliefs in the society have also a huge impact on the moral values and habits of an individual.
1.3.9. Pro: -> See 1.3.7.6.
1.3.10. Con: There will always be outliers in any system who will abuse it. However, it’s socially irresponsible to do away with an entire system because of those statistically few individuals. Just like a small percentage of drivers drove drunk or some people scam Welfare checks, some women will have abortions instead of using birth control. However, we can’t scrap those laws or programs because they aren’t used as intended 100% of the time.
1.3.11. Con: Irresponsible behavior that doesn't harm others should not be prohibited.
1.3.11.1. Con: The whole basis of the argument is whether or not the fetus counts as a "life."  Abortion is clearly a behavior that harms that life.
1.3.11.2. Con: While the rule in this claim is true, it is potentially inappropriately applied here. The child may be an 'other' that will be harmed by the irresponsible behavior in question.
1.3.12. Pro: If you have sex, you may get pregnant. No contraception is perfect, so it is the responsibility of the couple to plan for sex and use contraception if they need. Abortion is not a "bail-out" from a mistake and it cannot be treated that way. Abortion removes the consequences of irresponsible behavior, so it incentivizes people to do it more, ending more innocent lives.
1.3.12.1. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.4.3.
1.3.12.2. Con: Not all sex is between couples, planned, voluntary or any other assumption this claim makes. Banning abortion on these grounds fails to account for many other real-life situations that occur.
1.3.12.3. Con: Abortion is a serious medical treatment with potential risks to the patient. This alone disqualifies it from being incentive for irresponsible behaviour - it has a big psychological and physiological cost attached to it.
1.3.12.4. Con: This argument is only works if we accept sex that is inherently immoral and/or having an abortion is inherently immoral. If neither sex nor abortion is immoral, then there is no reason to punish the behavior of having sex and getting pregnant with restricted access to abortion, just like there is no reason to punish mistypes by removing the backspace key from a keyboard.
1.3.12.5. Con: Carrying a child is an important thing for a woman. Choosing abortion isn't an easy decision, and the women that find this decision easy are a minority. Generally when a woman is considering abortion, she thinks about why she can't rather than why she 'just doesn't want to'.
1.3.12.5.1. Pro: There should be laws requiring mandatory consultations to make this decision as informed and conscious as possible. This will go a long way towards eliminating "convenience abortions".
1.3.13. Con: Abortion does not incentivise sex. Physical pleasure incentivises sex. Abortion may mitigate the consequences.
1.3.13.1. Pro: Women should feel able to have as much sex as they like. Society shouldn't judge them for this, and label such behavior 'irresponsible'.
1.3.13.1.1. Pro: There is a sexist double standard, men who have lots of sex, receive praise from their peer group. However, women who have lots of sex, are labelled 'sluts' and shamed by society.
1.3.13.1.2. Pro: -> See 1.3.4.1.
1.3.13.1.3. Con: What an individual personally feels "should be" and what nature made that "is" are different matters. Sexual behaviors that are more likely to lead to unwanted pregnancies, STDs or compulsive habits are, in fact, short-sighted, pleasure-seeking and irresponsible, and should not be encouraged or supported by society.
1.3.13.1.3.1. Pro: STD risk increases with multiple partners[long term or over short periods](https://www.guttmacher.org/journals/psrh/1999/09/sexual-partnership-patterns-behavioral-risk-factor-sexually-transmitted) of time.
1.3.13.1.3.2. Pro: [Early initiation of sexual activity increases the risk for STDs and unplanned pregnancies.](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2674603/)
1.3.13.1.3.2.1. Con: The authors of this cited paper claim that teaching kids both better contraceptive use and to wait for sex at a younger age decreases the risk for STDs and unplanned pregnancies. Age is not the determinant for safe sex, education is.
1.3.13.1.3.3. Con: This point begins by drawing a contrast between what an individual believes "should be" and what "is", then ends by stating what "should not be" encouraged by society. Society is an artificial construct, so all opinions relating to it are subjective and outside what nature made that "is".
1.3.13.1.3.3.1. Con: Artificial constructs we call "society" have immense influence on human behavior and environment humans operate in. Exactly because it is artificial, actions of elements taking part in the construct are influencing all other parts of it. For example, legalization of abortion causes population decline, which causes decline in GDP, which causes decline in living standard and so on and so forth.
1.3.13.1.3.4. Con: This is the naturalistic fallacy. We, as humans living in a society, get to decide what decisions will make that society the best it can be.
1.3.13.1.4. Pro: Where wanton sexual intercourse and promiscuity is not penalised by laws, there is little reason to impose indirect moral penalties and other sanctions for perfectly legal conduct. If people are legally permitted to conduct themselves in such a fashion, invoking no legal penalty, then they should suffer no legal-moral judgment when they are left to deal with the consequences of their lawful comportment.
1.3.13.1.5. Con: The absence or presence of judgement has no logical or causal relationship to pregnancy or abortion — pregnancy is not the result of society's judgement. It is a possible result of sexual intercourse, and as such must be considered by both parties independent of other concerns.
1.3.14. Con: In sexual intercourse that could possibly result in a conception, a man and a woman are required. If abortion is illegal, this means that what was, for the man a 'fun one-night stand' turns into a nine month period of punishment for the woman. A man played a vital role in the contraception, and the woman shouldn't have to pay for a joint 'mistake'.
1.3.15. Pro: Legal abortion will lower the sense of responsibility. Being responsible for your own sexual actions and performing safe sex is essential and the lack thereof should not be sufficient argument for legal abortion. We are responsible for our own actions.
1.4. Pro: -> See 1.2.2.1.2.
1.5. Pro: When abortion is banned, women who do not want a child are forced to [seek out illegal abortions](http://www.nbcnews.com/id/21255186/ns/health-womens_health/t/abortion-rates-same-whether-legal-or-not/). These are unsafe, and risk the lives of the women that try them.
1.5.1. Con: -> See 1.1.
1.5.2. Pro: The methods used by women when they are unable to legally have an abortion are very unsafe, these include; the use of a [sharp objec](https://drjengunter.wordpress.com/2013/07/13/anatomy-of-a-coat-hanger-abortion/)t to break the amniotic sac to induce an abortion, the use of [abortifacients](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abortifacient), and pumping [toxic mixtures](http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/africa/7328830.stm) inside a women's body. These methods, can cause infection, internal injuries, toxic shock, and a range of other medical complications.
1.5.2.1. Pro: [25%](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2709326/) of the women who survive unsafe abortion suffer long-term health complications \(5 million out of 19,932,000\).
1.5.2.2. Pro: An estimated [100,000-240,000](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-abortion-usa-texas-doityourself/up-against-strict-laws-texas-women-learn-do-it-yourself-abortions-idUSKCN0YF1BC) Texas women have self-induced abortions \(most commonly with [black market misoprostol/Cytotec](https://www.theatlantic.com/health/archive/2014/06/the-rise-of-the-diy-abortion-in-texas/373240/)\) since restrictive abortion laws that forced the closing of many Texas abortion clinics were passed in 2013.
1.5.2.3. Con: The solution is to educate women about the risks of unsafe do it yourself abortions so that its not attempted at all.
1.5.3. Pro: Laws are useless unless they can be properly enforced. Experience shows that prohibiting abortion doesn't diminish abortion cases. In fact, it can increase the numbers of abortions, given that the hesitation for women to confess their intent to commit an illegal activity makes it harder for people to show them better alternatives.
1.5.3.1. Pro: There is an association between unsafe abortion and restrictive abortion laws. Abortion-related [deaths](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2709326/figure/F1/) are more frequent in countries with more restrictive abortion [laws](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2709326/figure/F2/) than in countries with less restrictive laws.
1.5.3.1.1. Con: Consequences for one party are independently enough of a driving factor in decision making in scenarios involving multiple parties or potential parties.
1.5.3.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.10.4.2.1.1.
1.5.4. Con: No one is 'forcing' the woman to get an abortion. There is no armament or law compelling her to do so. In such a scenario, she would be choosing to break the law and terminate another life of her own accord and personal wishes, not because she was 'forced' to undertake the procedure.
1.5.4.1. Con: This [previously posted study](http://www.nber.org/papers/w18338) shows that less than 15% of women would keep the baby based on legality. That means 85% of women have already made the choice to terminate the pregnancy no matter what. Removing the safe and legal options leaves only illegal and often less safe alternatives.
1.5.4.1.1. Con: Those women who have decided to abort, regardless of law, then would be lawbreakers. There are punishments for lawbreakers, and we should not cave to their demands.
1.5.4.2. Pro: The woman can choose to not have an unsafe illegal abortion if abortion was illegal. She could instead choose to continue with the pregnancy. She does not have to choose an unsafe and dangerous abortion.
1.5.4.3. Pro: Breaking the law often results in negative consequences.
1.5.4.4. Con: When there is no other option to terminate a pregnancy safely, and there are circumstances that the child will endanger or harm her in some way, women are forced to seek out illegal abortions.
1.5.4.4.1. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.5.1.4.
1.5.4.4.2. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.5.1.2.
1.5.4.4.3. Con: This is like saying people are 'forced to seek out' illegal drugs when they are unavailable - it's an illogical claim. No one is forcing the woman to do anything.
1.5.4.4.3.1. Con: When someone needs/decides to leave a room and you lock a door it is not illogical to claim that you are forcing them to find another exit, even though you have not indeed forced them to leave.
1.5.4.4.4. Con: The woman still is able to get normal medical treatment, which more effectively targets the problem than abortion in the majority of such cases.
1.5.4.4.4.1. Pro: "Today it is possible for almost any patient to be brought through pregnancy alive, unless she suffers from a fatal illness such as cancer or leukemia, and, if so, abortion would be unlikely to prolong, much less save, life."
- Dr. Alan Guttmacher, 1967
1.5.4.4.4.1.1. Con: Science and medicine have developed significantly since 1967. Today, we have numerous methods to cure what then used to be terminal diseases. Not all of them aresafe for the embryo or fetus, and therefore in some cases the pregnancy should be terminated to prevent irreparable damage. Also, pregnancy is a significant energy cost to a woman's body. The chance of a non-pregnant woman surviving chemo or a complex surgery and then fully recovering is higher.
1.5.4.4.4.1.1.1. Con: Unless the woman needs immediate treatment within the first three months of pregnancy, there are many types of cancer treatment she can opt for that carry [minimal risk to the fetus.](https://www.cancer.net/navigating-cancer-care/dating-sex-and-reproduction/cancer-during-pregnancy) Even risk from the mother's side effects is less than risks from inducing labor early.
1.5.4.4.4.1.1.1.1. Pro: Chemotherapy, a common form of treatment for pregnant mothers, [does not carry a significant risk to the fetus.](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/health/news/9071349/Pregnant-women-can-be-treated-for-cancer-without-harming-baby.html)
1.5.4.4.4.1.1.2. Con: Pregnancy in and of itself [doesn't increase risk](https://www.cancer.net/navigating-cancer-care/dating-sex-and-reproduction/cancer-during-pregnancy) or harm to the mother, except in cases where the mother needs immediate treatment.
1.5.5. Pro: Removing women's right to legal and safe abortion does not remove the necessity for it. Women, if they feel desperate enough, will seek [dangerous abortion methods](https://www.nytimes.com/2016/03/06/opinion/sunday/the-return-of-the-diy-abortion.html) anyway.
1.5.5.1. Pro: In Romania, [more than 9,000 women died](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2013/jan/15/abortion-romanian-history) between 1965 and 1989 due to complications with illegal abortions. This was under Ceausescu's rule and at a time when access to abortion was extremely limited.
1.5.5.1.1. Pro: Legalised abortion furthermore has a great impact on reducing [maternal mortality](https://www.gapminder.org/documentation/documentation/gapdoc010.pdf), as seen in Romania after the liberalization of abortion in 1989.
1.5.5.2. Pro: Clandestine abortions exploit this necessity by making these operations expensive and not taking into consideration the health of the woman.
1.5.6. Pro: If abortions will happen anyway, it is preferable to make them as safe as possible so at least the women survive the procedure.
1.5.6.1. Pro: -> See 1.5.5.1.
1.5.6.2. Pro: -> See 1.5.2.1.
1.5.6.3. Con: Abortions will occur regardless of whether abortion is legal or not. However, when abortion is illegal, fewer abortions will take place, and less babies will die. This is preferable.
1.5.6.3.1. Con: There will be a reduction in the number of babies that will die, but there are other factors to consider. More mothers will die or be injured. More unwanted children will be born. This will strain families and social services. This could lead to more citizens in unstable situations \(unstable homes, orphanages, foster homes\) which is a negative for our society.
1.5.6.3.2. Con: Less babies will die partially because [less babies will be made](https://www.guttmacher.org/gpr/2016/03/new-clarity-us-abortion-debate-steep-drop-unintended-pregnancy-driving-recent-abortion). This suggests that preventing pregnancies helps reduce abortions more than banning abortions, without the increased deaths and lasting harm caused by unsafe abortions.
1.5.6.4. Con: If burglaries happen anyway, it is preferable to make them as safe as possible so at least the burglars do not get harmed in the process.
1.5.6.4.1. Con: If a burglar is injured during the burglary this has a high chance to stop the burglary from taking place. If a woman is injured during an unsafe abortion this has no chance of stopping the abortion. These two situations are not comparable.
1.5.6.5. Pro: Unsafe abortions \(those that take place in unsanitary conditions or are performed by unskilled individuals\) result in [47,000 deaths](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abortion) per year.
1.5.7. Pro: [Nearly 70,000 women](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2709326/) die and [7 million develop dangerous complications](http://www.who.int/mediacentre/factsheets/fs388/en/) every year because they aren't able to access a safe and legal abortion \(not even counting those who die from pregnancy complications or in childbirth\). There is nothing "pro-life" about supporting the criminalisation of abortion.
1.5.7.1. Con: [652,639 abortions were reported by the CDC in 2014](https://www.cdc.gov/reproductivehealth/data_stats/abortion.htm). The WHO estimates 40-50 million annual abortions. Each adult life would have to be worth over 7142 fetuses for your claim to be valid.
1.5.7.1.1. Con: Since adult life is objective and foetal life is subjective, it is perfectly reasonable to claim that an existing adult life is worth more than a potential future one.
1.5.7.2. Pro: Abortion is a moral issue for conservative Christians. Abortion is not a moral issue for most everyone else. It should never be the federal government's job to dictate morality. The government's first priority is to defend it's borders and the freedom of it's people. A Christian would never choose abortion, but it's not a Christian's place to impose morality upon others. All law abiding citizens expect, and even demand, freedom. Pro-choice is the most logical solution.
1.5.8. Con: Abortion could be banned while contraception and adoption is made more accessible. Claiming that forbidding abortion will cause an increase in one issue forgets that other factors might reduce that issue at the same time.
1.5.8.1. Con: Abortion would not disappear no matter how accessible birth control and adoption becomes. There will still be cases of raped, failed birth control, and pregnancies that carry dangers to the Women. As seen from[Sweden's abortion statistics](http://www.johnstonsarchive.net/policy/abortion/ab-sweden.html), despite the fact many parts of the country provide[heavily subsidised birth control for women up to their mid-twenties, and the country provide free condoms at clinics, and free abortions up to 25-26.](http://gynopedia.org/Sweden)
1.5.8.2. Con: Access to contraception will not help when many religious and cultural circles demand abstinence. Young women may have access to contraception but choose not to carry or use it because they are at a higher risk of being caught and punished for being sexually active.
1.5.9. Con: Assuming legal and illegal abortions are equally immoral, the burden on us remains to prevent them from happening. To this end we can prevent women's lives from being needlesly risked \(and support them through their crisis pregnancies and present alternatives to motherhood like adoption\) as well as fulfil our moral obligation to the baby. The objective should be to prevent illegal abortions and provide support structures for the mother.
1.5.10. Con: Many women will keep their baby if abortion is banned. This [study](http://www.nber.org/papers/w18338) found if abortion were prohibited in 31 states, the national US abortion rate would fall by 14.9%.
1.5.10.1. Con: That leaves over 550,000 women every year that will still get an abortion but in an illegal way, which is much less safe.
1.5.10.2. Pro: Making abortion illegal will free up funds for education for women on methods of birth control that also help prevent the spread of sexually transmitted infections, including HIV, help with adoption, pre-natal care and family support, etc.
1.5.11. Pro: When abortion is banned, in practice this means that only women who can afford it can access safe abortion. Getting a safe abortion when it is illegal is more expensive and in low-income countries, a significant fraction of the population cannot afford it. [Who is at risk?](http://www.who.int/mediacentre/factsheets/fs388/en/)
1.5.11.1. Con: This is a marxist-leninist fallacy. The objective shouldn't give poor women safe abortions like the rich ones do. The objective should be avoid having more children killed.
1.5.11.2. Pro: This increases economic inequality, because rich women who are able to travel can get abortions, while poor women who aren't able to travel can't. For example, in the US, [women who are denied abortions are three times more likely to be living below the poverty line two years later than women who are able to access them](http://www.nytimes.com/2013/06/16/magazine/study-women-denied-abortions.html).
1.5.12. Con: Committing murder is not without risk. When a person intentionally sets out to murder another, such an activity always has a level of risk involved for the murderer. The risks involved could be considered between a spectrum of physical death and spiritual purgatory.
1.5.13. Con: The argument that a law has some negative consequences only has merit if those negative consequences are substantial compared to the good effects of the law. In this case, the injuries from unsafe abortion are not substantially comparable to millions of innocent lives saved by banning the practice.
1.5.13.1. Pro: Abortion being illegal would likely lead to a reduction in the number of abortions, which would mean an overall reduced number of lives lost, when considering both the mother and the fetuses.
1.5.13.1.1. Con: -> See 1.1.10.4.2.1.1.
1.5.13.1.2. Con: The overall number might be reduced, but this does not consider the quality of those lives. To begin a life does not assure its well-being; or well-doing.
1.5.13.2. Con: Banning the practice does not save any life. Women will seek abortions whether they are legal or not. The difference here is whether the practice is made by professional doctors or by clandestine doctors.
1.5.13.2.1. Con: Banning the practice of abortion will save unborn lives.
1.5.13.3. Pro: The suggestion is that we should not make laws because people who will still want to break them will break them in a more dangerous way. This logic not only could be used to eliminate all laws that stop immoral things, but is also overlooking the main issue of saving lives that will certainly be killed otherwise, the child.
1.5.13.4. Con: If the mother is in a bad environment, didn't consent with the pregnancy, or is ill prepared to go through the pregnancy, it would cause more harm to the mother and child \(for example bad parenting, crime, mental health issues or little to no opportunity to go beyond the poverty line, transmitted disease, serious birth defect\). The ban would save lives, but those lives can be very cruel.
1.5.13.4.1. Con: This is suggesting that death for the child is not the worst possible outcome. This is called euthanasia and is an unsubstantiated claim.
1.5.13.5. Con: [Nearly 60% of US women who get abortions already have at least one living child](https://www.guttmacher.org/report/characteristics-us-abortion-patients-2014). An increase in unsafe illegal abortions would lead to an increase in orphans and would increase the strain on partners, families, and the government to care for children whose mothers died or were hospitalized after botched abortions.
1.5.14. Con: A better alternative than abortion for reducing these risks is reducing the number of unwanted pregnancies in the first place. Abortion is a poor substitute for contraception, sexual education, and abstinence.
1.5.14.1. Pro: This is why most pro-choice people support universal sexual health education and free contraceptives.
1.5.14.2. Con: The issue is that these resources are not properly allocated or presented to the populace. Women should not be made to suffer because of a failure of government.
1.5.14.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.3.1.8.
1.5.14.3. Con: Abortion is not a replacement for contraception or sexual education, it should be complementary: sexual education and contraception to minimize unwanted pregnancies and legal abortion to minimize risks inherent to an abortion.
1.5.14.4. Pro: Abortion is a band-aid solution to systemic issues in society. While it may need to remain legal, it does nothing to address the reasons behind unwanted pregnancy.
1.5.15. Con: Any act will still happen regardless of whether it is legal or illegal. This is not a sufficient reason to legalize an activity which is wrong.
1.5.15.1. Con: In a democracy, you need a reason to make something illegal, not a reason to make it legal.
1.5.15.1.1. Con: The United States is not a democracy. It is a republic, which is similar, but with key differences.
1.5.15.1.2. Con: There are legitimate reasons for banning abortion. Health and the right to life are some of these.
1.5.15.2. Pro: That a robber will rob a bank regardless of the law is not reason for a bank to pull security and order the guards not to fire lest it be 'unsafe' for the robber.
1.5.15.3. Con: Legality affords those under 'common law' to experience the ability to pursue their intentions with their own methods and ideals, and without the hinderence of others in ways that contradict their ability to pursure their dreams. The 'right to abortion' simply provides anyone a free unbiased environment to choose, it does not determine whether the action is moral. Therefore 'wrong' is not definitive enough to call a reaonable conclusion, and disregarding law is disregarding context.
1.5.15.4. Pro: That's like saying "We shouldn't regulate guns because people would buy guns illegally and from dangerous people anyway".
1.5.15.5. Pro: A great example of this can be seen in the ban on hard drugs. The government knows people will seek out illegal and potentially harmful drugs, but that is not a reason to lift the ban on them, making them easier to access.
1.5.15.5.1. Con: The war on drugs is an good example of why prohibition does not work. Criminalizing behavior may not deter that behavior as long as incentives exist and may only compound the problem without addressing the underlying cause.
1.6. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.
1.7. Con: Abortion might be used for genetic selection.
1.7.1. Con: The above assumes that genetic selection is a bad thing. This cannot be simply assumed without justification.
1.7.1.1. Pro: While there are forms of genetic selection that civilized society agrees is unethical \(genocide\), there is also genetic selection that is universally considered acceptable \(mate selection\). Therefore, genetic selection itself cannot be referenced as a categorically ethical nor categorically unethical practice.
1.7.1.2. Pro: Genetic selection is the cornerstone of Darwinian evolution, however it has traditionally been carried out by mate selection rather than selective birth. To suggest that there is an issue with genetic selection is to suggest that evolution itself is immoral.
1.7.1.3. Con: Genetic selection is by definition the application of stereotypes and would result in racism and sexism against unborn organisms. If the parents don't want short children they would kill the unwanted organism.
1.7.1.3.1. Con: Genetic selection is not the application of stereotypes by definition. Genetic selection can be used for other reasons.
1.7.2. Con: Using abortions for genetic selection can be prevented without outlawing abortion.
1.7.2.1. Pro: [Ohio](http://www.cleveland.com/open/index.ssf/2017/12/gov_john_kasich_signs_down_syn.html) and other states have recently banned abortion after a diagnosis that the child has down syndrome.
1.7.2.1.1. Con: The law bans women from getting an abortion on the basis of that diagnosis - but it is extremely difficult to prove a causal connection between the two.
1.7.2.2. Con: Parents can easily lie about their reasons for wanting an abortion.
1.7.2.2.1. Con: The law could state that pregnant people cannot learn \(non-critical\) information about the fetus until they agree to carry the pregnancy to term except in case of medical complications, thus preventing them from aborting based on genetics.
1.7.2.2.1.1. Con: Preventing women from knowing about the disability status of their child is inconsistent with the critical pro choice argument that she has right to make an informed decision about her body.
1.7.3. Con: It is not unethical to use genetic testing, to prevent babies with severe disabilities from being born. Indeed, it would be cruel to allow individuals whose lives would be characterised by extreme suffering to be born.
1.7.3.1. Con: It is unethical to prevent babies with severe disabilities from being born. A severe disability does not necessarily mean the child will suffer. And yet we allow genetic testing for the purpose of preventing severely disabled children from being born.
1.7.3.1.1. Con: Women might decide to abort a fetus with a disability because they know that they do not have the capacity, time and financial resources to care for a child \(and later, an adult\) with such needs.
1.7.3.2. Pro: Children can be tested for the genetic disease [Tay-Sachs](https://www.nhs.uk/conditions/tay-sachs-disease/symptoms/) whilst they are in the womb. Children with the disease have a maximum life expectancy of 4 years. When the child is alive, they suffer terribly. The child looses their ability to see and hear, the child has difficulties swallowing, and eventually the child will become paralyzed. A women who considers aborting a child with this condition, is not acting immorally, they are preventing their child from suffering.
1.7.3.3. Pro: [Edwards syndrome](https://ghr.nlm.nih.gov/condition/trisomy-18#) can be detected when a baby is in the womb.  The condition causes abnormalities and defects in multiple organs. The majority of children with this condition will die due to a miscarriage. Those that are born, suffer from several life-threatening medical problems. The small percentage of children with Edwards' syndrome who live for longer than one year, often suffer from severe intellectual disabilities. It is not unethical for a woman to abort a child with Edwards syndrome.
1.7.3.4. Con: It is unethical to determine on behalf of another human being that their life is not worth keeping as it may cause them undue suffering, because suffering is subjective. This decision could never be made objectively.
1.7.3.5. Pro: -> See 1.7.3.1.1.
1.7.3.6. Pro: Some birth defects are fatal or severely limiting to a child. A women deserves to choose the best life \(or kindest death\) for themselves and their child.
1.7.3.7. Pro: If people want to voluntarily commit genetic selection they should have a right to.
1.7.3.8. Con: Improvements to medical treatment could be found to [treat](https://nypost.com/2017/10/25/doctors-perform-incredible-surgery-on-baby-inside-womb/) and extend the life of babies with genetic birth defects. Due to medical improvements the average life expectancy of individuals with Down syndrome [is 60.](http://www.nads.org/resources/facts-about-down-syndrome/) [Killing people with genetic defect as a medical solution to genetic disorders](https://www.nationalreview.com/2017/08/down-syndrome-iceland-cbs-news-disturbing-report/) rather then pushing for new treatments or cures leads us back to the same fail vision of the eugenics movement in the 1900's and ultimately can lead to the [systemic genocide of a group of people.](https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/whats-the-real-down-syndrome-problem-the-genocide/2018/03/14/3c4f8ab8-26ee-11e8-b79d-f3d931db7f68_story.html?utm_term=.7ad36c9455f5)
1.7.3.9. Con: Although it is hard to find statistics on the subject, the fact that many people with disabilities live without attempting suicide would seem to imply that they think that their lives are worth living.
1.7.3.9.1. Pro: Most disabled individuals are glad that they were given the chance to be alive, and they are glad that they were not aborted. The able bodied shouldn't make decisions about whether or not a disabled person's life is worth living - without consulting the individual or the disabled community.
1.7.3.9.1.1. Pro: Many [disabled](https://successstory.com/inspiration/10-best-successful-personalities-with-disabilities) people have contributed to society and have lived successful lives.
1.7.3.9.1.1.1. Pro: [Stephen Hawking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_Hawking) is one of the most well-known physicists in the world, and was able to achieve that despite being diagnosed with ALS when he was 21.
1.7.3.9.1.1.2. Pro: [Stevie Wonder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stevie_Wonder) is a musician, singer and songwriter who was born blind. He is considered to be one of the most critically and commercially successful musical performers of the late 20th century.
1.7.3.9.1.1.3. Pro: [Helen Keller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helen_Keller) was an American author, political activist, lecturer and the first deaf and blind person to earn a college degree.
1.7.3.9.2. Con: This is only feasible in economically stable societies with resources to aid the severely disabled.
1.7.4. Con: This is irrelevant. The act of having sexual intercourse and any subsequent decision on whether to have an abortion \(or not\) could also be seen as genetic selection.
1.7.4.1. Pro: The function of mate selection is inherently genetic selection. Most western societies strongly uphold the ideal that one should be allowed to choose whom to have children with. Often married couples will use surrogates to ensure that their children don't inherit potentially devastating genetic diseases. This is not often frowned upon. Genetic selection is not inherently wrong, only the means by which it is accomplished are.
1.7.4.2. Pro: Ones decision with whom to have a baby also counts as genetic selection.
1.7.5. Pro: In many countries girls are more likely to be aborted, resulting in a disproportionate male-to-female ratio.
1.7.5.1. Pro: In China, sons are often seen as more desirable. This is particularly the case in rural areas, in which, sons are valued because of their ability to perform manual and agricultural work. The result of this, is that women are [disproportionately aborted](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/women/womens-life/11393782/China-and-gender-abortion-Government-policy-isnt-the-answer.html).
1.7.5.2. Pro: If there are less women than men in society, large numbers of men will find it harder to get married and have a family. This can result in men feeling [lonely, hopeless and suicidal](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3367246/).
1.7.5.3. Pro: When women are more likely to be aborted, this normalizes a narrative that women's lives are less important.
1.7.5.4. Con: This argument is easily separated from the larger argument by making it illegal to determine the sex of the fetus in these countries as is the case in countries like [India](http://indianexpress.com/article/explained/sex-determination-an-old-law-a-new-debate/) already.
1.7.5.4.1. Con: This approach undermines the freedom of couples to properly plan for their baby. There are legitimate medical and social reasons to find out the baby's sex ahead of time \(e.g. preparing older siblings, intersex children, pure curiosity\) that do not involve sex-based abortion. This unfairly limits all couple's options to prevent some couples from discriminatory abortions.
1.7.5.5. Con: This is actually beneficial to surviving women as a society with significantly fewer women than men gives the women more choices in dating, and consequently more power than they would have before.
1.7.5.6. Pro: In [India](https://www.newscientist.com/article/mg22530074-400-technology-driving-rise-in-abortions-of-girls-in-india/), approximately 10 million girls were aborted between 1991 and 2011, which has led to there being 914 girls to every 1000 boys by 2011.
1.7.5.6.1. Pro: A [study](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21612820) found that in Indian families where the firstborn was a girl, the second child was unnaturally likely to be a boy, whereas if the firstborn was a boy, sex ratios among subsequent children were normal. The study also found that second boys were not aborted, only second girls.
1.7.5.6.2. Pro: A [study](https://www.newscientist.com/article/2083801-records-reveal-gender-selective-abortion-taking-place-in-canada/) found that some Indian-born immigrants in Canada are electively aborting female fetuses if they have already had two daughters.
1.7.5.6.2.1. Con: The incidence of this is low, and the practice is likely to go away on its own as immigrants become [settled](https://www.newscientist.com/article/2083801-records-reveal-gender-selective-abortion-taking-place-in-canada/).
1.7.5.7. Con: This is not an issue relevant to abortion, rather a separate problem. Banning abortion altogether to stop discrimination would be like banning knives or guns to stop murders.
1.7.6. Pro: Disabled children, have just as much of a right to life as any other child. In a society in which women have the right to choose an abortion, the disabled will disproportionately be aborted.
1.7.6.1. Pro: If many disabled children are aborted, the disabled children which are born will have to live in a society with very few people like them.
1.7.6.1.1. Pro: Doctors and specialists will increasingly not learn about disabilities and how to approach subjects such as therapy, physical training, and educations because the market for these products will disappear. This is likely to be incredibly harmful to the disabled children which are born.
1.7.6.1.1.1. Con: Perhaps a "market" need not exist, and bespoke products could take their place.
1.7.6.1.2. Pro: Disabled people will increasingly lack a community of similar peers to support them.
1.7.6.1.2.1. Con: By the same logic, we should prevent those that suffer from any specific ill to get better \(or at least, we shouldn't help others to avoid the ill in the first place\), because that would deprive those that keep suffering from peers to be supported by.
1.7.6.1.3. Pro: People in society will be very unaccustomed to disability which is likely to increase bullying and make people act in ways which are more harmful to these children.
1.7.6.1.3.1. Con: [Positive Behavioral Interventions and Supports](http://www.apa.org/pubs/journals/releases/amp-a0039114.pdf) can help prevent bullying.
1.7.6.1.4. Pro: If there are less disabled individuals, then there are less people who can lobby for the rights of the disabled within society.
1.7.6.1.5. Con: Abortion is currently legal in many countries, and there are still a reasonably sizeable disabled community, such that this does not seem to be the case.
1.7.6.1.6. Con: If a technology is developed, that would allow curing \(preventing\) certain disabilities during gestation, this same argument would go against using it. However, all other factors being equal, curing is evidently always preferable.
1.7.6.2. Con: Aborting a disabled child is not inherently more immoral than aborting a healthy one.
1.7.6.2.1. Con: Aborting an unhealthy child is not more unjust than aborting a healthy child if the reason is the same. If the mother is aborting the child because they are disabled, however, that is discriminatory.
1.7.6.2.1.1. Pro: One has an intuition that if the Nazis had simply spun a wheel and killed 6 million random individuals, this would not have been as bad as killing 6 million individuals because they were Jews. Crimes are worse when they are committed with the intent to harm a person based solely on their identity.
1.7.6.2.1.2. Pro: Intent is the determining factor in a crime. This is why murder is a crime even though the act is the same as killing in self defense. Simply because two people abort does not mean that these two abortions are equally morally valid.
1.7.6.3. Con: This is wide open to reductio. We can replace “disabled children” with any other category of children more likely to be aborted \(say “the children of mothers who are open to the idea of abortion” or “children conceived through rape”\)  and construct an analogous argument.
1.7.6.3.1. Con: The legitimacy of the argument remains. Bottomline, we'll be choosing what type of lives are worth living and what are not.

1.7.6.5. Pro: Countries where women have the right to choose abortion, such as Norway, Denmark and [Iceland](https://www.lifesitenews.com/news/new-report-iceland-aborts-100-of-babies-with-down-syndrome), are about to [eradicate Down syndrome](https://www.lifesitenews.com/news/denmark-denies-practicing-eugenics-because-it-didnt-abort-4-babies-with-dow) through abortion, that is, [eugenics](https://www.nationalrighttolifenews.org/news/2013/12/deselecting-our-children-2/#.WluXxa6nGHt).
1.7.6.5.1. 1.7.6.6. Con: The cost of raising some disabled children can be [four times](https://mom.me/kids/13673-cost-raising-child-special-needs/) the amount of a normal child.
1.7.6.6.1. Con: Some dependent spouses may have much higher demands and be more costly to maintain than others. Assuming the unborn child is a life, and applying the logic and principles of your claim: A supporting spouse would be able to subjectively determine a financial threshold at which their dependent spouse becomes financially unviable. Once this threshold is reached, the supporting spouse can then take the dependent spouse to a designated medical clinic for termination.
1.7.6.7. Pro: By allowing women to choose to abort disabled babies, the state furthers the prejudiced idea that the lives of the disabled are not worth living.

Con: Some parents do not have the money to give disabled children a comfortable life, and adoption agencies do not take many of them because families looking to adopt prefer able bodied babies. 1.7.6.8. Con: A child with a disability may be aborted, to spare them the life of that disability.
1.7.6.8.1. Con: The [social model](https://www.scope.org.uk/about-us/our-brand/social-model-of-disability) of disability, states that disability is primarily caused by societies prejudices. If society provides disabled individuals with the resources that they require, disabled individuals are just as capable of living fulfilling lives as anyone else in society. They do not need to be aborted, in order to spare them of their 'disability.'
1.7.6.8.2. Con: -> See 1.7.3.9.1.
1.7.6.9. Con: The problem with this is that it assumes all women have the resources necessary to raise disabled children. When they do not, those children live a short life full of suffering because they cannot get the services they desperately need.
1.7.6.9.1. Con: If women do not have the necessary resources, adoption is still an option. Adoption and the foster care system may not be great, but they are still preferable alternatives to death.

1.7.6.9.1.2. Con: Adoption is not necessarily a better option - disabled children are less likely to get adopted, which means many of them will be confined to foster care throughout their entire childhood.
1.7.6.9.1.3. Con: In most countries the foster care system is already overburdened, and they barely have the resources to provide for healthy children. It is unlikely that the system would be able to provide sufficient care for an influx of children with special needs.

1.7.7.2.1. 1.7.7.4. Pro: Aborting children purely on the grounds of future looks would be completely unethical and unreasonable.
1.7.7.4.1. Con: "Unreasonable" means "without reason". However the reason for an abortion in this case is that the fetus will grow up unsightly, which is a reason. One must substantiate that the harm of having an abortion supersedes the benefit of producing good looking children.
1.7.7.4.2. Con: This argument only addresses a specific reason for having an abortion. There are many other more compelling reasons for having an abortion. Unless the law were to differentiate the legality of abortions based on the mother's reasons for having the procedure, banning abortions for this reason would ban abortions for much more compelling reasons \(for example, the pregnancy is the result of rape, the baby suffers from a terminal defect, etc.\).
1.7.7.4.3. Con: All abortions are equal. It doesn't matter why you are aborting them; it's either wrong, or its not.
1.7.7.5. Con: In that case, banning genetic testing would be less costly than banning the practice of abortion itself.
1.7.7.5.1. Con: In the future, genetic testing will likely be easy to perform, high in demand, and cheap - making banning it near impossible.
1.7.8. Con: Banning an act because it "might" be used harmfully is unjust and does not take into account the benefits of the its usage.
1.7.8.1. Pro: If we banned everything that might be used in a bad way, we'd have no cars, guns, kitchen knives, etc.
1.7.8.2. Con: The magnitude of harm caused by designer babies, sex-selective abortions, and other forms of genetic selection are so great that they justify preemptive action.
1.8. Con: A significant proportion of the genetic material of the baby belongs to the male. Since the male has a large stake in the fate of the fetus, any decision regarding abortion should be made jointly by both parties, and not just by the woman.

Fatherhood may serve as a signal to potential employers for greater maturity, commitment, or stability. In the context of higher employer expectations for the “family man,” fathers are given less scrutiny for poor performance and more opportunities to demonstrate their abilities than are childless men. \([Pg.11](http://content.thirdway.org/publications/853/NEXT_-_Fatherhood_Motherhood.pdf)\)

The results showed that women with children were 50 percent less likely to get a response from an employer while men with children were slightly more likely than any other applicant to get a call back for an interview.
1.8.2.1.3.1. Pro: When a similar experiment was reproduced in laboratory settings, mothers were offered salaries of around $11,000 less than women without children. Fathers were offered salaries of around $2,000 more. \([Pg.1315](http://gender.stanford.edu/sites/default/files/motherhoodpenalty.pdf)\)

1.8.3. Con: Humans have two types of DNA, the one inside the nucleus which we obtain from both our parents and the one inside the mitochondria which although minimal in comparison can [only be passed on from the mother](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0167488913001092), that said, even in an strictly objective discussion the mother would still have the upper hand since there's more of her DNA in the embryo than there is of the father.
1.8.4. Con: In the cases of rape, incest, and other power situations, a woman should not need the guidance of the man to make personal decisions concerning her pregnancy.  The man should not be allowed to have any say whatsoever.

1.8.5.2. Con: This argument might come from an article that misinterpreted the original study, which definitively does not say anything like "a child has more genetic material in common with it's father". This paper does not support that claim at all. Genotype and phenotype are confused: indeed the paper suggests that the phenotype -protein expression patterns- are more father-like, not the genotype. so genetically speaking the child would still be an equal representation of both parents.

The biological parents of a child adopted by another family do not have the right to reclaim custody just because of their DNA. Biological parents who abuse their children can have their children seized by Child Protective Services because genetic relation does not equal the right to someone else's body and quality of life. A man cannot refuse a woman an abortion even if the fetus contains his genes.
1.8.6. Pro: [Half of the child's chromosomes are inherited from the father](https://www.23andme.com/gen101/origins/) to make up one of each chromosome pair.
1.8.6.1. Con: It isn't half if you take [mitochondrial DNA](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitochondrial_DNA) into account.
1.8.7. Con: A genetic relationship to a child does not grant a person any rights that would supersede a mother's right to bodily autonomy.
1.8.7.1. Pro: The genetic makeup of an embryo should not be considered relevant. By analogy, the blueprints of a building are distinct from the potential building described, the genetic code of an embryo is distinct from the potential infant. A building is built by input of labor and materials from the workers that build it, and an infant is produced by the input of energy and materials from the mother in whose womb it grows. It is immoral to enslave a woman to the labor of producing an infant.
1.8.7.1.1. Con: The comparison to a building blueprints cannot remotely capture the complexity of discussing humanity and genetics. That said, regardless of definitions of start-of-life or nondescript labeling of living things, the father is still an integral dynamic in that decision. Understanding that many situations involve involuntary pregnancies, it is not the mother's right to determine whether the father of the future child deserves a voice. The implications of such have been and are devastating.
1.8.7.1.2. Pro: Genetic material is largely irrelevant to rights of ownership, as in cases of sperm donors, and miscarriages.  Framing a right around this principle leads to absurdity.
1.8.7.1.3. Con: To continue the building analogy; while the blueprints for the building are shared, so could be the costs of labour and materials. If the man "finances" the pregnancy, paying for food and accommodation, for example, he should surely then retain some rights over the foetus. In your analogy, we must ignore the cost of materials and ownership of the building is split by time among those who physically helped to build it.
1.8.7.2. Pro: If a pregnancy is the result of rape, the rapist would also have contributed half of the genetic material to the pregnancy. If the amount of genetic material contributed gives a person a right to choose, then a rapist would have as much right to that choice as the victim of his rape.
1.8.7.2.1. Con: When any individual commits and is convicted of an illegal act, they lose some of their freedoms. It stands to reason that if the father of the child were a convicted rapist, they would not legally have a right to the child.
1.8.7.3. Pro: If someone were to end up with an organ from an organ donor, the donor should not get to have a say about what the receiver can and can't do with that organ simply because it contains his or her genetic material.
1.8.7.4. Pro: The amount of DNA is irrelevant when it is the woman's body that will be subjected to pregnancy and its consequences, and, ultimately, the man has no ownership over that body. After all, a man does not have the right to rape a woman as part of the right to conceive a child, even if he is in a relationship with her. No one can force a child into existence in any way when the vessel is someone else's body.

1.8.9. Con: There may be cases where the man and woman have fundamentally different views about what they should do regarding a pregnancy. In these instances, the woman's view is more important as otherwise she is being forced to either carry a child or have a medical procedure she does not want.
1.8.9.1. Pro: Having a child affects a woman far more than it does a man. Birth is painful and hazardous \(even with modern medical advances\). Having a child reduces income earning potential of the mother but not the father.  Therefore, at a minimum, the woman should have more of a say.
1.8.9.2. Con: Asking the male provider of the baby's genetic material, what their opinion is, is not the same thing as giving the male a veto, and it is preferable to women making the decision to have an abortion unilaterally.

It goes without saying a man would get his just punishment in deceiving a woman, in terms of the lifelong emotional pain and suffering he causes.
