1.9. Con: -> See 1.2.7.5.1.
1.10. Pro: Making abortion accessible brings a variety of social benefits.
1.10.1. Pro: Unless women have the right to choose abortion, the planet will exceed its [carrying capacity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carrying_capacity).
1.10.1.1. Con: Concerns about overpopulation and exceeding a carrying capacity are unfounded.
1.10.1.1.1. Pro: Applied to humans, carrying capacity is an ill-defined concept. The underlying assumption of the carrying capacity argument is that there is a fixed number of people the Earth can sustain. This is simply not the case. As humans change the environment, they also modify the amount of resources available to them. The concept of carrying capacity only makes sense when applied to non-human animals, which do not have the abilities to significantly alter their environment.
1.10.1.1.1.1. Con: All closed systems must by definition have finite resources. The earth is a closed system, therefore there are finite resources and human activity will not change that fact. Our ability to recover used resources is questionable and a goal post that will move, but the amount available will not.
1.10.1.1.1.1.1. Con: Since the earth receives energy from the sun, it is an open system with regard to energy. Humans have the ability to change carrying capacity in all sorts of ways. Advancements in solar power efficiency, for example, could lead to a higher carrying capacity.
1.10.1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: Energy is different from matter. Solar energy allows plants and/or humans to process matter. Higher carrying capacity means more materials/matter and space, since we can't have that, we can't increase the planets carrying capacity.
1.10.1.1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: Even technology like a skyscraper changes the carrying capacity. More people fit with one than without. While there may be theoretical upper limits, the carrying capacity of the Earth isn't fixed.
1.10.1.1.2. Pro: Overpopulation "fear mongering" is unfounded and as societies improve [the number of children reduce over time](https://youtu.be/QsBT5EQt348), as shown by the [Mouse Utopia/Behavioral Sink Experiment](https://youtu.be/HfNKFvHtA3g). Nature will correct itself in one way or another before overpopulation becomes a problem.
1.10.1.1.3. Pro: Plenty of other factors are accelerating a trend of reducing birth rates already in the status quo.
1.10.1.1.3.1. Pro: There is a rise in the accessibility of effective forms of contraception.
1.10.1.1.3.1.1. Pro: In [developed](https://ourworldindata.org/world-population-growth/#population-growth-by-the-level-of-development) countries where birth control is readily available population growth is already negative. Those populations are only growing through immigration, not birthrate.
1.10.1.1.3.2. Pro: Increased urbanization, on the aggregate, gives people better access to family planning and increases competition for space.
1.10.1.1.3.3. Pro: As countries develop more, costs of raising children increase as education standards \(and costs\) rise and it takes longer before children enter the workforce.
1.10.1.1.3.4. Pro: Development leads to proper pension programs, which decrease the necessity for children to take care of oneself in old age
1.10.1.1.4. Pro: At any point the planet could experience a catastrophic event that would drastically reduce the human population. Viral illness, famine, earthquakes near nuclear plants, loss of power grid integrity, etc. We should not end human life to avoid hypothetical future capacity issues.
1.10.1.1.4.1. Con: Modern science and technology has drastically reduced the likelihood of widespread catastrophic events such as viruses, disease, and famine.
1.10.1.1.4.2. Con: Capacity issues are not hypothetical. We already have issues of access to clean water, crops, energy, etc.
1.10.1.1.5. Pro: People living in more developed countries have relatively cheap and accessible birth control already. And population growth is not the immediate problem many think it is. In fact, countries like Denmark offer incentives to couples that bear several children. Their fertility rate is currently at [1.73](https://www.indexmundi.com/denmark/total_fertility_rate.html), sure to result in a population decrease within their borders and financial distress for a generation that will have to care for a large, aging population.
1.10.1.1.6. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.5.1.2.
1.10.1.1.7. Pro: The growth curve for K selected animals \(including humans\) is logistic as it reaches carrying capacity, not exponential. Therefore as human population increases, growth rate slows down.
1.10.1.2. Pro: Abortion has an indirect effect on population growth because women are able to postpone marriage and childbearing where abortion is available, rather than having to get married at a young age because of an unintended pregnancy. The result of these later marriages is that fewer children are born than would be the case if women married at a younger age. \(The Oxford Encyclopedia of Women in World History, Volume 1, [pg.14](https://books.google.com.pk/books?id=EFI7tr9XK6EC&lpg=PA14&ots=o_cTS_axlJ&dq=women%20are%20able%20to%20postpone%20marriage%20and%20childbearing%20where%20abortion%20is%20available%2C%20rather%20than%20having%20to%20get%20married%20at%20a%20young%20age%20because%20of%20an%20unintended%20pregnancy.&pg=PA14#v=onepage&q&f=false)\)
1.10.1.3. Con: Concerns about overpopulation are an incentive to promote contraception, not to promote abortion.
1.10.1.4. Con: Concerns about exceeding the carrying capacity some time in the future are not a good reason to justify abortion, as ending life is not a reasonable response to over population.
1.10.1.4.1. Pro: Society does not allow one person to terminate the life of another, such as a mother murdering her five year old, to keep the planet's population down. If terminating an older child is ethically unacceptable to stave off overpopulation, then terminating the unborn for reasons of population growth is ethically unsustainable.
1.10.1.4.1.1. Pro: If this argument is taken to its logical conclusion, the elderly, the mentally disabled, criminals, the poor, and any other group can also be eliminated for the sake of population control.
1.10.1.4.2. Pro: The solution to overpopulation is not killing individuals \(that is what the Nazis thought\). One should rather invest in sexual education and teach responsibility.
1.10.1.4.3. Con: It can be difficult to predict what levels of over population will be catastrophic for the earth, and therefore it is important to consider methods for population control now.
1.10.1.4.4. Pro: Saying abortions are good for population control is like saying that concentration camps are good for unemployment.
1.10.1.4.5. Pro: Genocide could be a form of population control but morality rules it out, as it does abortion.
1.10.1.5. Con: If this is true, then the burden is on us to formulate a solution which does not sacrifice the moral values that our civilization is predicated on. Abortion erodes those values, birth control does not.
1.10.1.6. Con: This statement assumes that that abortion is the only means of preventing childbirth. This is a faulty assumption. Abortion is only one of several different forms of birth control. It also assumes that men and women have no choice in engaging in intercourse. Practicing abstinence \(which can be done by either of parties involved\) is a lower health risk, no financial cost, more widely available alternative to prevent overpopulation.
1.10.1.7. Con: If we determine that losing lives is necessary to resolve overpopulation then this could equally be done by making abortion illegal, as many women die from accessing illegal abortions.
1.10.1.8. Pro: Every additional human contributes to an increase in humanity's [carbon footprint](https://www.carbonfootprint.com/) on the planet.
1.10.1.8.1. Con: The net marginal impact on climate change of another person existing is far smaller than the comparable impact on a child's life. This issue is relatively unimportant.
1.10.1.8.2. Con: -> See 1.10.1.1.3.1.1.
1.10.1.8.3. Con: Carbon footprint per capita varies greatly across the world. Reducing each person's footprint is more effective and more important than reducing the number of people, as the number of people born will always be a small fraction of the number of people alive.
1.10.1.8.3.1. Con: Having one less child reduces an adult's carbon emissions by an average of [58.6](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/science/2017/07/11/save-planet-cut-holidays-sell-car-dont-have-many-children-say/) tonnes of CO2 per year. Other lifestyle changes result in a much tinier reduction in an adults carbon footprint. For example, if an adult decides not to drive, this only saves around [2.4 tonnes](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/science/2017/07/11/save-planet-cut-holidays-sell-car-dont-have-many-children-say/) of C02 per year. If an adult decides to not eat meat, this only saves [0.8 tonnes](https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2017/jul/12/want-to-fight-climate-change-have-fewer-children) of C02 a year.
1.10.1.9. Pro: Without legalised abortion, population size will increase. An increased global population will put a strain on resources, potentially resulting in [large scale poverty and starvation](https://web.archive.org/web/20120302185414/http://www.dpi.inpe.br/sil/cst310/Aula2_fundamentos/THE_POST_WAR_INTELLECTUAL_ROOTS_OF_THE_POPULATION_BOMB_-_FAIRFIELD_OSBORNS_OUR_PLUNDERED_PLANET_AND_WILLIAM_VOGTS_ROAD_TO_SURVIVAL_IN_RETROSPECT.pdf).
1.10.1.9.1. Pro: It is difficult for states, particularly in the developing world, to provide services and infrastructure, to support expanding populations.
1.10.1.9.2. Con: If the poorest 5 billion people use the same resources per capita as the richest 2 billion, [not even 5 planet earths](http://bigthink.com/big-think-tv/hans-rosling-illustrates-future-energy-consumption-with-legos) will be enough. The effect of reducing population through abortion is insignificant when compared to the potential effects of changes in technology and lifestyles.
1.10.1.9.3. Con: The addition of extra human beings on the planet is not necessarily to the detriment of those already living. Indeed, a shortage of new human beings results in the state having less revenue, since there are less working- age tax payers. This makes it harder for the state to fund healthcare and [pensions](https://www.ft.com/content/49b3fcd4-63f9-11e6-a08a-c7ac04ef00aa) for all of its citizens.
1.10.1.9.4. Con: The amount of people using contraceptives, sterilizing themselves, and/or choosing not to have children will likely already lead to a slowing in population growth.
1.10.1.9.4.1. Pro: -> See 1.10.1.1.3.1.1.
1.10.1.9.5. Con: China has seen significant population [growth](http://www.worldometers.info/world-population/china-population/) recently, even with the one-child policy, yet is a [middle income](https://chinapower.csis.org/china-middle-class/) country.
1.10.1.9.5.1. Con: China has revoked the one child policy for parents who were both only children. These couples are now allowed to have two children.
1.10.1.9.5.2. Con: The one child policy has frequently been circumvented by simply paying a fine to be permitted to have more than one child.
1.10.1.9.6. Con: Population growth as a problem is [overstated](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FACK2knC08E).
1.10.1.10. Con: Abortion is not an effective tool for population control.
1.10.1.10.1. Con: Abortion would mean that people who accidentally become pregnant past the population limit would not be subject to any of the penal systems associated with that limit, or the pain of giving up a fully grown baby because government penalties forced them to.
1.10.1.10.2. Pro: If women are likely to have abortions regardless of whether it is legal or illegal, then the right to abortion doesn't prevent humans from passing some sort of environmental tipping point or carrying capacity.
1.10.1.10.3. Con: Abortion is one of many methods to aid in population control. As one-size-fits-all solutions rarely work effectively in complex systems, it is important to have many legal methods available.
1.10.1.10.4. Pro: The easiest way to stop population growth is to not have unprotected sex off birth control.
1.10.1.10.5. Pro: [It has been shown](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3709011) that widespread availability of abortion is not a sufficient condition to solve the problem of global population growth.
1.10.1.10.6. Pro: Assuming a carrying capacity exists, governments would impose birth limits. Abortion is a poor birth control method as it is reactive and not proactive.
1.10.1.10.7. Pro: Not enough people get abortions to have a meaningful impact on population size.
1.10.1.10.7.1. Pro: Abortion rates have been [decreasing](https://www.guttmacher.org/fact-sheet/induced-abortion-united-states) steadily over the past few decades in the US. Factors such as greater access to contraceptives have meant that fewer and fewer women use abortion.
1.10.1.10.7.1.1. Con: According to that source, 19 percent of pregnancies ended in abortion in 2014. That is almost 1 in 5. Just because they are decreasing doesn't mean "not enough people get abortions to have a meaningful impact on population size." Nineteen percent is a meaningful impact.
1.10.1.10.7.2. Con: Not having a child is the most significant thing an adult can do to reduce their carbon footprint. Every additional child a parent has will result in an extra [58 tonnes](https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2017/jul/12/want-to-fight-climate-change-have-fewer-children) of CO2 being emmitted per year.
1.10.2. Pro: Abortion is a necessary [public good](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2014/oct/14/abortion-right-to-privacy-women-right-to-equality) - it is good for everyone if women only have the children they want and can raise well.
1.10.2.1. Pro: Society has an interest in having a healthy and well educated population. Access to abortion supports that interest in avoiding unnecessary population growth and unwanted children.
1.10.2.2. Con: If raising only children a mother wants is a moral good, then for the logic to be consistent she must also be allowed to have legal access to infanticide when she does not want to raise a child. Wantedness is therefore not a justification for legalization of abortion.
1.10.2.3. Pro: When women cannot afford to raise their children they are forced to go on welfare, which is a cost to everyone.
1.10.2.3.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.2.4.5.
1.10.2.3.2. Con: Society is best when we look out for others and therefore supporting people, where needed, through welfare is not necessarily a bad thing.
1.10.2.3.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.10.4.2.2.2.
1.10.2.4. Pro: -> See 1.2.4.1.1.1.1.
1.10.2.5. Pro: Many women who become pregnant are still in high school and are [forced to drop out](http://www.ncsl.org/research/health/teen-pregnancy-affects-graduation-rates-postcard.aspx).
1.10.2.6. Pro: -> See 1.2.2.1.2.9.6.2.2.
1.10.2.7. Pro: Even if women are out of high school, unwanted pregnancy can force them to leave their jobs, furthering inequality in the workforce.
1.10.2.7.1. Con: Preference for equality in the workforce is not a satisfactory reason for abortion.  Many childless women are treated unequally in the workforce as it is.  We can strive for equality whilst also supporting childbearing.
1.10.2.7.1.1. Con: One of the reasons why women are treated unequally in the workforce is that employers assume women can get pregnant and leave their job any time. If we deny women the option to terminate unwanted pregnancies we further increase this perceived risk of them leaving their jobs due to pregnancy, which in turn encourages discrimination and confirms prejudices.
1.10.2.7.1.1.1. Pro: The option to have an abortion gives women more autonomy over their careers, as it allows them to plan ahead and discuss maternity leave with their employers before actually needing it.
1.10.2.7.1.2. Con: Giving women the right to have an abortion if they want to does not oppose or contradict support for childbearing. Allowing women a choice does not make anything compulsory.
1.10.2.8. Con: Just because a child isn't raised well or wanted doesn't mean the child doesn't have the right to life.
1.10.2.8.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.8.3.
1.10.2.8.2. Con: A harder life is often a life that will lead an individual to resort to crime, thus harming the quality of life of others.
1.10.2.8.2.1. Con: Then we should kill every poor person, because, since their life is hard, they could harm the quality of life of others. If humanity make life and death choices based on probability rather than heart and compassion, many innocent people will die.
1.10.2.9. Con: This would be true only if you exclude the unborn in the definition of "everyone".
1.10.2.10. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.1.1.1.
1.10.3. Pro: Everyone benefits if women are able to [commit](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2014/oct/14/abortion-right-to-privacy-women-right-to-equality) to work and education, without having to worry about getting derailed in life due to an unplanned pregnancy.
1.10.3.1. Con: Women do not have to have an abortion in order to achieve education and work related goals. Feminists should lobby the state to provide better day care facillitiies and welfare subsidies for mothers, instead of advocating for abortion rights.
1.10.3.1.1. Con: No amount of social support can negate the long-term difficulties that working or studying mothers have to face. It is unfair to suggest that better social support would make these women's lives as easy as those of childless women.
1.10.3.1.1.1. Pro: Parents in the US, on average, are less [happy](https://greatergood.berkeley.edu/article/item/july_newsletter_are_you_a_miserable_parent) than their childless counterparts.
1.10.3.1.2. Con: The two things are not mutually exclusive. One can advocate simultaneously for [economic, social and cultural rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic,_social_and_cultural_rights) and for[civil and political rights.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_and_political_rights)
1.10.3.1.3. Con: This implies that not having an abortion will work for every woman who is pursuing education or career goals.  Some women may carry a child to term and be successful with the extra work load.  Other women will find themselves unable to meet their goals while also giving a child the care that they need.  Whether a women has an abortion or not, they are still making sacrifices.
1.10.3.2. Pro: -> See 1.2.7.3.
1.10.3.3. Pro: Pregnancy will always have more of an impact on a woman than a man.  Pregnancy is a major medical condition that will limit their ability to work during and after the pregnancy.  Women make far greater sacrifices to become mothers than men, and that is a biological fact \(physically and emotionally\).  A man doesn't have to participate in the pregnancy, but can seek custody after the baby is born, which has it's own negative implications, particularly if the father is abusive.
1.10.3.4. Pro: Between 1970 and 1990 The Pill accounted for nearly three quarters of the increase in the number of women who became doctors and lawyers. The right to abortion contributed significantly to the same [phenomenon](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2014/oct/14/abortion-right-to-privacy-women-right-to-equality).
1.10.3.4.1. Con: A society has real reason to question its morality and values when social improvement can be counted and measured in the number of human lives lost.
1.10.3.4.1.1. Pro: The quality of society can be measured by its ability to support and preserve life
1.10.3.4.2. Con: The contraceptive pill is not the same as abortion. Any attempt to equate them is misleading and incorrect. Improved levels of education, increased demand for lawyers and doctors, changes in traditional beliefs that women should work, and TV shows depicting women doing more than just minding kids likely all contributed to an increase in women professionals too.
1.10.3.4.2.1. Con: The Pill and abortions are not equal, but in effect they complement each other - they give women the power to determine their readiness for reproduction.
1.10.3.4.2.2. Con: The Pill had a radical effect on society - it meant that for the first time in human history, women gained control of their sexuality. Single women have been having sex since the beginning of history, but it was only from the 1960s onwards that they were able to do this without the imminent threat of [pregnancy](http://edition.cnn.com/2010/OPINION/05/06/pogrebin.pill.roundup/index.html).
1.10.3.4.2.2.1. Con: The sexual liberation of any individual or social group, does not necessarily equate to true individual liberty or contribute towards social improvement.
1.10.3.4.2.3. Con: In the 1960s - when The Pill was introduced in the US - employers could \(without penalty\) fire a woman who got [pregnant](http://edition.cnn.com/2010/OPINION/05/06/pogrebin.pill.roundup/index.html).
1.10.3.4.2.4. Con: With The Pill, large numbers of college women could embark on careers that involved long-term, up-front time commitments in education and training as physicians, lawyers, veterinarians, managers, and academics, among others. A pregnancy could derail a career, but The Pill enabled women to stay on [track](http://edition.cnn.com/2010/OPINION/05/06/pogrebin.pill.roundup/index.html).
1.10.3.5. Con: The millions of humans who have their life taken by abortion do not benefit from it. Instead, they are deprived of the rest of their life. This is like saying killing newborns by the millions would benefit everyone. It conveniently leaves out the victims and therefore is incorrect.
1.10.3.6. Con: Free child care, more part-time roles, free access to online and distance education programs, encouraging men to raise children and other social programs, are all more favourable and beneficial ways to help women lead full and productive lives. Furthermore, there is no evidence that abortion provides any long or midterm social benefits to women, and there are physical and psychological risks for the woman associated with abortion.
1.10.4. Con: Social benefits should not be an important factor in decisions concerning life or death.
1.10.5. Pro: We live in a world of limited resources. As a society we will be better off resources are devoted to children who are raised and supported by parents with the means and interest in producing productive members of society.
1.10.5.1. Con: You can achieve this preventing pregnancy. It doesn't justify murdering.
1.10.6. Con: Murder is morally wrong. A woman isn't justified in killing a child for any reasons particularly her own 'social benefit. This claim is glib and insulting and makes it sound as murder is a gift to society that just keeps on giving!
1.10.6.1. Con: Roe v Wade determined that in the US a fetus is [not legally recognised](https://rewire.news/article/2013/01/03/fetal-personhood-laws-juridical-persons-are-not-natural-persons-and-why-it-matter/) as a person.
1.10.6.1.1. Con: As admitted in the article cited, the Supreme Court of the U.S. is not an infallible arbiter of who counts as a person with rights.
1.10.6.1.2. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.2.
1.10.6.1.3. Pro: The right to life is fundamental, but life begins at independent viability.
1.10.6.1.3.1. Con: Left to its own natural development a fetus will develop and be born. The externality of abortion changes this fact and therefore can only be considered killing/murder. For this reason any definition of life that begins with viability cannot be substantiated.
1.10.6.1.3.1.1. Con: There is no guarantee that a fetus 'left untouched' would develop into a baby. Regrettably, miscarriages may occur.
1.10.6.1.3.1.1.1. Pro: Miscarriages are remarkably common and as many as 1 in 4 pregnancies end in [miscarriage](https://www.tommys.org/our-organisation/charity-research/pregnancy-statistics/miscarriage).
1.10.6.1.3.1.1.1.1. Con: Since the above claim is under the "Life begins as conception" branch and its source says, we should research why miscarriage happens to "save lives and prevent future loss," it fits as a pro argument. If preventing miscarriage would save lives so would not aborting babies.
1.10.6.1.3.1.2. Con: This argument is [begging the question](https://yourlogicalfallacyis.com/begging-the-question). Calling the abortion of a fetus murder presupposes that the fetus is a life capable of being murdered. Asserting that life must begin before viability based on the declaration that terminating it is considered murder is circular reasoning.
1.10.6.1.3.2. Con: Just as it would be unethical to separate conjoined twins if only one had enough vital organs to survive, it is unethical to separate a fetus from his/her mother. Just as the 'non-viable' twin has a right to life supporting organs, so does the fetus.
1.10.6.1.3.2.1. Con: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.1.
1.10.6.1.3.2.2. Con: In the case of [parasitic conjoined twins](http://abcnews.go.com/International/story?id=82566&page=1), where the life of one twin would mean significant hardship or death for the other, parents are allowed to separate them, ending the life of the reliant twin. If this procedure is legal and ethical, then the choice to abort, when the fetus isn't even fully formed, should be.
1.10.6.1.3.2.2.1. Con: The unborn child is generally not in a parasitical relationship with the mother. While the unborn human does receive nutrients from the mother, the relationship is symbiotic both for the mother and [for the species](https://www.unicef.org/socialpolicy/index_53294.html). The mother receives [benefits](https://www.todaysparent.com/pregnancy/pregnancy-perks-the-health-benefits-for-mom/) such as reduced risk of breast and ovarian cancer, eventual reduction of period pain, higher estrogen levels, lower risk of MS, etc. The fetus [even 'donates' stem cells to the mom to treat problems like heart disease](https://www.newscientist.com/article/dn21185-fetus-donates-stem-cells-to-heal-mothers-heart/).
1.10.6.1.3.3. Con: Viability is one of the weaker arguments. A human on life-support isn't viable, but we still believe they are are human beings with rights.
1.10.6.1.3.3.1. Con: This obscures the order in which personhood is first attained. A human on life-support attains viability before losing it in this example.
1.10.6.1.3.3.2. Con: Life support is legally allowed to be turned off meaning they lack an absolute right to life.
1.10.6.1.3.4. Con: Independent viability is a moveable target, so irrelevant to the ethics of life and value. No one is 'viable' in an environment contrary to the needs of survival, such as a child in the ocean or an adult in the vacuum of space.
1.10.6.1.3.4.1. Pro: Future technology may be able to develop an artificial womb or incubation method as an alternative to pregnancy.  This means what is "viable" is partially dependent upon current technology and doesn't ultimately answer the question.
1.10.6.1.3.5. Con: Humans are not dead pre-birth and alive post-birth. Birth doesn't mark the beginning of life, development, or growth, but rather the passage of a human life from the womb to the outside world, and from receiving nutrients via the placenta to eating/breathing with the digestive system and lungs, respectively.
1.10.6.1.3.5.1. Con: Considering a fetus a human life just before birth is almost irrelevant to the abortion discussion, when [less than 1% of abortions are done after the 21st week.](https://www.guttmacher.org/evidence-you-can-use/later-abortion)
1.10.6.1.3.6. Pro: When a fetus is able to exist independently from the mother's body they can be considered to be independent living beings. At this stage they are not reliant on someone to maintain their life, which makes them more independent.
1.10.6.1.3.6.1. Pro: -> See 1.10.6.1.3.2.2.
1.10.6.1.3.6.2. Con: The major difference between an unborn baby and baby is the degree to which they rely on someone else. Everyone relies on other people to survive. Embracing this fact would make people less selfish, and less lonely.
1.10.6.1.3.6.3. Con: When people become incredibly sick and are dependent on machines or other people to keep them alive, we still consider them to be living beings.
1.10.6.1.3.6.4. Con: An infant is not independent of his mother post-birth, and will die if exposed or not given food, etc. Independence, then, is not a reason one life is more valuable than another.
1.10.6.1.3.6.4.1. Con: While an infant requires care by an adult, the ability for the infant to remain alive is not dependent on being physically attached to an adult at all times. In this way, it is still significantly more independent than pre-birth.
1.10.6.1.3.7. Con: -> See 1.10.6.1.3.6.4.
1.10.6.1.3.8. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.25.3.
1.10.6.1.3.9. Con: Even though a fetus cannot necessarily exist outside a mother's body immediately, it is a living being with the potential to live a full life and therefore should be protected.
1.10.6.1.3.9.1. Con: The potential to have a full life does not guarantee that the life should be protected. A person dying of kidney failure still has the potential for full life, but that does not grant them the right to risk the life of someone else by demanding a kidney transplant. In the same way, a fetus with the potential for full life cannot demand the use of the mothers body because pregnancy risks the mothers life.
1.10.6.1.3.9.1.1. Con: This is not a very good example. The person dying of kidney failure is not being euthanized, but is receiving all the medical treatment needed to maintain the best quality life possible until their natural death. Pregnancies that risk the mothers life are an entirely different argument.
1.10.6.1.3.9.1.2. Con: This argument may be valid for risky pregnancies, but not for the unrestricted right to abortion, since most pregnancies do not present imminent risk.
1.10.6.1.3.9.2. Pro: Allowing abortions means allowing people to end potential lives, removing all future possibilities of this being existing and having their own desires and wants.
1.10.6.1.3.9.2.1. Con: By that argument no woman could turn down sex or use a contraceptive.
1.10.6.1.3.9.2.2. Con: It's philosophically untenable for a 3rd party to make an argument for just one of another person's potential futures, against that person's own interest. Almost anything could conceivably prevent almost anything else in the future; it's called the [butterfly effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Butterfly_effect). A woman might have 2 children after a few years, but only if she weren't already having a child this year.
1.10.6.1.3.9.3. Pro: The rights of an unborn child should not be seen as less valid than the rights of a deceased grandparent. Pre-natal rights are very analogous to funeral rights — where the subject's current rights, and status of life are largely immaterial in view of the potential exercise of rights before they were deceased.  This is not meaningfully different than the potential exercise of rights after birth.
1.10.6.1.3.9.4. Con: The vast majority of conceptions fail, either due to miscarriage or because the fertilised egg never implants in the uterus. Human reproduction is just too inefficient to consider conception the beginning of even a potential life.
1.10.6.1.3.9.5. Pro: A baby in the womb isn't just a ball of [tissue](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=RDmwPGrZkYs). Even if it is only considered potential for human life, it still has value.
1.10.6.1.3.9.6. Pro: Even if the fetus is not "human" in the sense that it looks, walks, and talks like us, the fetus has potentiality. Left untouched, it will develop naturally into a person.
1.10.6.1.3.9.6.1. Con: -> See 1.10.6.1.3.1.1.
1.10.6.1.3.9.6.2. Pro: As soon as fertilization takes place, it's unclear at what point conscious life begins for the baby. It is clear that there is no conscious life before fertilization and that there is after. Because of this it would be unethical to take a life from a possible conscious being.
1.10.6.1.3.9.6.3. Con: A fetus left untouched would immediately fail and never grow into a human. A mother has to touch the fetus with her uterus and an umbilical cord.
1.10.6.1.3.9.6.4. Pro: Someone who is in a temporary coma is not conscious or actively alive, but we acknowledge they have rights because they are going to wake up.
1.10.6.1.3.9.6.4.1. Con: People in comas do not need to live inside a human being, and if they did, you would definitely be allowed to take them out.
1.10.6.1.3.9.6.4.2. Con: It is implicitly understood that with few exceptions, people in comas had previously demonstrated their intent and ability to continue living.
1.10.6.1.3.9.6.5. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.11.
1.10.6.1.3.9.6.6. Con: Leaving the fetus in the womb is not the same as leaving it "untouched". At multiple stages fetus requires assistance from the mothers body or it will cease to develop and quickly die. The assistance from the mothers womb is "touching" the fetus.
1.10.6.1.3.9.6.7. Con: "Untouched" implies that the womb is a stagnant, independent environment for the fetus to grow. The womb has a constant influx of energy and nutrients, and constant efflux of wastes. The above claim ignores - or even dehumanizes - the woman's role in providing the nutrients and receiving the wastes.
1.10.6.1.3.9.7. Pro: Abortion takes away any future experiences \(good and bad\) from a baby that was meant to be born. While you might not consider abortion to be same as murder, the same thing that is wrong with abortion is wrong with murder. Killing somebody is not wrong because their heart stops or they stop to think, but because they lose their future selves.
1.10.6.1.3.9.7.1. Con: The concept of a baby being "meant to be born" can as easily be rephrased as "not meant to be born" and abortion being just the tool to achieve this. For a thing to be meant to happen, there has to be something higher that is meaning for it to happen. Unless that something shares with us what it wants and what it does not, using this sort of argument does not make sense. Provided that [something higher even exists](https://www.kialo.com/the-existence-of-god-2629), of course.
1.10.6.1.3.9.7.1.1. Con: In this line of thinking all murder is ok. You could just say a person is not meant to be alive and murder is the vehicle to do so. All murder would be acceptable under this thinking because life is meaningless without a higher power.
1.10.6.1.3.9.8. Con: It is also true that all eggs and sperm could form to create potential lives. If it is determined that potential lives should therefore be protected, an extreme version of this argument would be that people should not use contraception as then they are stopping potential lives from coming to fruition.
1.10.6.1.3.9.8.1. Con: Though eggs and sperm are living beings, there is no science claiming that they are specifically human beings already. The protection of potential life refers to the future of already human beings, not pre-human organisms.
1.10.6.1.3.9.9. Con: If potential to live a full life is the sine qua non for legal protection, such legal protections would not extend to those with congenital abnormalities that would deny them the potential for a full life. Furthermore, the meaning of "full life" is ambiguous, does it mean a long life, or a personally fulfilling life, or a life full of normal experiences? How this is defined might not protect a fetus that would be born under different racial, ethnic, religious, and socio-economic circumstances.
1.10.6.1.4. Con: When this was determined, ultrasonography was not widely used in America to see images of babies in the [womb](https://www.livescience.com/32071-history-of-fetal-ultrasound.html). These images allow us to see their development and early human form. Also, we have since made significant advancements in [genomics](https://www.yourgenome.org/facts/timeline-history-of-genomics) allowing us to see that babies in the womb are genetically human beginning at [conception](http://www.latimes.com/science/sciencenow/la-sci-sn-genes-human-embryo-development-20150903-story.html). Further, we have made progress in the ability to keep premature babies [alive](http://www.radiolab.org/story/update-23-weeks-6-days/). These scientific advancements warrant a reconsideration of the Roe v Wade decision.
1.10.6.1.5. Con: The law does not necessarily always reflect what should be the case. Morally, one can still argue that a fetus should be recognised as a person.
1.10.6.1.5.1. Pro: If laws were always moral, there wouldn't be any reason to ask for a change in the law.
1.10.6.1.6. Con: While fetuses may not be considered people, the law has still given them rights in certain situations.
1.10.6.1.6.1. Pro: If an embryo in the uterus is not a human being and someone punches a woman in the stomach and she has a miscarriage they can only be charged with the simple assault of punching her in the stomach.
1.10.6.1.6.2. Pro: Some states have held women [criminally liable](https://legal-dictionary.thefreedictionary.com/Fetal+Rights) for using illegal drugs that harm the fetus, therefore recognising that the fetus does have some right to not be harmed.
1.10.6.1.6.3. Pro: [Fetal protection policies](https://legal-dictionary.thefreedictionary.com/Fetal+Rights) were used to bar women from working in roles that could cause harm to embryos or fetuses.
1.10.6.1.6.3.1. Con: The [US Supreme Court](https://legal-dictionary.thefreedictionary.com/Fetal+Rights) determined that such policies were a form of sexual discrimination which violated the Civil Rights Act.
1.10.6.1.6.4. Pro: The [Unborn Victims of Violence Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unborn_Victims_of_Violence_Act) recognises fetuses as legal victims if they are injured or killed as the result of a federal crime of violence.
1.10.6.1.7. Pro: Numerous attempts have been made to pass [personhood laws](https://rewire.news/legislative-tracker/law-topic/personhood/) in the US, which would classify zygotes, embryos and fetuses as persons, but such attempts have had little success.
1.10.6.1.7.1. Pro: If even the cells and ingredients of a pregnancy were given personhood, then every masturbation would be genocide.
1.10.6.1.7.1.1. Con: There is no scientific basis to give personhood to the gametes of any of the two sexes. Neither of them is a totipotent cell, with the potentiality to become human beings on their own.
1.10.6.1.7.2. Con: That they have had little success doesn't mean that they are wrong.
1.11. Con: Life begins at conception. Abortion therefore violates the right to life of the fetus.
1.11.1. Con: The same way an egg is not a new-born chicken, a fetus can't be considered a human life. Humans are the only species with the right to life: the fetus is more an object of right than a subject of right. Therefore, it is the decision of the owner \[the mother in this case\] what happens with the object.
1.11.1.1. Con: Most people are comfortable killing chickens. The analogy, therefore, falls apart at the point where its not as if people are comfortable killing one but not the other.
1.11.1.2. Con: [A human life begins at conception](https://www.kialo.com/should-women-have-the-right-to-choose-abortion-5637/5637.0=5637.1-5637.2+5637.371). A gallus gallus domesticus \(chicken\) living organism begins at the fertilization of the egg. Both start out as embryos.

The infant stage of a human being begins at birth. The chick stage of a chicken begins after hatching. Eventually the human will reach the adult stage if it doesn't die, and the chick will reach the adult chicken stage as a hen or rooster.

There are many stages of development, but it is the same living organism from conception until death.
1.11.1.3. Con: In cases where a guardian is appointed to decide what happens to another human, such as in cases of small children or the elderly with medical issues, the societal hope is that the  guardian will decide in the best interests of the other human, not act out of self-concern.
1.11.1.4. Con: A chicken egg is analogous to a human woman's unfertilized egg. There is little debate that neither constitutes a person. A more apt argument would reference a fertilized chicken egg, relating it to a chicken, and not referencing the stages of gestation process.
1.11.1.5. Con: A baby is not an adult neither. Following this argument, it could be concluded that adults are subjects of right while babies are objects of right owned by their parents. Perceived differences between a fetus and a baby \(or a baby and an adult\) should not be the criteria to decide which one is object of right and which one is subject of right.
1.11.1.5.1. Pro: Such logic would make infanticide legal and morally acceptable.
1.11.2. Con: While life arguably begins at conception, "life" is technically present in insects and bacteria, both of which we kill billions of every day without any moral dilemma. What makes the life of humans and some animals different is consciousness, and fetuses don't have the structures which science sees as responsible for consciousness.
1.11.2.1. Con: Infants don't begin to show signs of consciousness until [about 5 months](http://www.sciencemag.org/news/2013/04/when-does-your-baby-become-conscious), and aren't considered to be conscious in the same manner as adults are. As such, the scientific determination of lack of consciousness can't be a valid reason to terminate a human life.
1.11.2.1.1. Con: The issue is not that lack of consciousness is a reason to destroy something, but that the cost of destroying something that lacks a consciousness is not a reason to injure someone who has one.
1.11.2.1.2. Pro: Infanticide \(including of prematurely-born viable babies\) is illegal in almost all jurisdictions \(including the entirety of the USA and EU\) and a late-term fetus is negligibly different than a newborn infant. A society’s law should be philosophically consistent.
1.11.2.1.3. Pro: Insofar as morality may be inferred from longstanding and near-universal consensus, the fact that infanticide \(from birth\) is both illegal and abhorred almost everywhere is evidence that it is immoral to kill humans even at ages younger than the supposed “consciousness” milestone referenced here.
1.11.2.2. Con: Many animals are [conscious in a similar manner to humans,](https://www.psychologytoday.com/blog/animal-emotions/201208/scientists-conclude-nonhuman-animals-are-conscious-beings) yet are sometimes killed for food for humans. They also may kill other animals. Consciousness, then, is not a good deciding factor for who or what may be killled.
1.11.2.2.1. Con: The fact that those things do happen does not mean that they ought to happen.
1.11.2.2.1.1. Con: The majority of all human societies on Earth throughout recorded history have been primarily omnivores and not vegetarian or vegan. This does indicate that the killing of animals for food is not ethically wrong, and is not considered morally wrong by the vast majority of humans.
1.11.2.2.1.1.1. Con: Society seems to be moving in the direction of trying to avoid animal cruelty and reduce harm done to animals, with an increasing population wanting not to hurt them at all. This indicates that hurting or killing animals is considered morally wrong to the extent that there must be at least some utility gained from doing it.
1.11.2.2.1.1.1.1. Con: In countries like the U.S., most claimed vegetarians  [actually eat meat](https://www.psychologytoday.com/blog/animals-and-us/201109/why-are-there-so-few-vegetarians).
1.11.2.2.1.1.1.1.1. Con: The nutrients and pleasure gained by eating meat represent a utility gain, and thus do not contradict the claim that animals are considered to have nonzero value.
1.11.2.2.1.1.1.2. Pro: A [survey of Americans](http://www.aspca.org/sites/default/files/public_memo_aspca_farm_animal_research_ag_gag.pdf) found that the majority support investigating farms to expose animal abuse.
1.11.2.2.1.1.1.3. Pro: [A Canadian poll conducted by Mercy for Animals](http://vancouversun.com/news/local-news/majority-of-canadians-oppose-animal-cruelty-would-pay-more-at-the-grocery-store-to-ensure-welfare) shows that 86% say they would be willing to pay more for chicken meat if it meant that chickens would be treated humanely.
1.11.2.2.1.1.1.3.1. Con: Whether or not they would support more humane treatment of the chicken in life, note that they still support the chicken being killed and eaten. This, then, is not a support for consciousness being the deciding factor in what a human may choose to kill or not.
1.11.2.2.1.1.2. Pro: In 2010 the world's population was 6.9 billion and the estimated number of vegetarians by choice, not necessity, was 75 million. That's 1.09% of the world's population that believes it is morally wrong to eat meat.
1.11.2.2.2. Con: That conscious beings are considered unimportant \(or less important than people are\) does not imply that non-conscious objects are as important as people are. One could hold that having a consciousness is a requirement for having intrinsic value but that some animals/humans/AIs have more value than others.
1.11.2.3. Con: Recent evidence supports the theory that [insects are conscious.](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/science/insects-are-conscious-claims-major-paper-that-could-show-us-how-our-own-thoughts-began-a7002151.html)
1.11.2.4. Pro: If we include the ability to experience happiness and suffering in the concept of "being conscious", then the argument is valid. Science understands that at least some degree of complexity \(e.g. neurological networks\) is required for this. An early-stage fetus without the necessary bodily systems cannot experience such things. In that sense, an early-stage fetus is not conscious - just like bacteria aren't.
1.11.2.4.1. Con: Unlike bacteria, fetuses have the potential for consciousness. In our decisions about terminating life we should consider 'prospective consciousness' as much as existing consciousness, as having moral value.
1.11.2.4.1.1. Con: Science has not found conclusively that bacteria are not conscious, and evidence points to [the possibility that they are.](http://www.biowars.com/blog/are-bacteria-conscious-beings/)
1.11.2.5. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.12.6.
1.11.2.6. Con: Particularly in the U.S. Constitution, human rights are considered "inherent," rather than dependant on traits or values. See the Declaration of Independence: "all men are created equal" and "inalienable rights" are operant phrases in defining why we have rights. A fetus may not be conscious or have the ability to make moral decisions, but this does not negate the fact that it is alive and human.
1.11.2.6.1. Con: In the constitution, these rights are innumerated. Among them, life, liberty, and the pursuit of happiness. Allowing government to make this choice for an individual is both a violation of one’s liberty and their pursuit of happiness. In certain medical scenarios, the life of the mother may be at stake, and an abortion ban would violate her right to life, as well.
1.11.2.6.1.1. Con: The Declaration of Independence, not the Constitution states that natural law gives us the right to life. The Constitution doesn't cover right to life, generally, only in specific, limited instances, so there is not a Constitutional guarantee of right to life.
1.11.2.6.1.2. Pro: Forced Birthing Demanders normalize violence against women. For a democratic society where we are all entitled to life, liberty and the pursuit of happiness women must be honored and respected as the Life Givers not as the Life Bearers without personal agency. Women have used abortificants for thousands of years. They have the fundamental human right to object to any set of cells growing in their body.
1.11.2.6.2. Con: The U.S. Constitution is irrelevant here. It applies only to people with rights; whether a fetus belongs to that group is at question in this thread.
1.11.2.6.2.1. Con: The Constitution is irrelevant but not for the reason stated. It's irrelevant because all people have rights whether the Constitution acknowledges them or not.  That's the definition of "inalienable rights." Therefore, the phrase "people with rights" is redundant. It's just "people".  Whether a fetus is "people" is at question in this thread.
1.11.2.7. Con: Comparing a fetus to any other life form is useless because it is widely accepted that it is okay to kill animals and insects. Abortion is immoral because this is human life we are considering and the belief that human life is worth defending and honoring is an integral part of our western civilization.
1.11.2.7.1. Con: It is not widely accepted, but rather a dividing factor, that the life of a fetus is equal to the life of a born human. It is not culturally set in stone that the life of a fetus should be defended and honored to the same degree. The comparison to other life forms is therefore not a useless one to make since it points out that there is nothing morally wrong in itself to valuing various forms of life differently.
1.11.2.8. Pro: A single zygote can split into two or more zygotes. Humans cannot split into two or more humans. Similarly, two zygotes can fuse together to become one zygote. Two humans cannot fuse together to become one human. Zygote life is profoundly different from human life.
1.11.2.9. Con: [Article 3](http://www.un.org/en/universal-declaration-human-rights/) of the Universal Declaration of Human Rights does not apply to insects and bacteria. It also makes no requirement of the conscious state of a human, otherwise we could legally kill anyone in a coma.
1.11.2.9.1. Con: People in a coma once had consciousness, while zygotes never did.
1.11.2.10. Con: However, science is conflicted about when a fetus develops consciousness. They have all the needed traits [for consciousness](https://medlineplus.gov/ency/article/002398.htm) \(a brain, nervous system etc\) by 16 weeks and are also known to experience sounds.
1.11.2.11. Con: The above suggestion makes an unqualified assertion that consciousness, or sentience, or any other capability of brain function for that matter, is what gives an organism's life meaning and significance. The pros need to offer a reason for why life should not be respected in and of itself.

1.11.5. Pro: Human life is extremely valuable and therefore should be protected from the moment it begins.
1.11.5.1. Pro: No civilized society permits one human to intentionally harm or take the life of another human without punishment, and abortion is no different.

1.11.5.1.1.1. Con: The purpose of the military is generally to protect life, and service in the Military is a choice. Abortion does not compare to military, as the fetus is incapable of consenting to self-sacrifice, and in the overwhelming majority of cases there is no life being protected.
1.11.5.1.2. Con: This is not true. Many societies permit humans to end the life of another. For example, euthanasia is legal in many states. Similarly, doctors are often permitted to end the lives of patients who are on life support.
1.11.5.1.2.1. Con: Nazi Germany was one such society. Their euthanasia program targeted mentally and physically disabled patients living in institutional settings and predated the Holocaust by approximately two years. It aimed to eliminate what eugenicists and their supporters considered "life unworthy of life".
1.11.5.1.2.1.1. Con: The fact that euthanasia has been used by dictators in problematic ways does not undermine the fact that there are a number of states and countries that now have legal euthanasia which many people consider to be legitimate.
1.11.5.1.2.1.2. Pro: This was legal and considered to be perfectly legitimate by many people and a good solution to what they considered to be a problem.
1.11.5.1.2.2. Con: Euthanasia and patients on life support are only killed when there is next to zero chance that the person will survive, and are still outlawed in many countries because there is still great debate on whether or not they are considered ethical. By contrast, unborn children have a near certain chance of survival with modern technology.
1.11.5.1.2.2.1. Con: -> See 1.10.6.1.3.1.1.1.
1.11.5.1.3. Pro: There cannot be any dispute whatsoever that the fetus that a human woman is pregnant with is a human also, and a member of the human species is defined as a human being. Regardless of a "persons" \(a human and an individual\) age they are still of the human species and biologically different and unique from the mother and have life, these are scientific proven facts.
1.11.5.1.3.1. Con: The single aspect undisputed is only that during pregnancy a "human infant" is developing inside a woman's womb. The neural tube doesn't even start developing for the first six [weeks](https://www.plannedparenthood.org/learn/pregnancy/pregnancy-month-by-month/what-happens-second-month-pregnancy). The definition of life is heavily disputed, but if you're using the direct [definition](https://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/life), an infant in the womb could only be considered living at [18 weeks](https://www.healthline.com/health/pregnancy/when-can-a-fetus-hear#1) old as that is when the first sense allows them to be the bare minimum responsive.
1.11.5.1.4. Pro: At [least 38 US states have fetal homicide statutes](http://www.ncsl.org/research/health/fetal-homicide-state-laws.aspx). If it is illegal to cause the death of the baby in utero for someone other than the mother, then it follows that it should be illegal for the mother as well.
1.11.5.1.4.1. Con: The current laws of states are irrelevant; this discussion aims to decide whether those laws are ethical.
1.11.5.1.5. Con: Taking life for self-preservation and self-defense are permissible in many civilized societies. The woman who becomes pregnant is required to sacrifice her own nutrition, energy, and bodily space for the growth and existence of a fetus, which could put her own life and well-being at risk. Therefore the woman may choose to preserve herself and not make that sacrifice.
1.11.5.2. Pro: If people view children's death due to illness, accident, or them being killed as a tragedy, it shouldn't be different when a child's life is lost through abortion.
1.11.5.3. Pro: The moral justification for abortion is not compatible with the intrinsic value of human life. It is widely accepted human life post-birth is of immense intrinsic value, and yet before birth this is less so. It is hard to identify an objective difference between born and in-born babies that provides a satisfying justification for this distinction.
1.11.5.3.1. Con: Even under optimal circumstances there is a high rate of miscarriage, which is not morally equivalent to killing. Unborn babies are a potential life, with a nonzero chance of not living when born.
1.11.5.4. Pro: The question of allowing abortion isn't merely a question of destroying lives that already exist. It's about the worth of bringing a human life into existence. Bringing a human life into existence is worth the cost: from the loss of comfort, to the loss of our dreams, even to the loss of our lives. To accept abortion as a valid option is to accept that these things are more valuable than the creation of human life itself.
1.11.5.4.1. Con: The net effect of abortion may increase the number of human lives. Women can have more babies later, making the choice of abortion about whether to have a child now or the future, not a choice between life and no life.
1.11.5.4.2. Con: Circumstances matter. If child is to be introduced to a world where its early years might be severely negatively affected due to various circumstances \(which are often priors for the act of abortion\), then not only does the quality of life of that child suffer, but [as shown by numerous factors](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2708328/), humans brought up in bad environments are much more likely to have negative societal impact. The claim about the "worth" of a human life cannot be generalized.
1.11.5.5. Con: People hold different views about when the right to life begins. As such, abortion should remain a personal choice but be accessible to those who wish to access it.
1.11.5.5.1. Con: Years ago, people held different views about whether persons of color and women were people. As such, it follows from your argument that slavery and sexual slavery should have remained a personal choice but be accessible to those who wish to access it. Precautionary principle indicates that if something might harm human lives, then it should be avoided unless certain that it does not harm any human life.
1.11.5.5.2. Pro: There can never be consensus on life being sacred or not from the moment of conception. So what are legislators to do? We can be as polite as we can to the pro life viewpoint but if the achievement of banning abortion is what happens after a political campaign you have one group in society exercising power another group. Better for the state to back off. Let people who disagree with abortion teach their own followers their values and leave it at that.
1.11.5.5.3. Pro: If a gestating human holds the view that life begins at conception, and the mother holds the view that life begins some other time and aborts the gestating human, the human’s rights have been infringed in the eyes of them, but not in the eyes of the mother. This raises a confusing paradox. As such, it’s most likely the case that personal preference has little bearing when deciding whether a gestating human lives or dies.
1.11.5.5.3.1. Con: If one mother holds the view that her life is of value but another mother holds the view that the 1st mother's life isn't worth living and kills her, the 1st mother's rights have been infringed in the eyes of them but not in the eyes of the 2nd mother. This would not be considered a confusing paradox. As such, it is the case that personal preference has no legal baring in deciding whether one human lives or dies.
1.11.5.5.4. Con: Two hunters may have differing views of whether a movement in the bushes is a deer or another hunter. The right course of action in that case as well as this one is to determine with certainty if the target is or is not a person deserving the right to life before taking that life away.
1.11.5.5.5. Pro: Not everyone who gets pregnant will choose an abortion. The question is about control--just because some don't get abortions doesn't mean that nobody should be allowed to. Just because some do get abortions doesn't mean that everyone should have to.
1.11.5.5.6. Pro: The question of the right to choose is a moral/ethical question, not a question of law. Thus, whether or not one believes morally or ethically that a woman should abort a child, ultimately the decision is tested by the moral and ethical beliefs of said woman. The law cannot dictate individual morals and ethics, and thus cannot stand in the way of the right to choose.
1.11.5.5.7. Pro: By making abortion legal, then both pro-life and pro-choice positions are supported. Each person will have the freedom to decide according to their own beliefs. Laws, at least in a secular democracy like United States, should consider the rights of all people. Making it legal respects both sides.
1.11.5.5.8. Con: Choosing is a mental process, not a right. Every human that can think has the ability to choose anything always. No one has the right to choose anything always, because there is no such thing as a right to choose anything always.[youtube.com](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JGsrrR9uCbE)
1.11.5.5.9. Pro: Many scientists would state that they still [do not know](http://www.slate.com/articles/double_x/doublex/2017/04/when_does_life_begin_outside_the_christian_right_the_answer_is_over_time.html) when life begins, as there are many landmark moments such as the development of the spine and brain. As a result, it could be seen that a fetus goes on a gradual process to personhood.
1.11.5.5.9.1. Con: Even if a fetus is only potential for human life, it still has [value.](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=48PMlt2vTRA)
1.11.5.5.10. Con: Scientific literature is [conclusive](https://www.princeton.edu/~prolife/articles/embryoquotes2.html) on the "humanness" of an unborn human fetus at the moment of conception.

1.11.5.5.10.3. Con: "Human" in scientific terms refers to the species of embryo, and is not markedly different from using the term to define the species of sperm, oocyte, stem cell, DNA sample, tissue sample, organ, etc. Fetus refers to the growing organism after approximately 8 weeks. Prior to 8 weeks, the proper terms are zygote, blastula, and embryo.
1.11.5.5.10.3.1. Con: It is markedly different. While one can say human sperm to describe sperm, no one can correctly say the sperm is a human. The sperm has only half the genetic information needed to be considered human. You can say human zygote to describe zygote but also could call the zygote a human in its earliest stage of development. It has all the genetic information and is following it, beginning to grow. All that is necessary for life. A DNA sample and the other examples also don't grow and develop.
1.11.5.5.10.4. Con: Skin cells and fertilized human egg cells are equally "human", yet no one mourns dead skin cells. The issue is "personhood", not the species or DNA of the cells involved.
