1.11.5.6. Con: You're making a claim that you do not and can not substantiate. There is no support for the conclusion that human life is so valuable.
1.11.6. Con: -> See 1.11.5.5.
1.11.7. Pro: The US government has a constitutional obligation to protect the lives and liberties of it's citizens. A fetus' heart can be heard within the first month, therefore those constitutional rights should be afforded to that individual.
1.11.7.1. Con: The right to life is not absolute.
1.11.7.1.1. Pro: All rights require the consent of a society to be applied/protected and there is no consensus in society on this issue.
1.11.7.1.1.1. Con: Many rights are intrinsic to every individual human and require absolutely no societal agreement.
1.11.7.1.1.2. Con: Basic individual rights, such as the right to life, exist independent of popular opinion and should never be subject to a public vote. The only issue society can decide is whether or not it will respect and protect those rights.
1.11.7.1.2. Con: The only exceptions to the universality of the right to life are those in which the person to be killed has committed some wrong, either to his own nation or to another. A baby has done no moral wrong worthy of punishment by death.
1.11.7.1.2.1. Con: There are many cases in which people who have done no wrong are denied a right to life. The court's interpretation of the [4th Amendment](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fourth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution), since [Graham v. Connor](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graham_v._Connor#), and the [Stand-your-ground laws](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stand-your-ground_law) enacted in many states, both justify the use of lethal force in the event someone feels threatened—even if they aren't actually being threatened and/or they caused the situation that made them feel threatened in the first place. The victims of this force are innocent, but society condones their killing.
1.11.7.1.2.1.1. Con: These "victims" are not always innocent. In the context of the original argument, a baby/fetus usually does not present a legitimate threat to the life of the mother. When it does, possible exceptions can be considered.
1.11.7.1.3. Pro: Murder is not always unethical. Murder in times of war is considered lawful, and soldiers who commit such acts cannot be prosecuted. Abortion is arguably an act of self-defense on the part of the woman, and is therefore analogous to the acts of soldiers in wartime.
1.11.7.1.3.1. Con: If a military member violates any of the governing laws of war, laws of armed conflict, rules of engagement, or escalation of force then they should be prosecuted for murder. Police departments have a homicide investigative detail to ascertain whether a homicide is a crime i.e. manslaughter or murder. Separation of homicide, which is not a crime, and murder, which is, is very important in this case.
1.11.7.1.3.2. Con: This argument still does not justify abortion, it only says that one would be philosophically inconsistent to believe abortion were wrong but war were okay. That does not answer the question of whether or not abortion is justified.
1.11.7.1.3.3. Con: Many anti-abortion advocates are also anti-war. Most Americans would justify military action only in self-defense, while 99% of aborted children pose no threat to their mothers.
1.11.7.1.3.4. Con: We do not allow a free pass for soldiers to kill innocents. There are many examples of soldiers being convicted of war crimes for such acts, In most societies, soldiers act under strict rules of engagement designed to protect innocents, non-combatants and combatants who are wounded or captured.
1.11.7.1.3.5. Con: The adjective 'murder' does not apply to official combatants killing opposing soldiers in wartime. To be classified as murder, there needs to be [prior intention to kill one specific victim](http://criminal.findlaw.com/criminal-charges/homicide-definition.html), and [no legal excuse or authority.](https://legal-dictionary.thefreedictionary.com/murder)
1.11.7.1.3.5.1. Con: Then abortion is not murder if there is no malicious intent and it is predominantly legal.
1.11.7.1.3.5.1.1. Con: The definition of malice aforethought is prior intention to kill one \(or more\) specific victims. E.G. to kill Joe, not to kill a random enemy soldier. Abortion \(save pills taken when not sure if one is with child or not\) has the goal of terminating one specific victim.
1.11.7.1.3.5.1.1.1. Con: By this definition, targeting a high-ranking officer of an enemy during wartime would be murder.
1.11.7.1.3.5.1.1.1.1. Pro: Assassination is generally considered [a type of murder](http://www.differencebetween.info/difference-between-murder-and-assassination) with a political motivation. It is "[murder](https://legal-dictionary.thefreedictionary.com/assassination) committed by a perpetrator without the personal provocation of the victim."
1.11.7.1.3.5.1.1.1.2. Con: That assassination is a form of murder because it targets a specific person would support the point that abortion is murder because it targets a specific person - not oppose the point.
1.11.7.1.3.5.1.2. Con: A 'legal excuse or authority' to justify a killing would be self defense in view of an immediate violent threat, or other [justifiable homicide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justifiable_homicide), or due process in a court of law such as a judge sentencing a criminal to death.
1.11.7.1.3.5.2. Con: Even the source referenced affirms that prior mens rea, \(pre-meditation and guilty-mind\), is not a necessary requirement to be guilty of murder.  Only the "first degree" of murder, according to this definition, requires pre-meditation, which is likely not universal among all societies.
1.11.7.1.3.6. Pro: Murder is acceptable when one is defending oneself and one's autonomy. Soldiers must kill or else they will captured, injured or killed by the enemy. Likewise, mothers who bear unwanted children lose their bodily autonomy, freedom, and sometimes their health.
1.11.7.1.3.6.1. Con: That comparison only works in cases of rape and when the woman's life is in risk. Presence of someone unwanted isn't the same as occupation. If that were the case, you should be allowed to kill a born unwanted child regardless of its age as raising a child make you lose the same qualities.
1.11.7.1.3.6.1.1. Con: You might lose some of those qualities but not all. The deciding factor is the possibility of your death, which isn't given post birth.
1.11.7.1.3.6.2. Con: Serving as the caregiver to a spouse with Alzheimer's also threatens one's health and freedom, yet killing one's spouse in order to restore one's freedom or protect one's health is considered murder.
1.11.7.1.3.6.2.1. Con: The above claim is logically irrelevant. The spouse does not live inside the body of the caregiver in this example, and technically the caregiver can simply walk away \(though the morality of that would be a separate argument entirely\).
1.11.7.1.3.7. Con: The killing that soldiers do is a necessity for the survival of the state during a time of war. It is killing to protect life, which is a necessary prerequisite for all other rights. Abortion has no such necessity.
1.11.7.1.3.7.1. Con: In most wars, the goal is not to kill the enemy population, but to take control of it. As such, the soldier is not really protecting life, he's just protecting the government of said life.
1.11.7.1.4. Pro: Governments do not do everything they can to ensure that people remain alive for as long as possible, which they should if the right to life is absolute and fundamental.
1.11.7.1.4.1. Pro: Governments do not put all of their money into healthcare and medical research to allow people to live as long as possible.
1.11.7.1.4.2. Pro: Governments do not make it a requirement of people to donate organs even though this would mean being able to save many people's lives.
1.11.7.1.4.3. Pro: There is an action/inaction distinction, such that consequences can be morally reprehensible if they come from inaction. Yet, the government chooses to spend money on things other than charity.
1.11.7.1.4.4. Con: The 'right to life' is not the same as 'the right to be kept alive for as long as possible'. It only means that a human has the right to live, and should not be killed by another human being.
1.11.7.1.5. Pro: Capital punishment is still [legal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital_punishment_by_country) in a number of countries, and in a number of US states. This shows that at times the state condones the ending of life, meaning the right is not absolute.
1.11.7.1.5.1. Con: The removal of rights after due process is never the case with abortion. The gestating human has either done nothing to warrant the removal of their rights, or does not even possess such rights. Capital punishment has no bearing on the abortion discussion.
1.11.7.1.5.2. Con: Capital punishment is a penalty meant for someone who committed serious crimes. The fetus' life should not be terminated since he/she did not commit any crime.
1.11.7.1.5.3. Con: Capital punishment is a specific circumstance where people have committed a heinous crime and therefore have a number of their rights restricted or taken away.
1.11.7.1.5.4. Con: Capital punishment is an act of self-defense, imparted only by the State, and is an act of last resort, i.e. the prisoner is still a danger to society. It is not a statement on the value or right to life of the one being executed.
1.11.7.1.5.4.1. Pro: Capital punishment protects the right to life by establishing consequences for murderers.
1.11.7.1.6. Pro: A few countries and US states have now [legalised](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legality_of_euthanasia) euthanasia, which allows people the ability to determine that they wish to end their lives and this action is condoned by the government.
1.11.7.1.6.1. Con: Choosing euthanasia ends only the choosers life. Choosing an abortion ends only the life of the child, not the person doing the choosing.
1.11.7.1.6.1.1. Con: In case of [non-voluntary euthanasia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-voluntary_euthanasia) the decision to end a life is taken by a family member or the doctor.
1.11.7.1.6.1.1.1. Con: Non-voluntary euthanasia takes into account the wishes of the patient. From the link, NVE is “based on what the incapacitated individual would have wanted if they could be asked.” Abortion does not necessarily take this concern into account, and is a separate issue from euthanasia.
1.11.7.1.6.1.1.2. Con: These cases usually occur when a patient is at the end of its life. A fetus/baby would typically be at the beginning of its life.
1.11.7.1.6.1.2. Pro: A baby/fetus cannot legitimately express a desire to be aborted. If it could, it is unlikely that a fetus would reject its own life.
1.11.7.1.6.2. Con: Although the ethics of this is still under much debate, this has no bearing on the abortion argument because abortion is not consensual for the child.
1.11.7.1.6.2.1. Con: That is because unborn children are not capable of giving consent. Even in cases when the explicit consent of the individual concerned is unavailable, such as when the person is in a persistent vegetative state, or in the case of young children, [non-voluntary euthanasia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-voluntary_euthanasia) can be conducted.
1.11.7.1.7. Con: The right to life is enshrined in [Article 3](http://www.claiminghumanrights.org/udhr_article_3.html) of the Universal Declaration of Human Rights.
1.11.7.1.7.1. Con: The Universal Declaration of Human Rights is not a legally binding instrument.
1.11.7.1.7.1.1. Con: The legal ramifications of a document have no bearing on the moral applicability of its implications.
1.11.7.1.7.2. Con: The fact that the right to life is enshrined in the Universal Declaration of Human Rights \(UDHR\) doesn't make the right to life absolute. The UDHR says nothing about the right to life of animals or \(hypothetical\) aliens. The first article makes it clear that such rights [begin at birth.](https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/pdf/10.1016/S0968-8080%2805%2926218-3)
1.11.7.1.8. Con: All other human rights depend on life.
1.11.7.1.9. Pro: The right to life can trade off with other rights. We generally defer to the right to life, but not always when the harms of preserving life are massive.
1.11.7.1.9.1. Con: Unless the consequences of birth is possible fatal harm to the mother, preserving the life of yet-unborn children does not cause massive harm.
1.11.7.2. Con: The established test is the survivability of the foetus autonomously from the parent's body. This is not possible within 1st trimester. Heart beating doesn't warrant survival outside of uterus.
1.11.7.3. Pro: The Roe v. Wade decision ruled abortion legal under ["right to privacy"](https://nwlc.org/resources/roe-v-wade-and-right-abortion/) language in the constitution, and ignored the government's obligation defend it's citizens.
1.11.8. Pro: Abortion is invariably murder. To support abortion as a whole while holding any other belief which treats human life as valuable is directly contradictory.
1.11.8.1. Con: Many countries and their citizens are living their life despite this alleged contradiction indicating that this isn't a direct contradiction but rather a cultural norm.
1.11.8.2. Con: Some beliefs in our current society benefit the life of one human being while taking the life of another.
1.11.8.2.1. Pro: An example of this is taking the life of another in self defense.
1.11.8.3. Con: Looking at abortion as killing is a legitimate point. A pregnant woman however, under carefully considered circumstances and limitations, may have the right to kill. This would make it something else than murder, in the same way that capital punishment isn't murder.
1.11.8.3.1. Con: Following this logic, a woman having given birth to a child, realizing how much work, money and time goes into taking care of it, could have the right to kill this child. Capital punishment cannot be compared to abortion, unless you also accept the premise that you could kill the child after birth.
1.11.8.4. Con: To murder is to take the life of another human being. While zygotes, embreyos and fetuses are stages of human development, they are not yet autonomous human beings. They do not have human faculties and the termination of their development is not homicide.
1.11.9. Pro: Life must be defined to exist right after conception. Otherwise, if a woman drinks to the point of intoxication while the child is in womb she can be charged with nothing because there's no one's life she could possibly be violating.
1.11.10. Pro: If a child in the womb won't be considered a human being, it would lead to a conclusion there should be no prenatal care offered because there's no value in offering prenatal care to a non-human entity.
1.11.10.1. Con: Whether or not the child is considered a human or not is often decided by the mother, based on whether or not the pregnancy is wanted. Just because some women do not want to carry a pregnancy to term is not a pathway to concluding that there should be no prenatal care offered.
1.11.10.2. Con: A fetus does not need to be considered a child in order for it's care to be valued. Women who want children will want those children to be healthy. We know that caring for a fetus will help it develop into a healthy child. Doctors, parents and society as a whole are not likely to forget the value of fetal care simply because we know that a developing fetus is not yet a child.
1.11.10.3. Con: A child in the womb isn't currently considered a human being and it has not lead to a conclusion that there should be no prenatal care.
1.11.11. Con: -> See 1.10.6.1.
1.11.12. Pro: Biological facts indicate that fetuses are human.
1.11.12.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.7.1.1.
1.11.12.2. Pro: Human development is a continuum. From fertilized egg to old age, going through embryo, fetus, baby, toddler, adolescent, adult. At no point there is a discontinuity, therefore the only plausible beginning of human personhood is during fertilization.
1.11.12.2.1. Con: There is no discontinuity in human development between adolescence and adulthood, yet we still recognize them as distinct phases of life. There's no rule saying a phase change requires a discontinuity.
1.11.12.2.1.1. Con: It is recognized that embryo, fetus and child are distinct phases of life, exactly like adolescence and adulthood are. The point is that human life is equaly valuable in all of its phases; old age, adulthood, adolescence, childhood, newborn, fetus, embryo.
1.11.12.2.2. Con: There is a discontinuity. At first the fetus is unable to survive on its own outside the body of the mother. Then at some point the baby is able to survive on its own.
1.11.12.2.2.1. Con: It is not entirely clear at what stage during the pregnancy this occurs, making it difficult to draw a line about when abortion would and would not be acceptable based on this.
1.11.12.2.2.2. Con: 'At some point' is not a true discontinuity anymore than a bird flying at some point or a joey leaving the pouch at some point is. It is just a mark of growth, not a discontinuous stage like a larva or chrysalis would be.
1.11.12.2.2.3. Con: That someone cannot survive on their own if ejected from their current environment is not a logical justification for deliberately terminating that life.
1.11.12.2.3. Pro: The argument that a fetus is not a human requires the assumption that the fetus does not develop further. This is obviously untrue as when left alone, fetuses do develop into infants.
1.11.12.2.4. Con: This continuity begins with sperm and egg, which would make masturbation similar to abortion.
1.11.12.2.4.1. Con: Masturbation generally does not include both eggs and sperms present simultaneously, and by most definitions does not include fertilization. There is a distinct beginning of continuity with fertilization.
1.11.12.2.4.2. Con: Continuity doesn't begin with sperm and egg, since neither of them autonomously directs their own development. On their own, sperm and egg will not develop any further. They are part of an already existing human being, similar to other cells in human body. 
Unlike the embryo which autonomously directs its own development and has a distinct and unique DNA which differentiates it from both parents.
1.11.12.3. Pro: Human embryos autonomously [direct their own development](https://www.nature.com/articles/ncb3347) after conception, even when they are not in their mothers’ wombs.
1.11.12.3.1. Con: An embryo's development cannot occur for extended periods ex vivo. Therefore, the embryo depends on the woman's uterus.
1.11.12.3.2. Con: This is not enough to define embryos as complete humans worthy of every human right.
1.11.12.3.3. Con: "Autonomously" is the wrong word. It implies intent and cognition. My bowels do not autonomously eliminate waste. My heart does not autonomously pump blood. These are biological functions, quite apart from thought or intention. It is the same with gestation.
1.11.12.4. Pro: After 20 days of fetal development, the fetus develops a heartbeat, and because a heartbeat is an indication of life, the fetus should get legal protections as it is human and has the right to life.
1.11.12.4.1. Con: In general, humans are totally comfortable killing animals with a heartbeat for food. It is unclear why this is a meaningful bright line.
1.11.12.4.1.1. Con: We're discussing a human life, not an animal one. Most people would consider them to be very different.
1.11.12.4.2. Con: A heartbeat is a mechanical function like any other. Machines can be designed with systems which are analogous to heartbeats. The heartbeat is "an indication of life" insofar as a person without a heartbeat is generally either dead or likely to die imminently, not such that an object having a "heartbeat" makes it a living being.
1.11.12.4.3. Con: A heartbeat is not enough to define life. The neural system is far more relevant to draw a line between an alive and conscious human and a bunch of worthless cells.
1.11.12.4.3.1. Con: Given scientists and philosophers haven't reached a consensus on the difference between a human and a fetus in terms of the brain, using the brain as the sole criteria is an unnecessary ethical risk.
1.11.12.4.3.2. Con: Brain and heart activity are "life signs" as they are convenient indicators of when an individual is alive, but they are not themselves criteria to be alive. In an adult human, we know that if the brain and heart are both active, all cells are working together for the survival of systems as a whole. [This is an important component of cellular organization, a central benchmark of biological life.](https://www2.estrellamountain.edu/faculty/farabee/biobk/BioBookCELL2.html) While a fetus doesn't have brain and heart activity, it still has cellular organization.
1.11.12.4.4. Pro: If we claim a person to be dead when their heart stops beating, life should begin when their heart starts beating. Claiming the fetus is not independently survivable at that point doesn't matter. Many people are kept alive by the assistance of machinery and technology.
1.11.12.4.5. Con: It takes [6 weeks](https://www.babycenter.com/404_when-can-i-hear-my-babys-heartbeat_10349811.bc) to hear a babies heart beats. Some sources even say the heart is not made [before](https://www.mayoclinic.org/healthy-lifestyle/pregnancy-week-by-week/in-depth/prenatal-care/art-20045302) then. Apparently some doctors say it is normal to not find a heart beat until [8-10 weeks](https://www.babycenter.com/400_when-a-doctor-can-find-the-heartbeat-of-a-baby-which-week-wi_8096703_321.bc).
1.11.12.4.6. Con: A heartbeat is one of a few signs that are required to determine whether or not a human is alive. And it is no longer considered a primary sign in modern medicine. [In medicine the determining factor of whether or not a human is dead is brain function.](http://articles.chicagotribune.com/2014-01-10/opinion/ct-death-jahi-brain-legal-perspec-0110-20140110_1_brain-death-brain-trauma-brain-function)A fetal brain does not meet the criteria of functioning for months into the pregnancy.
1.11.12.4.7. Con: We do not consider it murder to "pull the plug" on someone who is brain dead, even if their heart is beating.
1.11.12.4.7.1. Con: Pulling the plug on a brain dead person occurs when medical professionals agree there is very little to no chance at life. This is not always the case for "voluntarily" aborted fetuses.
1.11.12.5. Con: Due to natural forces, human eggs are frequently fertilized without implanting or coming to term after implanting. Attempting to procreate is considered ethical despite the fact that it frequently leads to the destruction of a fertilized egg. It follows that destroying a fertilized egg for the health and well-being of the mother and would-be child is even more important and therefore also ethical.
1.11.12.5.1. Con: It is illogical to use "natural" causes of death as a justification for "unnatural" causes of death. There are two reasons for it: 1\) the two are not the same thing. 2\) natural causes of death are not "good" things and usually no more desirable than unnatural.
1.11.12.5.2. Con: The natural consequence of sexual intercourse is pregnancy, so the parents are simply employing a natural system to it's natural end. The possibility of a failure in the natural process is thus not the fault of the parents, but due to an accident of nature. Nature, unlike a person, is neither conscious of it's actions nor does it have the power to do otherwise, so it can in no way be held responsible for such death. Consequently, nothing immoral happens in the case of death by natural forces.
1.11.13. Pro: As [IVF has demonstrated,](https://www.legalzoom.com/articles/embryo-ethics-does-discarding-unused-embryos-constitute-murder) the fertilised egg is capable of existing and surviving outside the womb of its mother and is only in need of nutritional support or a gestational carrier. Thus the handling of fertilised eggs is an ethical problem. This is why the use of embryo's for research is an ethical dilemma if they lead to the destruction of the embryo.
1.11.14. Con: -> See 1.11.7.1.
1.11.15. Con: Even if the fetus is a life, so is the mother. This raises a question about whose rights should be prioritised. It is not clear that the right to life of a fetus necessarily trumps the right to bodily autonomy and self-preservation of the mother.
1.11.15.1. Con: The right to life of one innocent individual trumps the rights of another individual in the exercise of their bodily autonomy or desires of self-preservation to deprive the life of the former. Just as her rights to bodily autonomy and self-preservation do not extend so far as to permit her to exercise those rights to take the life an innocent adult, they do not extend to permit her to take the life of her innocent, unborn child.
1.11.15.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.12.2.4.
1.11.15.1.2. Con: Our right to autonomy and self-preservation actually does extend to the killing of others, otherwise known as the principle of self-defence. If another person was inside you, and you do not want it there, then you should have the right to remove it regardless of the consequences to them.
1.11.15.2. Pro: We should value an established life above potential life and recognize established life's right to choose their desired pursuits that naturally generate well-being.
1.11.15.2.1. Con: This just asserts a fetus is a potential life. By all means, a fetus is already a human life unless evidence of the contrary is provided.
1.11.15.2.1.1. Pro: IVF has demonstrated that the fertilised egg is a human being that is capable of living independent of its parents. It is merely in need of nutrition and a gestational carrier.
1.11.15.3. Con: There is absolutely zero precedent in law for anything other than a clear and imminent threat to life or property to be valued above the right of the other party to live. This has been codified as deadly force statutes defining acceptable justification to defend against charges of homicide. In [Texas law](http://www.statutes.legis.state.tx.us/Docs/PE/htm/PE.19.htm), the statute defining homicide had to be modified with a specific exemption because an assault on a pregnant woman which causes the death of the fetus can still be considered murder.
1.11.15.3.1. Con: An unwanted fetus inside a woman should be interpreted as an attacker violating the autonomy of the woman's body. People have the right to defend themselves against someone invading their body by the use of force. Even if by mental impairment an attacker is truly not responsible for his/her actions, the victim still has the right to resist her body being invaded.
1.11.15.4. Pro: It is impossible to give a foetus 'equal rights' to the person carrying it. To claim that a foetus has an inviolable right to life is to say that it should be born regardless of circumstances, even if it seriously harms or kills the pregnant person.
1.11.15.4.1. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.2.3.1.1.
1.11.15.4.2. Con: If the unborn child poses a risk to the life of the mother the aim is to deliver the child, not to kill it. This might pose an additional risk to the child if delivered very early but is not an abortion, e.g. aiming to kill the baby.
1.11.15.5. Con: Traditionally, the U.S Supreme Court recognizes the right to protections of life as of higher priority than the rights to liberty. Religion is the ubiquitous example of this, with human sacrifice being an explicit limit to religious freedom.
1.11.15.6. Con: It is likewise not clear that the maternal right to bodily autonomy and self preservation necessarily trumps the fetus' right to life. This is the crux of the entire debate and may be unresolvable.
1.11.15.7. Pro: Seeing a fetus as 'human life' does not imply its right of absolute protection, since there are many situations where human life depends on being sustained by the personal sacrifice \(and not the legal obligation\) of another human being, not only in the case of organ donations, where nobody is ever obliged to share their body to rescue or protect another human life, but also, for example, when you could prevent a lethal accident or drowning with only moderate risk for your own health.
1.11.15.7.1. Con: The woman is not being required to make any sacrifice beyond what was already implicated by her choice that led to the child being inside her in the first place- what is being argued is her option to reneg on her decision and purposefully end the innocent life she put there.
1.11.15.8. Con: The fetus has more value than the mother \(and the father\) because it is of the next generation. It represents the future.
1.11.15.8.1. Con: Imagine an hypothetical case where the parents are 18 years old and their son/daughter has a genetic mutation. This genetic mutation will most probably kill him/her at a very young age. The parents would be "the future" in this case and under your argument they should be allowed to ask for an abortion.
1.11.15.9. Pro: On an airplane using the breathing bag, you are always supposed to put the breathing mask on yourself first, then you should try to put a mask on the child. If it's a choice between saving your life and helping the kid or saving the kid's life with a chance of passing out and leaving both of you dead, you are supposed to choose your own. But you are able to make the choice for yourself. If the woman didn't mean to be pregnant/changed her mind, she should be free to do that.
1.11.15.9.1. Con: This analogy implies that the mother would save herself then save the child. In the case of the abortion, the mother saves herself then lets the child die. This analogy is deeply flawed.
1.11.15.10. Con: The right to life must be the higher one because without it there wouldn't be any rights; society wouldn't be possible. Hence, to protect the overall rights we need to begin by protecting everyone's life, and a fetus is a human life. That's the reason why, when our life is threatened, we can act in legitimate defences against our aggressor. The rights of an individual, as a whole, are not higher/lower because of whose rights they are but because of which right are we protecting.
1.11.15.11. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.5.
1.11.15.12. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.
1.11.15.13. Pro: -> See 1.2.7.5.1.11.3.3.
1.11.15.14. Con: The mother's right to bodily autonomy is less valid in this instance as she made choices which resulted in the existence of the fetus.
1.11.15.14.1. Con: The point of a right is that it is not conditional upon one's choices. People should never lose the right to their bodily autonomy based on their actions in life.
1.11.15.14.2. Pro: -> See 1.2.2.1.2.9.
1.11.15.14.3. Con: -> See 1.2.2.1.1.
1.11.16. Con: While all the cells of our body are [alive biologically](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life) most of them are not considered a human life and therefore destroying them is not killing. That is why scratching your nose or menstruating \(involving the deaths of millions of cells\) is not considered a crime. Given human life is a subjective concept, to define it at conception \(when it consists of two cells\) is arbitrary.
1.11.16.1. Con: Even when left alone, skin cells and menstrual blood will never become a human baby.
1.11.16.1.1. Con: A fertilized cell if left alone would never become a human being. It needs constant help from the mother and the mother can't be forced to provide this help.
1.11.16.2. Con: Skin cells and blood cells are not living, developing organisms, whereas biology holds that the human organism [begins at conception.](https://www.kialo.com/argument/5637.371) This is not a subjective definition, such as defining what rights or value a life has might be, but is a concrete biological one.
1.11.16.3. Pro: Even if the fetus is considered a biological human being, there is no reasonable social consensus on the morally relevant point in which it is entitled to the protection of its life. As long as such a consensus is not reached, abortions must be a personal decision based on one's belief in this matter.
1.11.16.3.1. Con: If there is no reasonable social consensus, then we should err on the side of caution instead.
1.11.16.3.1.1. Pro: There is certainly no consensus that the fetus is some special class of human that doesn't deserve human rights. A lack of consensus should reflect a lack of action, and people who seek abortions are the first-actors of the situation.
1.11.16.3.2. Pro: The law should not punish an act unless there is no reasonable doubt that a right was infringed upon, therefore, relevant social consensus is essential to define an act as criminal.
1.11.16.3.2.1. Con: There is no reasonable doubt that aborting a human prevents it from exercising any other rights.
1.11.16.3.3. Con: If the fetus is considered a biological human being, the social consensus across the world for generarions informs us that human beings have an irrefutable right to life. Hence a lack of social or moral consensus becomes irrelevant.
1.11.16.4. Con: The whole is more than the sum of its parts. Humans are most certainly more than a collection of nose and reproductive cells \(among others\). Our humanity, therefore, must come from a place other than the definition of our cells.
1.11.16.4.1. Pro: Our humanity comes from a combination of our bodies and our minds or consciousness. Therefore, humanity or human life cannot be present at the time of conception when we have human DNA, but lack both human bodies and human minds.
1.11.16.5. Con: A fetus has a distinct and functional genome denoting it as a different and complete organism.
1.11.16.5.1. Con: Being a distinct organism does not equate to being an autonomous human being.
1.11.16.6. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.4.1.
1.11.16.7. Con: Those two cells are the Genesis of life. They create the entire body and should be thought of as such. They are arguably more important than the billions of cells that make up the entire adult leg for example. One can live without a leg but it’s a serious crime if someone removes another’s leg. That life deserves all the same protections and rights that everyone has, wants and deserves.
1.11.17. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.
1.12. Pro: Access to abortion and control over reproduction is fundamental to achieving gender equality.

Poor sexual and reproductive health accounts for 1/3 of global diseases affecting women between 15 and 44 \([Planned Parenthood, p. 6](http://www.ippf.org/sites/default/files/2020_gender_equality_report_web.pdf)\).

1.12.3.1. Con: This argument presupposes that unborn fetuses constitute human beings

Not like the mother has to do when in her middle/late pregnancy. Abortion could be a choice for women to stand in the same ground as men.
1.12.7. Con: Gender equality is about mindset change, not quantity equivalency.

1.12.8.1. Con: Men and women will have different experiences, but gender equality can still be achieved if those different experiences are taken into account. Equality does not mean both genders should be treated the same, but it does mean both genders should be treated fairly.
1.12.8.2. Con: Men and women are not different in any way that has any bearing on the argument of equality/equal rights. Equality, in this respect, allows a woman to pursue her aspirations in an equivalent manner to which a man is able to pursue his - and in order to achieve that a woman must have reproductive control, which includes abortion.
1.12.8.2.1. Con: A man, just like a woman can have his aspirations affected by pregnancy. Giving a woman the choice to have an abortion without including the man gives her additional rights. It exalts her above the man and above the baby rather than making them more equal.
1.12.8.3. Con: It is still possible to achieve equality with regards to the rights and treatment that men and women receive, and to ensure that they are not unfairly treated as a result of their gender. This would include rights such as bodily autonomy being awarded to all.

In other words no legal or ethical decision on abortion will achieve "gender equality", until abortion is available to both genders - i.e. when males start conceiving \(and consequently sometimes aborting\) fetuses.
