1.13. Con: Abortions are immoral.
1.13.1. Con: Abortion is [a part of nature](http://blogs.discovermagazine.com/notrocketscience/2012/02/23/#.Wj4ISVQ-cWo).
1.13.1.1. Pro: Pregnant male [pipefish](http://blogs.discovermagazine.com/notrocketscience//2010/03/17/pregnant-male-pipefish-abort-babies-from-unattractive-females/#.WkFv3xM-fow) abort babies from unattractive females.
1.13.1.1.1. Con: This is straying very far away from the parent argument. If we want to consider all odd animal behavior regarding pregnancy, there are many \(e.g. spiders\) that literally die for their offspring to have a life.
1.13.1.2. Pro: The [Bruce effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bruce_effect) \(or pregnancy block\) is a tendency in animals \(mainly rodents\) to terminate their pregnancies following exposure to the scent of an unfamiliar male.
1.13.1.2.1. Pro: When a new male takes over a group of [geladas](http://blogs.discovermagazine.com/notrocketscience/2012/02/23/the-bruce-effect-why-some-pregnant-monkeys-abort-when-new-males-arrive/#more-6420) in the wild, the vast majority of females terminate their [pregnancies](https://theethogram.com/2015/03/05/the-bruce-effect/).
1.13.1.2.2. Pro: [Bruce effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bruce_effect) has been observed in deer-mice, meadow voles and collared lemmings.
1.13.1.2.3. Con: If it was natural for humans, we would have developed it ourselves. Instead, we have to rely on surgical procedures and/or drugs.
1.13.1.2.4. Con: This is another claim that doesn't have much to do with humans. Rodents and other animals also eat their babies if they aren't full enough to produce nutritious milk for all of [them.](https://news.nationalgeographic.com/news/2014/03/140328-sloth-bear-zoo-infanticide-chimps-bonobos-animals/)
1.13.1.3. Pro: Research suggests that pregnant female [horses](http://news.bbc.co.uk/earth/hi/earth_news/newsid_9440000/9440222.stm) might be able to make a subconscious decision, based on hormone levels to terminate their pregnancy.
1.13.1.4. Con: Just because abortion exists in nature does not give validity to its morality within human society.
1.13.1.5. Con: The contention that abortion is ethical or good because it occurs in nature is an [appeal to nature](https://rationalwiki.org/wiki/Appeal_to_nature), which is a logical fallacy.
1.13.1.6. Con: Rape and murder are natural but prevented through legal systems in most societies.
1.13.1.7. Con: Infanticide is also part of [nature](http://news.bbc.co.uk/earth/hi/earth_news/newsid_9440000/9440222.stm).
1.13.1.8. Con: So many strange things happen in nature regarding reproduction. Many of them no one would want to happen in human society. For example, female praying mantes often eat the male after having sex to provide more nutrients to the fetus.
1.13.2. Pro: Abortion promotes selfishness and a lack of respect for life as a whole.
1.13.2.1. Con: There is no evidence that abortion, or the legality of abortion, makes anyone more selfish or less respectful of anyone or anything.
1.13.2.1.1. Con: Abortion as well as the legality of abortion makes people less respectful of unborn babies.
1.13.2.2. Con: Selfishness would suggest that individuals engaging in abortion are gaining an immoral cost versus benefit of the procedure. This view discounts psychological and physical pain of abortion in addition to the necessity of abortion due to the surrounding circumstances such as quality of life for the infant, mother and the supporting community both familial and governmental.
1.13.2.3. Con: The same argument could be made for any kind of birth control. By that logic, wearing a condom is denying a potential child, similar to abortion.
1.13.2.3.1. Con: Genetically, a sperm is not identical to a human. A baby in the womb is.
1.13.2.4. Con: By definition, more women than men have had abortions. However, [women commit far fewer crimes](https://science.howstuffworks.com/life/inside-the-mind/emotions/men-more-violent.htm) or acts of violence than men do. Based on this, it does not seem that having an abortion makes a person less respectful of others.
1.13.2.4.1. Con: The previous claim is not true if you consider the unborn baby is another person. While legal, an abortion is an act of violence against the baby. In most cases it is a selfish choice that has no respect for the other life \(baby in the womb\).
1.13.2.4.2. Con: This does not counter the claim to the claim that having an abortion promotes selfishness and disrespect for life: Women who have not had abortions also commit fewer crimes than men. What is noted is a gender disparity. It remains possible that women who have abortions act with less regard for life, *and/or* that men who are the children / boyfriends / husbands of women who have aborted are more likely to commit crimes.
1.13.2.5. Pro: There are many claims here about "her body, her choice" putting "her" above all other considerations in this complex topic. Selfishness is very apparent.
1.13.2.5.1. Con: Everyone, at least in the US, has a right to their own bodily autonomy. So "her body" is in fact, a major consideration in this argument as there would be absolutely no chance for a baby without "her body". When a woman becomes pregnant her body undergoes drastic physical and hormonal changes to provide the environment to carry a child. She literally has to make lifestyle changes so that she can provide another with life. That in itself is the one of the greatest acts of unselfishness.
1.13.2.5.1.1. Con: Carrying, giving birth to, and raising a child in most cases is unselfish. Killing an unborn baby to avoid physical, hormonal and lifestyle changes on the other hand is selfish. This is true especially when taking in to account that pregnancy is avoidable.
1.13.2.5.2. Con: At the end of the day, it is 'her' who has to carry that child to term and raise it up into an adult. There is nothing more vital to the health and happiness of an individual than having a proper upbringing. If a woman who wishes not to have a child is theoretically forced to due to the law, then we can assume that child's life will suffer as a result. It is not selfishness, but about giving that child the best possible chance at life- with a mother who wishes for it to be born
1.13.2.6. Pro: Aborting an unborn baby requires placing the mothers convenience over the value of the baby's life.
1.13.2.6.1. Con: To the contrary, few women have abortions merely for convenience. There are many compelling reasons, economic, medical, emotional among others, why a woman might be compelled to have an abortion. Forcing a woman to bring a fetus to term not only requires her to be an incubator for 9 months, but may also lead to her death, poverty, inability to work, and other potential consequences that many do not consider. If it were just a matter of "convenience," abortions would be much rarer already.
1.13.2.6.1.1. Pro: Similarly, once that child is born the woman has to then raise it into an adult, provided she is not giving it up for adoption- something that is increasingly difficult to do when forming an emotional bond with the baby throughout the nine months of pregnancy. Raising a child requires a significant amount of time and money, something she may not be in the position to give. It is not about 'convenience', but about giving the child the best possible life.
1.13.2.7. Con: Imposing your will on another person, making them abide by your ideas and decisions is equally selfish and arguably more damaging. This whole argument is based on the idea that people have the right to tell women what to do, even if what they do doesn't harm you in any way.
1.13.2.7.1. Con: This is not a fair representation of the pro-life argument, which usually asserts that abortion is the intentional end of an innocent human life. Minimizing the argument to "\[telling\] women what to do" ignores the central argument of human rights and the right to life.
1.13.2.8. Con: Selfishness is not an inherently bad thing.
1.13.2.9. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.6.
1.13.2.10. Con: Criminalizing abortion, and consequently letting women risk their lives in clandestine abortion clinics, promotes a lack of respect for life as a whole.
1.13.3. Pro: In the U.S., 81% of Americans, including 66% of those who self-identify as pro-choice, support substantial [restrictions](https://www.washingtontimes.com/news/2016/jan/19/abortion-poll-finds-81-americans-66-pro-choice-adv/) on abortion, and 55% believe that overall an abortion does more harm to a woman than good. This shows that there are substantial ethical concerns regarding current laws on abortion in the U.S.
1.13.4. Pro: 6 in 10 Americans, including one-third of those who identify as pro-choice, [believe abortion is morally wrong](https://www.washingtontimes.com/news/2016/jan/19/abortion-poll-finds-81-americans-66-pro-choice-adv/).
1.13.4.1. Con: Popular opinion is not a relevant guide to morality; a majority of Americans once opposed interracial marriage, women’s suffrage, etc.
1.13.4.2. Con: This statement is a fallacy - an [appeal to majority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argumentum_ad_populum).
1.13.4.3. Con: 8 in 10 Swedes believe abortion should be permitted "whenever a woman wants one", whereas 85% of Brazilians believe the opposite. Morality isn't absolute. [buzzfeed.com](https://www.buzzfeed.com/lesterfeder/this-is-how-23-countries-around-the-world-feel-about-abortio?utm_term=.uaYdxypmV#.lqrK3PwkD)
1.13.4.4. Con: 4 in 10 Americans, including two-thirds who identify as pro-choice, [believe abortion is morally okay](https://www.washingtontimes.com/news/2016/jan/19/abortion-poll-finds-81-americans-66-pro-choice-adv/).
1.13.4.5. Con: Beliefs of population differ both in time and in space. What Americans in 2018 consider immoral is not an absolute verdict on something. As little as one generation can completely change the scores you use in your argument.
1.13.4.6. Con: 6 in 10 Americans have the right not to abort even if the other 4 have choice of undergoing the abortion. The reverse is not true. Having abortion as an option executes the freedom of all parties, banning abortion caters to a disputabe slight majority.
1.13.5. Pro: From a philosophical perspective, we cannot definitively determine when exactly a human life starts. We cannot therefore assume a fetus is not a human. As human life is protected by law \(in most countries is it protected directly in the constitution\) we have to apply the precautionary principle and assume the fetus is protected from the moment of conception.
1.13.5.1. Con: With this assumption a miscarriage should be punished as an involuntary homicide.
1.13.5.1.1. Con: This is a fallacious comparison. Barring negligent behavior, like alcohol consumption, miscarriages are usually not caused by choices or actions. They are natural deaths, like catching a disease or dying of old age. On the contrary, abortion is an unnatural death cause directly by intentional human intervention.
1.13.5.2. Con: We can define criteria for what constitutes human life and validate those claims with medical science.
1.13.5.3. Pro: We cannot objectively define criteria for what constitutes human life. Such judgement would be very subjective and would base the granting of that status on physical attributes which would be immoral.
1.13.5.4. Con: If we can’t assume a fetus is not human by virtue of our ignorance, then we can’t assume that spermatozoa or unfertilized ova aren’t human either. Positive determinism works equally well in both cases.
1.13.5.5. Pro: If it is an epistemic possibility that an abortion is murder, in the same way is it an epistemic possibility drunk driving can kill, then it follows that such an action ought to be avoided as an unnecessary risk. If an action may kill someone, we act in a prudent manner and avoid the action on the premise of probability of outcome alone.
1.13.5.5.1. Con: Abortion is not murder. An unborn child does not qualify for the same set of rights and legal obligations as adults. Therefore, we do not need need to 'avoid the action' based on the 'probability' that it might be murder.
1.13.5.5.1.1. Con: That an entity doesn't qualify for the same legal rights as another, under some set of laws, doesn't entail that the entity doesn't have the same basic ethical rights as another entity i.e. lacking legal rights doesn't entail lacking fundamental rights \(or value, personhood, etc.\). For example, frequently in history many minorities were not granted the same legal rights as white males but clearly still had equal fundamental rights.
1.13.5.5.1.2. Con: "An unborn child" is not the standard that most would hope to set abortion laws by. Terminating a pregnancy is typically advocated only up to a certain point as there is a great difference between terminating an embryo and terminating a fully formed cognisant baby just prior to birth.
1.13.5.5.2. Con: Epistemic possibility is a low bar for proof of risk. With a reasonable amount of imagination, there is an epistemic possibility that any action \(walking out the front door\) could lead to catastrophic harm to oneself or others, but that is not used as a basis to deny individuals said action.
1.13.5.5.3. Con: Comparing drunk driving and abortion is not a legitimate analogy.
1.13.5.5.3.1. Pro: Claiming it's an epistemic possibility that abortion is murder is just begging the question at hand. It's not at all the same as taking a reckless risk of drunk driving where a person may be killed. In the drunk driving case we all already agree that the life taken is protected by our laws and social norms. That is just the issue being debated here.
1.13.5.5.3.2. Pro: From an epistemic point of view, "Can drunk driving kill?" and "Is abortion murder" are fundamentally different questions. One is provable or refutable by statistics and by studying the effects of alcohol and is a scientific question, while the other is a question about what we consider murder rather than whether or not it kills the foetus, and therefore belongs to a discussion of ethics and is not a scientific question, because it cannot be proven or refuted by science.
1.13.5.6. Con: If we cannot assume a fetus is not a human, we cannot assume it's human either. Choosing one is just a matter of opinion, and if it's a matter of opinion, that shouldn't be illegal, so everyone can make the choice individually.
1.13.6. Pro: [Abortion is used to cover up rape of minors and other vulnerable women.](http://www.lifenews.com/2016/01/19/at-13-i-rejected-abortion-after-my-stepfather-raped-me-thank-god-i-did-because-now-i-cant-have-kids/) A pregnancy is an indicator of sexual activity taking place and may be the only red flag of a bigger problem. This does not seem to be an isolated incident as [Planned Parenthood has been accused of failing to report suspected sexual crimes.](https://www.lifesitenews.com/news/whistleblowers-expose-how-planned-parenthood-ignored-child-rape-in-latest-l)
1.13.6.1. Con: Reporting the sexual violence isn't the point of this discussion. The choice to terminate the pregnancy has nothing to do with whether or not sexual violence will be reported.
1.13.6.2. Con: This is not an issue of abortions, but of women's issues, gender issues, security, etc. If there is a safe enough environment, women will denounce their rapist.
1.13.6.3. Con: Abusers of women and girls should not have the right to choose an abortion - women should have the right to choose abortion.
1.13.7. Con: Even if abortion is immoral, this does not necessarily mean it should be illegal. Abortion should be legal but not publically funded.
1.13.7.1. Pro: If you are anti abortion you should not be required to pay for abortions. If you are pro abortions then you should fund and sponsor abortions.
1.13.7.2. Pro: Charity services can be implemented for poor people who cannot afford abortions.
1.13.7.3. Con: Access to health services should not be determined by a person's wealth.
1.13.7.4. Pro: This might be an acceptable compromise, provided that other objectionable things which people feel strongly about are also subject to exemptions from public funding.
1.13.7.5. Con: If abortion is immoral then we should legally forbid it.
1.13.7.6. Con: The mere possibility of abortion being both legal and morally reprehensible says nothing as to whether we ought to forbid it.
1.13.7.7. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.6.1.
1.13.7.8. Pro: Many women have abortions despite moral opposition to the procedure.
1.13.7.8.1. Pro: Research shows that women’s reasons for choosing abortion are overwhelmingly tied to their life situation as opposed to abstract, moral or religious principles. \([pg.3](http://www.abortionresearch.us/images/Vol20No1.pdf)\)
1.13.7.8.2. Pro: A 1981 [study](http://www.lifeissues.net/writers/air/air_vol20no1_20071.html) found that 25% of women facing an abortion decision considered the fetus to be human and regarded abortion as the taking of life whereas a 1995 study reported that 25% of women seeking an abortion agreed with the statement "abortion is against my beliefs."
1.13.7.9. Pro: The law exists to prevent harm, not enforce morality. As such the question of abortion's morality is irrelevant to the question of its legality.
1.13.7.9.1. Con: Ethics discusses not what it is, but what ought to be. Law should punish what ought not to be, and should not punish what ought to be. Slavery is not moral, or in other words, one ought not to enslave people, therefore, it should not be legal. Abortion's morality is relevant to the question of its legality if one ought to allow or ought not to allow abortion.
1.13.7.9.2. Con: A fetus is considered a separate entity, so by aborting it, you are causing harm towards it.
1.13.7.9.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.1.1.
1.13.7.9.2.2. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.7.1.1.5.1.
1.13.7.9.3. Con: The original claim makes no reference to the law. The question is one of rights in general. If the original claim were specifically about legal rights, then it would be a fundamentally different discussion.
1.13.7.9.4. Con: Morality exists as a construct to provide an internal framework within which human behavior does not cause harm. First degree murder, robbery, and kidnapping all fall under the descriptors of harmful, immoral, and illegal simultaneously for a reason.
1.13.7.9.5. Con: The law does prohibit immoral action. But it prohibits only a certain kind of immoral action. Illegal acts are acts that are immoral and also violate the rights of others.
1.13.7.9.5.1. Con: Not everything which is illegal is immoral by default. For example, women didn't have the right to vote, and while that was illegal, it clearly wasn't immoral. As such, something can't be immoral just because it's illegal.
1.13.7.9.5.1.1. Pro: Slavery is immoral as well, yet is still practiced in many parts of the world and many countries once considered it legal.
1.13.7.9.6. Con: This argument is predicated on the idea that an abortion does no harm to the child being aborted.
1.13.8. Con: Life is net suffering. Thus, every birth creates more suffering, especially when the child is unwanted. Abortion, therefore, is a means of restricting increases in the total amount of suffering in the world, which is not immoral.
1.13.9. Con: Fetuses don't have viable brains and aren't even capable of responding to averse stimuli until [about 23 weeks](https://www.nytimes.com/2005/06/19/books/chapters/the-ethical-brain.html). They're not sentient, not self-aware, not capable of thought, emotion, preferences, or [even aware of pain beyond reflex](https://philpapers.org/archive/LAGTEO-5.pdf) before the [third trimester](https://www.livescience.com/54774-fetal-pain-anesthesia.html). It has [less neurological activity](https://www.nytimes.com/2005/06/19/books/chapters/the-ethical-brain.html) than someone who has been declared brain dead. Is it life? Yes. Scientifically speaking, it is life, but it is not yet sentient life requiring moral consideration despite the potential to develop into such.
1.13.9.1. Con: This claim asserts that only sentience or the potential of sentience requires moral consideration. This is an unjustified assertion and therefore should not be used in order to permanently affect the lives of other humans, for example, ending them.
1.13.10. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.15.2.4.6.1.1.
1.13.11. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.1.1.
1.13.12. Pro: While ethics can change with the whims of a society, fundamental moral standards do not. If the murder of an innocent is a fundamental moral wrong, then [it would remain morally wrong](http://www.askphilosophers.org/question/5627), even if a society decided it was acceptable in some instances.
1.13.12.1. Con: Giving women the right to have abortions does not make abortions compulsory, it simply gives women the opportunity to make their own decisions. People should be able to make their own decisions about what they consider ethical and moral.
1.13.12.2. Pro: Choosing abortion implies the termination of an innocent life. The growing child inside her womb did not choose to be conceived, and the developing child hasn't broken any laws; it is innocent. Our rights do not allow us to harm the innocent lives of others, because our rights also protect us from being harmed by others.
1.13.12.2.1. Con: Choosing an abortion is the termination of a pregnancy and the prevention of a zygote/embreyo, or fetus from developing into a human being.
1.13.12.3. Pro: Murder of the innocent remains immoral whether a cannibalistic society allows it or not.
1.13.12.4. Pro: Slavery remains immoral regardless of a society that allows it.
1.13.12.5. Pro: The U.S. Declaration of Independence in particular takes note of the existence of underlying moral standards, regardless of societal ethics, with its declaration that humans have 'inalienable rights' such as life, liberty, and the pursuit of happiness which government cannot tamper with.
1.13.12.5.1. Pro: Humans retain these fundamental rights regardless of society. When the U.S. Supreme Court declared blacks to be non-persons according to the ethics of that time period, it had no moral force to make such a thing a reality.
1.13.12.5.2. Con: -> See 1.11.7.1.
1.13.12.5.3. Con: On this basis, banning abortion could constitute government interference with women's inalienable rights to liberty and the pursuit of happiness.
1.13.12.5.3.1. Pro: By not legalising or banning abortion what results is giving the "state" the power of decision over a person's body. The state should not have inherence on a person's body.
1.13.12.5.4. Con: Granting that all people have rights, the debate is precisely whether or not a fetus is a person who possesses those rights. If it's not, no rights are violated.
1.13.12.6. Con: There are different morals and there is no humanly universal moral which is violated by abortion.
1.13.12.6.1. Con: A universal moral, seen across cultures, is to not end a human life without reason. If one defines a fetus as human life, just "wanting to" kill the fetus is just as morally reprehensible as just "wanting to" kill one's neighbor.
1.13.12.7. Con: Morality is a constructed, relative and subjective concept. Reality dictates what must be done, not fabricated representations of it. The only question that matters is "what counts as life?" Once this is answered there will be no ambiguity.
1.13.12.7.1. Con: If morality is constructed, relative and subjective, the question of "what counts as life?" is arbitrary, as it places subjective value on human life. Any criteria to determine life would also be subjective, so no resolution can ever be reached, as both sides of the argument can put forth their subjective claims to support their position. The claim that there is no objective morality is a weak starting point for any discussion that aims to find one "correct" solution.
1.13.12.7.2. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.7.1.1.
1.13.13. Con: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.
1.13.14. Con: The definition of abortion encompasses both spontaneous abortion, otherwise known as miscarriage, and conscious abortion. Yet, we do not place a moral value on miscarriage nor personhood on a miscarried embryo or foetus.
1.13.14.1. Pro: Miscarriage is a deliberate action taken by the body when it assesses that a pregnancy will not result in a healthy, successful baby. It may be induced by genetic defects or even the mother's malnutrition. With our more advanced ability to assess a positive outcome, either with genetic testing or our own conscious assessment of our life position, abortion is merely a modern, volitional extension of the miscarriage process taken with better information.
1.13.14.1.1. Con: Advances in medicine have sought to decrease the possibility of natural miscarriage, not increase it. Women facing natural miscarriage may or may not have wanted the child. The volitional aspect of abortion is what makes it very distinct from natural miscarriage, not an extension of it.
1.13.14.2. Con: It is nonsensical to posit a "moral value" on miscarriage: by [definition](https://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/moral), morals pertain to decisions made by people resulting in behavior, and no such circumstance exists when a miscarriage occurs spontaneously.
1.13.14.3. Con: Abortions or miscarriages which are a result of nature, rather than an action that was carried out to end the pregnancy, are considered differently with regards to morality as one is unavoidable and the other is an active choice to end a life.
1.13.14.3.1. Pro: Only human persons are morally culpable for person-induced abortions. The loss of human life by natural causes \(e.g. miscarriage\) is not caused by persons. Therefore, natural causes are not morally culpable for abortions.
1.13.14.3.2. Pro: No court will put disease or age on trial for a death by natural causes, but a court will try a person accused of premeditated murder.
1.13.14.4. Con: Death encompasses both natural death, such as from age or disease, capital punishment, death in war, accidental manslaughter, and premeditated murder. In all cases there is value granted to the life involved, regardless of how it ends.
1.13.14.4.1. Con: In the case of a miscarriage, much less value is assigned to the life than in the case of the death of an infant, child, or adult. Family and friends usually mourn more publicly, more intensely, for longer periods, and at greater personal expense. Often women miscarry without even letting people outside their innermost circle know that it has happened. Usually their grief, though real, is muted and temporary, and is not shared as deeply by others.
1.13.14.5. Con: A lot of people do assign personhood to their miscarried babies. They mourn them as they would a baby who had been born and then died.
1.13.15. Pro: Abortion is the unjustified taking of human life in most cases and the unjustified taking of human life should always be illegal. Therefore, unborn humans should be protected from abortion in most cases.
1.13.15.1. Con: One of the core questions of the abortion debate is the definition of human life. This claim assumes unborn fetuses to be autonomous human lives deserving of the same rights and protections as already-born people, which is a point of contention, not a fact to be taken for granted.
1.13.15.1.1. Con: [life](https://www.google.com/search?rlz=1C1CHWL_enUS751US751&ei=Nvm6Wq34EqavjwTJxr-ABA&q=define%3A+life&oq=define%3A+life&gs_l=psy-ab.3..0i7i30k1j0l3j0i7i30k1l4j0j0i7i30k1.4212.6717.0.9137.8.8.0.0.0.0.186.951.2j6.8.0....0...1c.1.64.psy-ab..0.7.887...0i7i10i30k1.0.fRYLGD9LC64) noun 1.the condition that distinguishes animals and plants from inorganic matter, including the capacity for growth, reproduction, functional activity, and continual change preceding death.
2.the existence of an individual human being or animal.
A baby from the moment of conception has its own human dna distinct from the mother's and is beginning to grow. At week 5 blood cells develop and the baby can have a different blood type than the [mother's](https://biology.stackexchange.com/questions/29654/how-does-a-fetus-retain-a-blood-group-different-from-its-mother). It is clearly an individual human [being](http://abort73.com/abortion/mothers_body/).
1.13.15.2. Pro: An unborn child cannot choose its parents, so abortion would be punishing an unborn life for doing nothing wrong.
1.13.15.3. Pro: The right to choose to kill someone should not be delegated based on a demographic \(whether someone is an expectant mother or not\).
1.13.15.3.1. Pro: The core reason to oppose abortion on demand for one sex is the equal application of the law. Three people are involved in every abortion. Only women are given any recognized rights. The "rights" she is "given," negate the rights of two other people. Women have been bestowed with a "constitutional right" to kill their children. There are no other examples of a constitutional right granted to one sex, nor other examples of rights granted to kill, except in self defense.
1.13.15.4. Pro: The right to kill someone else should not be delegated based upon one's relation to the victim.
1.13.15.5. Pro: It is possible the fetus being aborted was destined to be someone of great importance, like the next Albert Einstein. Imagine how the world could be different today if Einstein's mother had an abortion, we might not have won WWII.
1.13.15.5.1. Con: Then the reverse of this supposition is an equally valid argument. It is possible that the fetus being aborted was destined to be someone horrible, like the next Hitler. Imagine how the world could have been saved if Hitler had not been born. Thus, abortion would have saved the world from WWII at all.
1.13.15.5.2. Con: It's worth noting that a future wanted child may be forgone because an unwanted pregnancy is kept. Who's to say that the later child would not be the Einstein rather than the first. In fact all things being equal children who's parents intended their conception are likely more prepared to be parents than those who did not. As such these children are less likely to have adverse childhood experiences which could negatively effect the rest of the child's life.
1.13.15.6. Pro: Every human being has a right to life, because it is a human being and human beings have value in and of themselves. Other species, such as [acorns](https://www.thenewatlantis.com/publications/acorns-and-embryos), have value based on other characteristic, like beauty or age, something they can gain or lose. Human beings cannot lose their value and have it as long as they live and a new member of the species is created after conception.
1.13.15.6.1. Con: If the mother has a fast-spreading uterine cancer, the surgery to remove the cancer may result in the loss of the child’s life. In an ectopic pregnancy the child is developing outside the uterus. He has no hope of survival, and may have to be removed to save his mother’s life. These are tragic situations, but even if one life must be lost, the life that can be saved should be. [epm.org](https://www.epm.org/resources/2010/Feb/20/what-about-woman-whose-life-threatened-pregnancy-o/)
1.13.15.7. Pro: Laws and courts have established that the decision to kill another human being should not be based on someone's personal belief that the other person is an inconvenience to them or the assumption that they might be to others, and that disregard for an individual's life and the ending that life should not be tolerated regardless of a person's age even if they are the parent.
1.13.15.8. Pro: The CDC and the National Association of Medical Examiners recognize [four categories of death](https://www.cdc.gov/misc/hb_me.pdf): 1\) Natural - death by medical illness or old age. 2\) suicide - intentionally ending one's own life. 3\) accidental - unintentionally ending a human life. 4\) homicide - intentionally ending another human life. Based on this, abortion \(an intentional act done to end the life of a fetus\) can only be considered homicide.
1.13.15.9. Con: Whether abortion is justified, is exactly the question we are trying to answer. You cannot just assume that the taking of a life in the case of abortion is unjustified in most cases, without explaining in which cases abortion would be justified or unjustified.
1.13.15.10. Con: "Human" and "Life" are arbitrary definitions, with no clear basis in biology. There is no clear line between "Human" and "not Human" nor between "Life" and "not Life". All such definitions are arbitrary and flawed, excluding some things we wish to include or vice versa.
1.13.16. Pro: Legal access to abortion means many doctors are put in the position of having to conduct an operation or aid an operation they may find deeply distressing and immoral.
1.13.16.1. Con: Women having the right to choose abortion does not mean that all doctors are required to perform abortions.
1.13.16.1.1. Con: In a society in which abortion is legal, doctors who are unwilling to perform abortions risk being stigmatised. This is unfair.
1.13.16.1.1.1. Con: Doctors specialize by nature of their profession. There is no stigma for choosing one specialty over another. Only [14%](https://www.npr.org/sections/health-shots/2011/08/22/139859979/proportion-of-ob-gyns-offering-abortions-may-be-lower-than-thought) of OB-GYNs perform abortions.
1.13.16.1.2. Pro: OBGYN physicians can choose which procedures they do or do not take part in. Some OBGYN's will perform abortions, but only under certain circumstances.
1.13.16.1.3. Pro: In a number of countries, medical professionals are allowed to [conscientiously object](https://www.bpas.org/get-involved/advocacy/briefings/conscientious-objection/) to performing abortions and the cases are passed on to other professionals.
1.13.16.1.3.1. Con: -> See discussion #2851: Conscientious objection to abortion should be banned
1.13.16.1.4. Pro: Doctors do not have to work in abortion clinics. If they feel the act is immoral, they can just not perform it.
1.13.16.1.4.1. Con: -> See 1.13.16.1.1.
1.13.16.2. Pro: Individuals become doctors, because they want to [save lives,](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hippocratic_Oath) they do not become doctors because they want to end life.
1.13.16.2.1. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.7.1.1.7.2.
1.13.16.2.2. Con: This is a very presumptuous assumption. Certainly it could be argued at least a subset of doctors are motivated by access to work opportunities and good pay rather than a desire to save life, and equally so for many other plausible alternative motivations.
1.13.16.2.3. Con: Do not confuse "Life" with "Personhood". We kill millions of living things daily. Abortion concerns the definition of a legal person and the definition of murder.
1.13.16.2.4. Con: Doctors take oaths to "do no harm". In some cases extending life does constitute a harm. This is a serious consideration that should be made before becoming a doctor.
1.13.16.3. Con: A doctor who feels strongly about this has the option of pursuing a different specialty.
1.13.16.4. Con: When we choose a vocation we should consider all responsibilities of that vocation and whether or not we are willing to do the job. If we are not willing to do the job we should select a different vocation.
1.13.16.4.1. Pro: If they aren't emotionally capable of performing important procedures, they shouldn't be doctors.
1.13.16.5. Pro: Abortions violate the [Hippocratic oath](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hippocratic_Oath).
1.13.16.5.1. Con: The Hippocratic Oath has no [legal](https://gizmodo.com/doctors-aren-t-actually-bound-by-the-hippocratic-oath-1465044222) status and is only a symbolic ritual that contains outdated content.
1.13.16.5.1.1. Pro: Technically, administering any medication with side effects violates the Hippocratic Oath.
1.13.16.5.2. Con: The [Hippocratic Oath](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hippocratic_Oath) originates from around the 3rd-5th centuries BC. Whatever it says should not be used as an argument in the 21st century.
1.13.16.5.3. Con: The [Hippocratic oath](http://www.arcc-cdac.ca/postionpapers/71-Abortion-Hippocratic-Oath.PDF) only forbids a specific abortion method - a "pessary" \(a vaginal insert of some sort\). Some texts attributed to Hippocrates describe abortions as a fairly common, uncontroversial procedure.
1.13.16.5.4. Con: -> See 1.13.16.2.4.
1.13.17. Pro: Late stage abortions are particularly ethically problematic, because the baby would likely have survived if it was born immediately.
1.13.17.1. Con: This point concerns a very specific \(and truly unfortunate\) scenario and cannot be used to judge the validity of the original claim - that abortions are universally "both immoral and unethical".
1.13.17.1.1. Con: The above claim does not undermine the idea that all abortions are immoral and unethical. Rather, it points to a specific instance where they are particularly ethically problematic.
1.13.17.1.2. Pro: According to the Guttmacher Institute, [88 percent](https://www.livestrong.com/article/181997-facts-about-adoption-instead-of-abortion/) of abortions occur within the first 12 weeks of pregnancy, with only 1.5 percent occurring after 21 weeks' gestation. This is mostly because late term abortions risk the life of the mother and are often done because of serious issues.
1.13.17.1.2.1. Pro: The possibility of a woman's death associated with abortion [increases](https://www.livestrong.com/article/181997-facts-about-adoption-instead-of-abortion/) with the length of gestation. The risk of the mother's death for an abortion at between 16 and 20 weeks' gestation is one in 29,000, while the risk increases to one in 11,000 for abortions after 21 weeks.
1.13.17.2. Pro: There is very little difference between a late stage fetus and a newborn baby in terms of development, such that late term abortions are questionable as we would not allow people to end the life of a newborn.
1.13.17.3. Pro: [4d ultrasound technology](https://www.theguardian.com/uk/2006/oct/03/health.healthandwellbeing) can show detailed images of  babies in the womb. From 12 weeks onward babies can be seen smiling, crying, walking, sucking their thumb, stretching and yawing. These images, which show babies acting like human beings, demonstrate why late stage abortion is wrong.
1.13.17.4. Con: Almost all post-viability abortions are on women whose fetuses have died or are severely impaired such that they will not survive outside the womb. [Forbes](https://www.forbes.com/sites/tarahaelle/2016/10/20/no-late-term-abortions-dont-rip-babies-out-of-wombs-but-they-are-needed/#5d67bd0b5cf8) [Jen Gunter, MD](https://drjengunter.wordpress.com/2016/10/27/how-many-late-term-abortions-are-really-performed-in-the-united-states/)
1.13.17.5. Con: There are [many reasons](http://www.spiked-online.com/newsite/article/10015#.WhrwQEpl86w) why women seek late term abortions that are legitimate and should not result in the woman's choice being removed.
1.13.17.5.1. Pro: Irregular period cycles can make pregnancies hard to detect.
1.13.17.5.2. Pro: A lack of access to abortion clinics within a region can mean that women have arrange to travel to a clinic, which can take time and resources to arrange.
1.13.17.5.2.1. Con: It is unlikely, especially in the US, that such travel limitations would last long enough to necessitate a late term abortion.
1.13.17.5.3. Pro: Pregnancies caused by rape or incest are traumatic, and this trauma can delay women seeking out an abortion.
1.13.17.5.4. Pro: Many young women delay getting an abortion because they feel ashamed and worry about how their parents might respond.
1.13.17.5.5. Pro: Drastic changes to a woman's situation could make her question her ability to raise a child, such as the death of her partner, or a large financial loss.
1.13.17.5.6. Con: None of the reasons that are made for having a late term abortion justify killing a living child that could survive outside the womb.
1.13.17.5.7. Pro: Such cases are often life or death for the mother. Doctors and the mother should be free to make those decisions based on sound medical practice. The State should not be involved in those decisions.
1.13.17.5.7.1. Pro: -> See 1.13.17.1.2.1.
1.13.17.5.7.2. Con: While abortion may be necessary when the pregnancy threatens the life of the mother, it should be restricted to cases of life and death, not issues of convenience.
1.13.18. Con: Abortions have the same ethical ramifications as abstinence and contraception - all three result in the lack of a life that could have existed. If abortion is unethical, so is avoiding impregnating or being impregnated at any time.
1.13.18.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.4.2.3.
1.13.18.2. Con: This is a fallacy of equivocation. In the event of an abortion, the life of the child has already begun, so there exists something to be destroyed.
1.13.18.3. Con: This only works if a child in a womb is not already living. Otherwise, there is a difference in moral categories here: Abortion is a direct act against a life already living. Abstinence is not.
1.13.18.3.1. Pro: Nor is preventing pregnancy through pre-conception methods.
1.13.18.4. Con: The three things are very different, so do not have equivalent ethical ramifications.
Abstinence: Cannot possibly terminate a biological human organism under any circumstances.
Contraception: Some forms can rarely lead to a biological human organism dying due to blocked implantation, while others forms \(like condoms\) can never harm a human life.
Abortion: Tries to, and usually succeeds, in directly terminating a  biological human organism.
1.13.18.4.1. Con: What is a "Human organism"? sperm? morula? fetus? there is a distinction between them too. A morula is not a human, a sperm is not a human, if you take out the morula from the uterus you cannot give it legal rights because it doesn't looks or act as a person. A fetus, from 3 months and on, is considered a person because only in that stage it reach a person's similarities.
1.13.18.5. Con: Neither abortion advocates nor pro-life advocates claim that there is an ethical mandate to bring all theoretically possible life into the world, so this interpretation of the ethical ramifications is an example of an [appeal to extremes](https://www.logicallyfallacious.com/tools/lp/Bo/LogicalFallacies/30/Appeal-to-Extremes) fallacy.
1.13.18.6. Pro: It is generally agreed that no one can force a woman to conceive a child. So no one can forbid a woman from using contraception. Therefore, no woman should be made to carry a fetus to term. There is no difference between preventing conception by killing sperm or preventing implantation and terminating pregnancy after contraception has failed.
1.13.18.6.1. Con: The key difference here is that separately, sperm and eggs are just reproductive cells, but once an egg has been fertilised, [prenatal development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_fertilization) is initiated and therefore a life has begun.
1.13.18.6.1.1. Con: The beginning of development doesn't mean that something has developed. The fact that a cell has begun to duplicate and become more complex doesn't mean that it is already a new person.
1.13.18.6.1.2. Pro: -> See 1.11.
1.13.18.7. Con: It is generally agreed upon that there is an action/inaction distinction. This is why not becoming an aid worker or not donating 90% of one's income to charity is not immoral. Given this, abstinence and contraception are merely inaction resulting in a lack of life, whereas abortion is a specific action which leads the destruction of life.
1.13.18.7.1. Con: According to this reasoning, eating seeds should be considered deforestation because a particular action \(eating\) is "destroying" the life of a tree.
1.13.18.7.2. Con: The action/inaction distinction is a matter of ease - it is hard to sacrifice your hard-earned money even when you know it's the right thing to do, but easy not to go out and rob a charity. An abortion and a healthy pregnancy both require effort and active intent.
1.13.18.7.3. Con: Contraception is not inaction, as it requires very specific actions to be used.
1.13.18.7.3.1. Con: Contraception prevents the action of initiating a life. Fertilization is the important action here.
1.13.19. Con: Ethics and morality are subjective and can vary from society to society or even from person to person. Therefore abortion is not necessarily always immoral or unethical.
1.13.19.1. Pro: One's moral system is the direct result of their religious upbringing in most cases.
1.13.19.2. Con: Different people can hold different opinions of ethics, however that does not mean they are all equally correct and does not prove the subjectivity of ethical rules.
1.13.19.3. Con: If this is the case, we cannot say that murder, rape, or theft are wrong, but simply considered unethical in our society.
1.13.19.3.1. Con: This is not an argument. The statement is correct but does not invalidate the fact that ethics and morals are subjective.
1.13.19.4. Pro: The very definition of ethics is very subjective: some may say it is linked to religion, others to what the majority believes or even to common sense, so ethics could even be used as an argument in support of abortion.
1.13.19.5. Pro: Morals are a set of rules that individuals live by. It is exceedingly arrogant to suggest that people with different morals are somehow incorrect or wrong. It is not up to other individuals to police the morals of any other person. That is why women should always have the right to choose what happens to their own body and to live by the morals they choose for themselves.
1.13.19.5.1. Con: If a society polices for murder, theft, or other crimes considered immoral, then that society finds it ethically acceptable to determine what is a crime, create laws to prohibit that crime, and then police to enforce the law. These laws may change over time as the society reevaluates and changes, but the fundamental ethics of the society hold that it may create laws based in moral principles and then enforce them.
1.13.19.5.2. Con: Saying that “women should always have the right to choose” is a moral judgment, that according to your argument, can not be judged as “correct” or “right.” All laws are codifications of moral judgments, and there are some acts that are universally considered immoral, such as the taking of an innocent human life.
1.13.19.6. Pro: Morality is not an universal concept. In countries such as Egypt, the simple act of a woman drinking alcohol on the street is considered immoral \(which does not happen to men\).
1.13.19.7. Con: Ethics can vary from culture to culture, some allowing cannibalism and slavery, for example. However, the underlying moral standards of right and wrong do not vary, even if a culture chooses not to base its ethics in those moral principles.
1.13.19.7.1. Con: There is no indication to believe that there are moral standards of right and wrong.
1.13.19.8. Pro: As with all acts, the morality of abortion varies with the person's context.
1.13.19.9. Pro: Abortions are only considered immoral and unethical on a religious basis. Forcing all women to adhere to a specific religion is religious discrimination.
1.13.19.9.1. Con: Many atheists and agnostics hold that abortions are unethical and do so on [secular grounds.](http://www.secularprolife.org/)
1.13.19.9.2. Con: [Many religions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_and_abortion), not just one 'specific religion,' take a stance against abortion.
1.13.19.9.3. Con: Religious individuals, just as irreligious individuals, voting for a law for or against an action, would not force anyone to adhere to a specific religion if the law was passed unless the law itself forced compliance with a particular religion.
1.13.19.9.3.1. Con: But if that law comes from a place of religious obligation, then isn't it by definition a "religious law"? By passing a law based on your religious beliefs you are effectively forcing them upon others by law.
1.13.19.9.3.2. Pro: In countries like the U.S., congress has no power to establish a religious denomination as the state religion or enforce a particular type of worship, etc., so a law forcing one to keep a religion cannot be made.
1.13.20. Con: -> See 1.11.7.1.3.
1.13.21. Con: In an instance where the pregnant woman's life is at risk and the fetus would not survive on it's own; utilitarianism argues that an abortion would be more ethical than letting both the woman and the fetus die since the overall good of saving the woman's life outweighs any unethical implications of abortions.
1.13.21.1. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.5.1.4.
1.13.21.2. Pro: A woman should have the right to take steps to defend her life in the event that carrying a child to term would end in the death of both the fetus and the mother.
1.13.21.3. Con: Most cases where the mother's life is in direct danger are treatable via medicine. While this often has the side effect of the unborn child dying, directly killing the child is usually unnecessary.
1.13.21.4. Con: The utilitarian argument is not the only basis in determining the ethical implications of abortion.
1.13.21.4.1. Con: This discussion contains many non-utilitarian arguments for and against abortion. Utilitarian evaluations are relevant to many people, particularly utilitarians, whether they are the sole basis for every person's opinion or not.
1.14. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.4.1.7.
